<span id="page-16-1"></span>**Fig. 6.** Game sequence for our selectively secure ABE for NFA<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> where  $i \in [\ell]$ . In the table, we only show the  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components of secret key. In the **Remark** column, "SD" and "DDH" indicate  $\mathrm{SD}_{\mathbf{A}_1 \to \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{a}_2}^{G_1}$  and  $\mathrm{DDH}_{1,Q}^{G_2}$  assumption, respectively; switching lemma and transition lemma were given in GWW, cf. Lemma 16 and Lemma 13.

### <span id="page-17-0"></span>4.5 Switching secret keys I

In this section, we will show that  $G_{2.i.0} \approx_c G_{2.i.1}$  for all  $i \in [\ell]$  and  $G_{2.\ell.4} \approx_c G_3$ . The proofs for them are similar. We begin with the following lemma stating that  $G_{2.1.0} \approx_c G_{2.1.1}$  and sketch the proofs for the remaining statements.

<span id="page-17-2"></span>**Lemma 7**  $(G_{2.1.0} \approx_c G_{2.1.1})$ . For all  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists  $\mathcal{B}$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{A})$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.1.0} \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.1.1} \rangle = 1] \leq O(|\Sigma|) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathrm{DDH}_{1,Q}^{G_2}}(\lambda).$$

Overview. Roughly, we will prove that

$$\left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^0, \overline{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^0}\right) = \left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^0, \overline{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{0,1}}\right)$$

By Lemma 4, we focus on  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components and prove:

$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{0}[2] = \begin{pmatrix} [\left(\mathbf{d} + s_{0}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^{*}}\right) \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{start} \mathbf{R} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \left\{ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{1} \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d} \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \left\{ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{0} \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d} \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \end{pmatrix} \approx_{c} \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{start} \mathbf{R} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{0}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^{*}} + \mathbf{z}_{1} \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d} \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \left\{ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{0} \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d} \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d} + \mathbf{w}_{end} \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}$$

given

$$\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2] = \big([s_0\mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}]_1, [s_0]_1, [s_0\mathbf{z}_1]_1\big).$$

Clearly, change of variables  $\mathbf{d} \mapsto \mathbf{d} - s_0^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}$  is at the core of the above statement, which ensures that: for all  $s_0$  and  $\Delta$ , we have

<span id="page-17-1"></span>
$$\frac{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{0}[2]}{\left\{\left(\mathbf{d}+\boldsymbol{s}_{0}^{-1}\boldsymbol{\Delta}\cdot\mathbf{f}_{0,x^{*}}\right)\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}+\mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}},-\mathbf{d}+\mathbf{z}_{1}\mathbf{R},\mathbf{R}\right\}} \approx_{s} \underbrace{\left\{\mathbf{d}\,\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}+\mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}},-\mathbf{d}+\boldsymbol{s}_{0}^{-1}\boldsymbol{\Delta}\cdot\mathbf{f}_{0,x^{*}}+\mathbf{z}_{1}\mathbf{R},\mathbf{R}\right\}}_{\mathbf{c}^{\mathsf{T}}} \quad \text{given } \underbrace{\mathbf{ct}_{x^{*}}^{0}[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}},\mathbf{z}_{1}} \quad (23)$$

However this does not hold if  $\mathbf{d}$  is also given out on the both sides which corresponds to  $\mathbf{d}$ 's appeared at other positions, as is our case. We address this issue by hiding other occurrences of  $\mathbf{d}$ 's via  $\mathrm{DDH}_{1,Q}^{G_2}$  assumption before the change of variable and getting them back via  $\mathrm{DDH}_{1,Q}^{G_2}$  assumption again after that.

Auxiliary hybrids. Formally, we need two more auxiliary hybrids:

–  $G_{2.1.0.a}$  is the same as  $G_{2.1.0}$  except that, for key query  $\Gamma$ , we return

$$\begin{pmatrix} [(\mathbf{d} + s_0^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}) \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}} \mathbf{R} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_2, [\mathbf{R} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_2 \\ \{ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_1 \mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{0} \cdot \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \{ [\mathbf{0} + \mathbf{z}_0 \mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{0} \cdot \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{0} + \mathbf{w}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \end{pmatrix}.$$

–  $G_{2.1.1.a}$  is the same as  $G_{2.1.1}$  except that, for key query  $\Gamma$ , we return

$$\begin{bmatrix} [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{u}^{\top} + \mathbf{w}_{start}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2} \\ \left\{ [-\mathbf{d} + s_{0}^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^{*}} + \mathbf{z}_{1}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{0} \cdot \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \left\{ [\mathbf{0} + \mathbf{z}_{0}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{0} \cdot \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{0} + \mathbf{w}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{bmatrix} .$$

Then we prove that:

<span id="page-17-3"></span>
$$G_{2.1.0} \stackrel{\text{DDH}}{\approx}_{c} G_{2.1.0.a} \stackrel{\text{(23)}}{\approx}_{s} G_{2.1.1.a} \stackrel{\text{DDH}}{\approx}_{c} G_{2.1.1}$$
 (24)

which is summarized in Fig 7.

| <b>Game</b> $? \cdot \mathbf{u}^{\top} + \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}} \mathbf{R} \mathbf{u}^{\top}$ | $?+\mathbf{z}_1\mathbf{R}$                               | $\mathbf{?} \cdot \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{R}$ | $\mathbf{?} + \mathbf{z}_0 \mathbf{R}$ | $? \cdot \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{R}$ | $\alpha \mathbf{f}$ -?+ $\mathbf{w}_{\text{end}}\mathbf{I}$ | R Remark                                                                   |
|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------|---------------------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| 2.1.0 $\mathbf{d} + s_0^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}$                                    | $-\mathbf{d}$                                            | d                                                                         | $-\mathbf{d}$                          | d                                                                | d                                                           | $sk^0_\Gamma[2]$                                                           |
| 2.1.0. $a \ \mathbf{d} + s_0^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}$                               | -d                                                       | 0                                                                         | 0                                      | 0                                                                | 0                                                           | DDH                                                                        |
| 2.1.1. <i>a</i> <b>d</b>                                                                         | $-\mathbf{d} + s_0^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}$ | 0                                                                         | 0                                      | 0                                                                | 0                                                           | $\mathbf{d} \mapsto \mathbf{d} - s_0^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}$ |
| 2.1.1 <b>d</b>                                                                                   | $-\mathbf{d} + s_0^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}$ | d                                                                         | $-\mathbf{d}$                          | d                                                                | d                                                           | DDH, $sk_\Gamma^{0,1}[2]$                                                  |

<span id="page-18-0"></span>**Fig. 7.** Game sequence for  $G_{2.1.0} \approx_c G_{2.1.1}$ . In the table, we only show changes of secret key and focus on its  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components; all secret key elements in the fourth and sixth column are quantified over  $\sigma \in \Sigma$ . In the **Remark** column, "DDH" indicates DDH<sup> $G_2$ </sup><sub>1,Q</sub> assumption.

<span id="page-18-1"></span>Lemmas. We describe and prove the following lemmas which imply Lemma 7 by (24).

**Lemma 8** ( $G_{2.1.0} \approx_c G_{2.1.0.a}$ ). For all  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists  $\mathcal{B}$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{A})$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.1.0} \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.1.0.a} \rangle = 1] \leq O(|\Sigma|) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathrm{DDH}_{1,Q}^{G_2}}(\lambda).$$

*Proof.* By Lemma 4, it suffices to prove the lemma over  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components which roughly means:

$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{0}[2] = \begin{pmatrix} [(\mathbf{d} + s_{0}^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^{*}})\mathbf{u}^{\top} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2} \\ \{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{1}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d} \cdot \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{0}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d} \cdot \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \end{pmatrix} \approx_{c} \begin{pmatrix} [(\mathbf{d} + s_{0}^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^{*}})\mathbf{u}^{\top} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2} \\ \{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{1}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{0} \cdot \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \{[\mathbf{0} + \mathbf{z}_{0}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{0} \cdot \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\alpha\mathbf{f} - \mathbf{0} + \mathbf{w}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}$$

in the presence of

$$\operatorname{ct}_{x^*}^0[2] = ([s_0 \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}]_1, [s_0]_1, [s_0 \mathbf{z}_1]_1).$$

One can sample basis  $\mathbf{A}_1$ ,  $\mathbf{a}_2$ ,  $\mathbf{A}_3$ ,  $\mathbf{A}_1^{\parallel}$ ,  $\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel}$ ,  $\mathbf{A}_3^{\parallel}$  and trivially simulate mpk,  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^0$  and secret key using terms given out above. Furthermore, this follows from  $\mathsf{DDH}_{1,O}^{G_2}$  assumption w.r.t  $\mathbf{z}_0$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}}$  with  $\sigma \in \Sigma$  which implies:

$$\left([\mathbf{z}_0\mathbf{R}]_2,\left\{[\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0}\mathbf{R}]_2\right\}_{\sigma\in\Sigma},\left\{[\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1}\mathbf{R}]_2\right\}_{\sigma\in\Sigma},[\mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{R}]_2,[\mathbf{R}]_2\right)\approx_c U\left((G_2^{1\times Q})^{2|\Sigma|+2}\times G_2^{k\times Q}\right)$$

where  $\mathbf{z}_0, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0}, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1}, \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  for all  $\sigma \in \Sigma$  and  $\mathbf{R} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times Q}$ . Here we use the fact that  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]$  does not leak  $\mathbf{z}_0, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1}, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0}, \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}}$  with  $\sigma \in \Sigma$ . This completes the proof.

**Lemma 9.** For all A, we have

$$Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2,1,0,a} \rangle = 1] = Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2,1,1,a} \rangle = 1].$$

*Proof.* This immediately follows from (23) implied by the change of variables:  $\mathbf{d} \mapsto \mathbf{d} - s_0^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}$ .

**Lemma 10.** For all A, there exists B with  $Time(B) \approx Time(A)$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.1.1.a} \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.1.1} \rangle = 1] \leq O(|\Sigma|) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathrm{DDH}_{1,Q}^{G_2}}(\lambda).$$

*Proof.* The proof is analogous to that for Lemma 8.

Via the same proof idea, we can prove the following two lemmas stating that  $G_{2.i.0} \approx_c G_{2.i.1}$  for all  $i \in [2, \ell]$  and  $G_{2.\ell.4} \approx_c G_3$ , respectively. We only sketch the proof for each lemma.

<span id="page-18-2"></span>**Lemma 11**  $(G_{2.i.0} \approx_c G_{2.i.1})$ . For all  $i \in [2, \ell]$  and all A, there exists B with  $Time(B) \approx Time(A)$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.i.0} \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.i.1} \rangle = 1] \leq O(|\Sigma|) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathrm{DDH}_{1,Q}^{G_2}}(\lambda).$$

Proof (sketch). We will prove that

$$\left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1},\boxed{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i-1}}\right) = \left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1}, \boxed{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i-1,i}}\right)$$

Recall that  $\tau = i \mod 2$ , the proof is analogous to that for Lemma 7: roughly, we want to prove the following statement over  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components:

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i-1}[2] \; = \; & \begin{cases} [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \big\{ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\left(\mathbf{d} + s_{i-1}^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^{*}}\right) \mathbf{M}_{x_{i-1}^{*}} + \mathbf{w}_{x_{i-1}^{*},1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \big\} \\ & \quad \quad \left\{ [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2} \big\}_{\sigma \neq x_{i-1}^{*}} \\ \big\{ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \big\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ & \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \quad$$

given

$$\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1}[2] = \left( [s_{i-1} \mathbf{w}_{x_{i-1}^*, 1-\tau}]_1, [s_{i-1}]_1, [s_{i-1} \mathbf{z}_{\tau}]_1 \right).$$

This relies on:

$$\frac{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i-1}[2]}{\left\{ (\mathbf{d} + s_{i-1}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}) \mathbf{M}_{x_{i-1}^*} + \mathbf{w}_{x_{i-1}^*,1-\tau} \mathbf{R}, \mathbf{-d} + \mathbf{z}_{\tau} \mathbf{R}, \mathbf{R} \right\}} \approx_{s} \underbrace{\left\{ \mathbf{d} \mathbf{M}_{x_{i-1}^*} + \mathbf{w}_{x_{i-1}^*,1-\tau} \mathbf{R}, -\mathbf{d} + s_{i-1}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} + \mathbf{z}_{\tau} \mathbf{R}, \mathbf{R} \right\}}_{\mathsf{sk}}$$

in the presence of  $\mathbf{w}_{x_{i-1}^*,1-\tau}$ ,  $\mathbf{z}_{\tau}$  leaked via  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1}[2]$ .

-  $\mathsf{DDH}_{1,Q}^{G_2}$  assumption w.r.t  $\mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}$ ,  $\mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}$ ,  $\{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\tau}\}_{\sigma \neq x_{i-1}^*}$ ,  $\{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,\tau}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{end}}$ ; this implies that

$$\left( [\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, \left\{ [\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2} \right\}_{\sigma \neq x_{i-1}^{*}}, \left\{ [\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2} \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, [\mathbf{w}_{\text{end}}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \right) \approx_{c} U \left( (G_{2}^{1 \times Q})^{2|\Sigma| + 2} \times G_{2}^{k \times Q} \right)$$

and will be used to hide all **d**'s irrelevant with the change of variables.

<span id="page-19-0"></span>**Lemma 12**  $(G_{2,\ell,4} \approx_c G_3)$ . For all A, there exists B with  $Time(B) \approx Time(A)$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.\ell.4} \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{3} \rangle = 1] \leq O(|\Sigma|) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathrm{DDH}_{1,Q}^{G_2}}(\lambda).$$

Proof (sketch). We will prove that

$$\left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^\ell, \overline{\mathsf{sk}_\Gamma^\ell}\right) = \left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^\ell, \overline{\mathsf{sk}_\Gamma^{\ell,*}}\right)$$

Recall that  $\ell = \ell \mod 2$ , the proof is analogous to that for Lemma 7: roughly, we want to prove the following statement over  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components:

$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{\ell}[2] \; = \; \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{\bar{\ell}}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [(\mathbf{d} + s_{\ell}^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\ell,x^{*}})\mathbf{M}_{x_{\ell}^{*}} + \mathbf{w}_{x_{\ell}^{*},\bar{\ell}}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \} \\ \{[\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,\bar{\ell}}\mathbf{R}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \neq x_{\ell}^{*}} \\ \{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{1-\bar{\ell}}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\bar{\ell}}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} \boxed{-\mathbf{d}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}$$

<span id="page-20-0"></span>
$$\approx_{c} \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}} \mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{\bar{\ell}} \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{x_{\ell}^{*}} + \mathbf{w}_{x_{\ell}^{*}, \bar{\ell}} \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2}\} \\ \{[\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma, \bar{\ell}} \mathbf{R}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \neq x_{\ell}^{*}} \\ \{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{1-\bar{\ell}} \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma, 1-\bar{\ell}} \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d} + s_{\ell}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\ell, x^{*}} + \mathbf{w}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}$$

given

$$\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{\ell}[2] = \big( [s_{\ell} \mathbf{w}_{x_{\ell}^*, \bar{\ell}}]_1, [s_{\ell}]_1, [s_{\ell} \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}}]_1, [s_{\ell} \alpha]_T \cdot m_{\beta} \big).$$

This relies on:

- change of variables  $\mathbf{d} \mapsto \mathbf{d} - s_{\ell}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\ell,x^*}$ ; this ensures that, for all  $s_{\ell}$  and  $\Delta$ , we have

$$\underbrace{\{(\mathbf{d} + s_{\ell}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\ell,x^*}) \mathbf{M}_{x_{\ell}^*} + \mathbf{w}_{x_{\ell}^*,\ell} \mathbf{R}, -\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{w}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{R}, \mathbf{R}\}}_{\mathsf{sk}_{\ell}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\ell,x^*}} \approx_{s} \underbrace{\{\mathbf{d} \mathbf{M}_{x_{\ell}^*} + \mathbf{w}_{x_{\ell}^*,\ell} \mathbf{R}, -\mathbf{d} + s_{\ell}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\ell,x^*} + \mathbf{w}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{R}, \mathbf{R}\}}_{\mathsf{sk}_{\ell}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\ell,x^*}}$$

in the presence of  $\mathbf{w}_{x_e^*,\bar{\ell}}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}}$  leaked via  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{\ell}[2]$ .

 $- \ \mathrm{DDH}_{1,Q}^{G_2} \ \mathrm{assumption} \ \mathbf{\hat{w.r.t}} \ \mathbf{w_{start}}, \mathbf{z_0}, \mathbf{z_1}, \{\mathbf{w_{\sigma,\bar{\ell}}}\}_{\sigma \neq x_{\ell}^*}, \{\mathbf{w_{\sigma,1-\bar{\ell}}}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}; \ \mathrm{this} \ \mathrm{implies} \ \mathrm{that}$ 

$$\left( [\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}} \mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{z}_0 \mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{z}_1 \mathbf{R}]_2, \left\{ [\mathbf{w}_{\sigma, \bar{\ell}} \mathbf{R}]_2 \right\}_{\sigma \neq x_{\ell}^*}, \left\{ [\mathbf{w}_{\sigma, 1 - \bar{\ell}} \mathbf{R}]_2 \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \right) \approx_c U \left( (G_2^{1 \times Q})^{2|\Sigma| + 2} \times G_2^{k \times Q} \right)$$

and will be used to hide all d's irrelevant with the change of variables.

## 4.6 Switching ciphertexts

In this section, we show that  $G_{2.i.1} \approx_c G_{2.i.2}$  and  $G_{2.i.3} \approx_c G_{2.i.4}$  for all  $i \in [\ell]$  using the switching lemma from GWW [11].

<span id="page-20-2"></span>Lemma 13 ((s, W)-switching lemma [11]). We have

$$\begin{aligned} &\mathsf{aux,} \ [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1]_1, & [\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \bar{\Delta} + \mathbf{W}\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2, \ [\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2 \\ \approx_{\mathit{c}} \ \mathsf{aux,} \ [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1 + \boxed{s}\overline{\mathbf{a}_2}]_1, \ [\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \bar{\Delta} + \mathbf{W}\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2, \ [\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2 \end{aligned}$$

 $\label{eq:whereaux} \begin{aligned} \textit{where} \, \mathsf{aux} &= ([\mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{a}_2, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}, \mathbf{a}_2 \mathbf{W}]_1, [\mathbf{W}\mathbf{B}, \mathbf{B}]_2) \,\, and \, \mathbf{W} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(2k+1)\times k}, \, \mathbf{B} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \, \mathbf{s}, \mathbf{r} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1\times k}, \, \bar{\Delta}, \, s \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p. \,\, \textit{Concretely, the advantage function} \,\, \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{SWITCH}}(\lambda) \,\, is \,\, bounded \,\, by \,\, O(1) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}_0}^{k\text{-LIN}}(\lambda) \,\, with \,\, \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}_0) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}). \end{aligned}$ 

We begin with the following lemma stating that  $G_{2.i.1} \approx_c G_{2.i.2}$  for all  $i \in [\ell]$  and sketch the proof of  $G_{2.i.3} \approx_c G_{2.i.4}$  for all  $i \in [\ell]$ , which is analogous.

<span id="page-20-1"></span>**Lemma 14**  $(G_{2.i.1} \approx_c G_{2.i.2})$ . For all  $i \in [\ell]$  and all A, there exists B with  $Time(B) \approx Time(A)$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.i.1} \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.i.2} \rangle = 1] \leq \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{SWITCH}}_{\mathcal{B}}(\lambda).$$

Overview. We will prove that

$$\left(\mathsf{mpk}, \left[\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1}\right], \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i-1,i}\right) \approx_c \left(\mathsf{mpk}, \left[\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1,i}\right], \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i-1,i}\right).$$

This roughly means that we will show that

$$\underbrace{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1}}_{[\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1]_1} \approx_c \underbrace{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1,i}}_{[\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1 + s_i \mathbf{a}_2]_1} \quad \text{given} \quad \underbrace{[-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot s_{i-1}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} + \mathbf{Z}_{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2}_{\mathsf{span}}.$$

The occurrence of  $\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel}$  hinders a direct application of  $\mathrm{SD}_{\mathbf{A}_1 \mapsto \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{a}_2}^{G_1}$  assumption. We will use  $(\mathbf{s}_i, \mathbf{Z}_{\tau})$ -switching lemma in the proof, which roughly states that  $[\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1]_1 \approx_c [\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1 + s_i \mathbf{a}_2]_1$  given  $[\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \bar{\Delta} + \mathbf{Z}_{\tau} \mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2$  and  $[\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2$ ; the auxiliary terms given out in the lemma will be used to simulate the terms involving  $\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel}$ .

*Proof.* Recall that  $\tau = i \mod 2$ . We prove the lemma using  $(\mathbf{s}_i, \mathbf{Z}_{\tau})$ -switching lemma. On input

aux, 
$$[\mathbf{c}_i]_1$$
,  $[\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \bar{\Delta} + \mathbf{Z}_{\tau} \mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2$ ,  $[\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2$ 

where  $\mathsf{aux} = ([\mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{a}_2, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{Z}_\tau, \mathbf{a}_2 \mathbf{Z}_\tau]_1, [\mathbf{Z}_\tau \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{B}]_2)$  and  $\mathbf{Z}_\tau \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(2k+1) \times k}, \mathbf{B} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times k}, \mathbf{r} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and

$$\mathbf{c}_i = \boxed{\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1}$$
 or  $\mathbf{c}_i = \boxed{\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1 + s_i \mathbf{a}_2}$ ,  $\mathbf{s}_i \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$ ,  $s_i \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ 

the reduction works as follows:

(Simulating mpk) We sample  $\mathbf{k} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times (2k+1)}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\text{start}}$ ,  $\mathbf{Z}_{1-\tau}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(2k+1) \times k}$  for all  $\sigma \in \Sigma$ , and then we can trivially simulate mpk from  $[\mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{Z}_{\tau}]_1$ .

(Simulating challenge ciphertext) On input  $(m_0, m_1)$ , we want to create a challenge ciphertext in the following form, which is either  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1}$  or  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1,i}$  depending on  $\mathbf{c}_i$ :

$$\begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{c}_{0}]_{1}, [\mathbf{c}_{0}\mathbf{W}_{\text{start}}]_{1} \\ \{ [\mathbf{c}_{j}]_{1}, [\mathbf{c}_{j-1}\mathbf{Z}_{1}^{-}]_{1}^{-} \cdot [\mathbf{c}_{j}\mathbf{W}_{x_{j}^{*}, 1^{-}}]_{1} \}_{j=i \text{ mod } 2} \\ \{ [\mathbf{c}_{j}]_{1}, [\mathbf{c}_{j-1}\mathbf{Z}_{1-\tau}]_{1} \cdot [\mathbf{c}_{j}\mathbf{W}_{x_{j}^{*}, 1-\tau}]_{1} \}_{j\neq i \text{ mod } 2} \end{pmatrix} \text{ where } \begin{cases} \mathbf{c}_{i} \in \{ [\mathbf{s}_{i}\mathbf{A}_{1}], \mathbf{s}_{i}\mathbf{A}_{1} + s_{i}\mathbf{a}_{2} \} \\ \mathbf{c}_{i-1} = \mathbf{s}_{i-1}\mathbf{A}_{1} + s_{i-1}\mathbf{a}_{2} \\ \mathbf{c}_{j} = \mathbf{s}_{j}\mathbf{A}_{1} & \forall j \notin \{i-1, i\} \end{cases}$$

Observe that.

- $\begin{array}{l} \text{ when } \mathbf{c}_i = \boxed{\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1}, \text{ the distribution is identical to } \boxed{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1}}; \\ \text{ when } \mathbf{c}_i = \boxed{\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1 + s_i \mathbf{a}_2}, \text{ the distribution is identical to } \mathtt{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1,i} \end{array}$

We proceed to create the challenge ciphertext as follows:

- We sample  $s_{i-1} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ ,  $\mathbf{s}_j \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  for all  $j \neq i$  and simulate  $\{[\mathbf{c}_j]_1\}_{j \neq i}$  using  $[\mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{a}_2]_1$ ; note that  $[\mathbf{c}_i]_1$  is given out in the lemma as the challenge term.
- We rewrite terms in the dashed box as:

$$[\mathbf{c}_{j}\mathbf{Z}_{\tau}]_{1} = \begin{cases} [\mathbf{s}_{j}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{Z}_{\tau}]_{1} & \text{if } j \neq i-1 \text{ and } j \neq i \text{ mod } 2\\ [\mathbf{s}_{i-1}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{Z}_{\tau}]_{1} \cdot [s_{i-1}\mathbf{a}_{2}\mathbf{Z}_{\tau}]_{1} & \text{if } j = i-1 \text{ (and } j \neq i \text{ mod } 2) \end{cases}$$

which can be simulated using  $\{\mathbf{s}_j\}_{j\neq i \bmod 2}$ ,  $s_{i-1}$  and  $[\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{Z}_\tau,\mathbf{a}_2\mathbf{Z}_\tau]_1$ ; here we use the fact that we do not have any terms involving  $[\mathbf{c}_i \mathbf{Z}_{\tau}]_1$  in the challenge ciphertext.

- We simulate all remaining terms using  $\{[\mathbf{c}_i]_1\}_{i\in[0,\ell]}$  and  $\mathbf{k}, \mathbf{W}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{Z}_{1-\tau}, \{\mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1}\}_{\sigma\in\Sigma}, \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}\}_{\sigma\in\Sigma}$ 

(Simulating secret key) On input  $\Gamma$ , we want to return a secret key for  $\Gamma$  in the form

$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i-1,i} = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{D}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{W}_{\text{start}} \mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \{ [-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{a}_{2}^{\mathsf{T}} \cdot s_{i-1}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^{*}} + \mathbf{Z}_{\tau} \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{D}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,\tau} \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \{ [-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{Z}_{1-\tau} \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{D}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1-\tau} \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{D} + \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}$$

We sample  $\mathbf{D} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(2k+1) \times Q}$  and  $\widetilde{\mathbf{R}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times Q}$  and implicitly set

$$\Delta = s_{i-1}\bar{\Delta}$$
 and  $\mathbf{R} = \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} + \mathbf{B} \cdot \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}$ .

We proceed to simulate  $sk_{\Gamma}^{i-1,i}$  as follows:

- We simulate  $[\mathbf{R}]_2$  from  $[\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_2$ ,  $[\mathbf{B}]_2$  and  $\mathbf{f}_{i-1.x^*}$ ,  $\widetilde{\mathbf{R}}$ .

- We can rewrite the term in the dashed box as:

<span id="page-22-2"></span>
$$[-\mathbf{D} + (\mathbf{a}_{2}^{\parallel} \cdot \bar{\Delta} + \mathbf{Z}_{\tau} \mathbf{r}^{\top}) \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^{*}} + \mathbf{Z}_{\tau} \mathbf{B} \cdot \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}]_{2}$$

 $\text{which can be simulated using } [\boldsymbol{a}_2^{\!\!\parallel} \cdot \boldsymbol{\bar{\Delta}} + \boldsymbol{Z}_{\!\scriptscriptstyle T} \boldsymbol{r}^{\!\scriptscriptstyle T}]_2, [\boldsymbol{Z}_{\!\scriptscriptstyle T} \boldsymbol{B}]_2 \text{ and } \boldsymbol{D}, \boldsymbol{f}_{i-1,\boldsymbol{x}^*}, \widetilde{\boldsymbol{R}}.$ 

– We simulate all remaining terms using  $[\mathbf{R}]_2$  and  $\mathbf{k}, \mathbf{D}, \mathbf{W}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{Z}_{1-\tau}, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,\tau}, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1-\tau}, \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}$ .

Observe that, when  $\mathbf{c}_i = \boxed{\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1}$ , the challenge ciphertext is  $\boxed{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1}}$  and the simulation is identical to  $\mathsf{G}_{2.i.1}$ ; when  $\mathbf{c}_i = \boxed{\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1 + s_i \mathbf{a}_2}$ , the challenge ciphertext is  $\boxed{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1,i}}$  and the simulation is identical to  $\mathsf{G}_{2.i.2}$ . This completes the proof.  $\Box$ 

Via the same idea, we can prove the following lemmas stating that  $G_{2.i.3} \approx_c G_{2.i.4}$  for all  $i \in [\ell]$ . We only sketch the proof by highlighting the difference.

<span id="page-22-3"></span>**Lemma 15**  $(G_{2.i.3} \approx_c G_{2.i.4})$ . For all  $i \in [\ell]$  and all A, there exists B with  $Time(B) \approx Time(A)$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.i.3} \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.i.4} \rangle = 1] \leq \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{SWITCH}}_{\mathcal{B}}(\lambda).$$

Proof (sketch). We will prove that

$$\left(\mathsf{mpk}, \boxed{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1,i}}, \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^i\right) \approx_{\mathit{c}} \left(\mathsf{mpk}, \boxed{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^i}, \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^i\right)$$

which roughly means that we need to prove that

$$\underbrace{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1,i}}_{[\mathbf{s}_{i-1}\mathbf{A}_1+s_{i-1}\mathbf{a}_2]_1} \approx_c \underbrace{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^i}_{\mathbf{s}_{i-1}\mathbf{A}_1]_1} \quad \text{given} \quad \underbrace{[\mathbf{DM}_{x^*_i}+\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot s_i^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}+\mathbf{W}_{x^*_i,\tau}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2}_{}.$$

The proof is analogous to that of Lemma 14 except that we use  $(\mathbf{s}_{i-1}, \mathbf{W}_{x_i^*, \tau})$ -switching lemma instead of  $(\mathbf{s}_i, \mathbf{Z}_{\tau})$ -switching lemma so that we can simulate the challenge ciphertext from the challenge term in the lemma and simulate secret key using the auxiliary terms given out in the lemma.

### <span id="page-22-1"></span>4.7 Switching secret keys II

This section proves  $G_{2.i.2} \approx_c G_{2.i.3}$  for all  $i \in [\ell]$  using the transition lemma from GWW [11].

**Lemma 16** ((**z**,**w**)-transition lemma [11]). For all  $s_{i-1}$ ,  $s_i \neq 0$  and  $\bar{\Delta} \in \mathbb{Z}_p$ , we have

$$\begin{aligned} &\mathsf{aux},\ s_{i-1}\mathbf{z} + s_{i}\mathbf{w},\ [\boxed{s_{i-1}^{-1}\bar{\Delta}} + \mathbf{z}\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2},\ [\mathbf{w}\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2},\ [\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}\\ &\approx_{c}\ \mathsf{aux},\ s_{i-1}\mathbf{z} + s_{i}\mathbf{w},\ [\mathbf{z}\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2},\ [\boxed{s_{i}^{-1}\bar{\Delta}} + \mathbf{w}\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2},\ [\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}\end{aligned}$$

where  $\mathsf{aux} = ([\mathbf{zB}, \mathbf{wB}, \mathbf{B}]_2)$  and  $\mathbf{z}, \mathbf{w} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}, \ \mathbf{B} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times k}, \ \mathbf{r} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}.$  Concretely, the advantage function  $\mathsf{Adv}_{\mathfrak{B}}^{\mathsf{TRANS}}(\lambda)$  is bounded by  $O(1) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathfrak{B}_0}^{k-\mathsf{LIN}}(\lambda)$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathfrak{B}_0) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathfrak{B}).$ 

<span id="page-22-0"></span>**Lemma 17** ( $G_{2.i.2} \approx_c G_{2.i.3}$ ). For all  $i \in [\ell]$  and all A, there exists B with  $Time(B) \approx Time(A)$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.i.2} \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.i.3} \rangle = 1] \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{TRANS}}(\lambda).$$

**Overview.** This roughly means

$$\left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1,i}, \boxed{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i-1,i}}\right) \approx_c \left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1,i}, \boxed{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i}}\right);$$

more concretely, we want to prove the following statement over  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components:

$$\begin{split} &[-\mathbf{d} + \boxed{s_{i-1}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} + \mathbf{z}_{\tau} \mathbf{R}}]_2, \qquad &[\mathbf{d} \mathbf{M}_{x_i^*} + \boxed{\mathbf{w}_{x_i^*,\tau} \mathbf{R}}]_2, \ [\mathbf{R}]_2 \qquad //\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i-1,i}[2] \\ \approx_{c} \qquad &[-\mathbf{d} + \boxed{\mathbf{z}_{\tau} \mathbf{R}}]_2, \ [\mathbf{d} \mathbf{M}_{x_i^*} + \boxed{s_i^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{M}_{x_i^*} + \mathbf{w}_{x_i^*,\tau} \mathbf{R}}]_2, \ [\mathbf{R}]_2 \qquad //\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i}[2] \end{split}$$

given  $\mathbf{d}$ ,  $\Delta$ ,  $s_{i-1}$ ,  $s_i$ ,  $s_{i-1}\mathbf{z}_{\tau} + s_i\mathbf{w}_{x_i^*,\tau}$  revealed by  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1,i}$ . This can be handled by the  $(\mathbf{z}_{\tau},\mathbf{w}_{x_i^*,\tau})$ -transition lemma and the fact that  $\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} = \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}\mathbf{M}_{x_i^*}$  mod p (see Lemma 5).

*Proof.* Recall that  $\tau = i \mod 2$ . By Lemma 4, it suffices to prove the lemma over  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components which roughly means:

$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i-1,i}[2] \; = \; \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \boxed{s_{i-1}^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^{*}} + \mathbf{z}_{\tau}\mathbf{R}} \end{bmatrix}_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{x_{i}^{*}} + \boxed{\mathbf{w}_{x_{i}^{*},\tau}\mathbf{R}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \\ \{ [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2} \}_{\sigma \neq x_{i}^{*}} \\ \{ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d} + \mathbf{w}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}$$

$$\approx_{c} \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{x_{i}^{*}} + \boxed{s_{i}^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^{*}}\mathbf{M}_{x_{i}^{*}} + \mathbf{w}_{x_{i}^{*},\tau}\mathbf{R}} ]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \\ \{ [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2} \}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [(\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d} + \mathbf{w}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}$$

in the presence of

$$\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1,i}[2] = \begin{cases} [s_0 \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}]_1, [s_0]_1, [s_0 \mathbf{z}_1 + s_1 \mathbf{w}_{x_1^*,1}]_1, [s_1]_1, [s_1 \mathbf{z}_0]_1 & \text{if } i = 1 \\ [s_{i-1} \mathbf{w}_{x_{i-1}^*,1-\tau}]_1, [s_{i-1}]_1, [s_{i-1} \mathbf{z}_{\tau} + s_i \mathbf{w}_{x_i^*,\tau}]_1, [s_i]_1, [s_i \mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}]_1 & \text{if } i \in [2, \ell-1]_1, \\ [s_{\ell-1} \mathbf{w}_{x_{\ell-1}^*,1-\bar{\ell}}]_1, [s_{\ell-1}]_1, [s_{\ell-1} \mathbf{z}_{\bar{\ell}} + s_{\ell} \mathbf{w}_{x_{\ell}^*,\bar{\ell}}]_1, [s_{\ell}]_1, [s_{\ell} \mathbf{w}_{\text{end}}]_1, [s_{\ell} \alpha]_T \cdot m_{\beta} & \text{if } i = \ell \end{cases}$$

One can sample basis  $\mathbf{A}_1$ ,  $\mathbf{a}_2$ ,  $\mathbf{A}_3$ ,  $\mathbf{A}_1^{\parallel}$ ,  $\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel}$ ,  $\mathbf{A}_3^{\parallel}$  and trivially simulate mpk,  $\operatorname{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1,i}$  and secret key using terms given out above. Furthermore, we prove this using  $(\mathbf{z}_{\tau}, \mathbf{w}_{x^*, \tau})$ -transition lemma. On input

$$\mathsf{aux}, [\bar{\Delta}_0 + \mathbf{z}_\tau \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}]_2, [\bar{\Delta}_1 + \mathbf{w}_{x_*^*,\tau} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}]_2, [\mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}]_2$$

where  $(\bar{\Delta}_0, \bar{\Delta}_1) \in \left\{ \boxed{(s_{i-1}^{-1}\bar{\Delta}, 0)}, (0, s_i^{-1}\bar{\Delta}) \right\}$  and  $\mathsf{aux} = (\bar{\Delta}, s_{i-1}, s_i, s_{i-1}\mathbf{z}_\tau + s_i\mathbf{w}_{x_i^*, \tau}, [\mathbf{z}_\tau \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{x_i^*, \tau} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{B}]_2)$ 

$$\mathsf{aux} = (\bar{\Delta}, s_{i-1}, s_i, s_{i-1}\mathbf{z}_\tau + s_i\mathbf{w}_{x_i^*, \tau}, [\mathbf{z}_\tau \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{x_i^*, \tau} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{B}]_2)$$

with  $\mathbf{z}_{\tau}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{x_{i}^{*},\tau}$   $\leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{1\times k}$ ,  $\mathbf{B} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k\times k}$ ,  $\mathbf{r} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{1\times k}$  and  $\bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{p}$ , we sample  $\alpha \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{p}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}$ ,  $\mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\tau}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\text{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{1\times k}$  for all  $\sigma \in \Sigma$  and  $\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,\tau} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{1\times k}$  for all  $\sigma \neq x_{i}^{*}$  and proceed as follows:

(Simulating challenge ciphertext) On input  $(m_0, m_1)$ , we trivially simulate  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1, i}[2]$  using  $s_{i-1}, s_i, s_{i-1}\mathbf{z}_\tau + s_i\mathbf{w}_{x_i^*, \tau}$  in aux and  $\alpha$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\tau}$ ,  $\mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\text{end}}$  as well.

$$\begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{u}^{\top} + \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \Delta_{0} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^{*}} + \mathbf{z}_{\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{x_{i}^{*}} + \Delta_{1} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^{*}} + \mathbf{w}_{x_{i}^{*},\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}$$

$$[\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d} + \mathbf{w}_{\text{end}}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2}$$
 where  $(\Delta_{0}, \Delta_{1}) \in \{ (s_{i-1}^{-1}\Delta, 0), (0, s_{i}^{-1}\Delta) \}.$ 

Observe that

- when  $(\Delta_0, \Delta_1) = \overline{(s_{i-1}^{-1}\Delta, 0)}$ , the distribution is identical to  $\overline{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i-1,i}[2]}$ ; when  $(\Delta_0, \Delta_1) = \overline{(0, s_i^{-1}\Delta)}$ , the distribution is identical to  $\overline{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i}[2]}$  since  $\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} = \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}\mathbf{M}_{x_i^*} \mod p$  (see Lemma 5).

We sample  $\mathbf{d} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_n^{1 \times Q}$  and  $\widetilde{\mathbf{R}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_n^{k \times Q}$  and implicitly set

$$\Delta = \overline{\Delta}, \quad (\Delta_0, \Delta_1) = (\overline{\Delta}_0, \overline{\Delta}_1) \quad \text{and} \quad \mathbf{R} = \mathbf{r}^{\top} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1, x^*} + \mathbf{B} \cdot \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}.$$

We then generate the key for  $\Gamma$  as follows:

- We simulate  $[\mathbf{R}]_2$  from  $[\mathbf{r}^T]_2$ ,  $[\mathbf{B}]_2$  and  $\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}$ ,  $\widetilde{\mathbf{R}}$ .
- We rewrite the terms in the dashed box as follows:

$$[-\mathbf{d} + (\bar{\Delta}_0 + \mathbf{z}_{\tau} \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}) \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} + \mathbf{z}_{\tau} \mathbf{B} \cdot \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}]_2, \ [\mathbf{d} \mathbf{M}_{x_i^*} + (\bar{\Delta}_1 + \mathbf{w}_{x_i^*,\tau} \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}) \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} + \mathbf{w}_{x_i^*,\tau} \mathbf{B} \cdot \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}]_2$$

and simulate them using  $[\bar{\Delta}_0 + \mathbf{z}_{\tau} \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_2$ ,  $[\bar{\Delta}_1 + \mathbf{w}_{x_i^*, \tau} \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_2$ ,  $[\mathbf{z}_{\tau} \mathbf{B}]_2$ ,  $[\mathbf{w}_{x_i^*, \tau} \mathbf{B}]_2$  and  $\mathbf{d}, \mathbf{f}_{i-1, x^*}, \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}$ .

- We simulate all remaining terms using  $[\mathbf{R}]_2$  and  $\alpha$ ,  $\mathbf{d}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}$ ,  $\mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}$ ,  $\{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,\tau}\}_{\sigma \neq x_i^*}$ ,  $\{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\tau}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\text{end}}$ .

Observe that, when  $(\bar{\Delta}_0, \bar{\Delta}_1) = \boxed{(s_{i-1}^{-1}\bar{\Delta}, 0)}$ , we have  $(\Delta_0, \Delta_1) = \boxed{(s_{i-1}^{-1}\Delta, 0)}$ , then the secret key is  $\boxed{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i-1,i}[2]}$  and the simulation is identical to  $\mathsf{G}_{2.i.2}$ ; when  $(\bar{\Delta}_0, \bar{\Delta}_1) = \boxed{(0, s_i^{-1}\bar{\Delta})}$ , we have  $(\Delta_0, \Delta_1) = \boxed{(0, s_i^{-1}\Delta)}$ , then the secret key is  $\boxed{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i}[2]}$  and the simulation is identical to  $\mathsf{G}_{2.i.3}$ . This completes the proof.

#### <span id="page-24-1"></span>4.8 Finalize

<span id="page-24-4"></span>We finally prove that the adversary wins  $G_3$  with probability 1/2.

**Lemma 18.**  $Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_3 \rangle = 1] \approx 1/2.$ 

*Proof.* First, we argue that the secret key  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{\ell,*}$  in this game perfectly hides the  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -component of  $\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}$ , i.e.,  $\alpha = \mathbf{a}_2 \mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}$ . Recall the  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components of the secret key:

$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{\ell,*}[2] = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0,1\}} \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d} + \boxed{s_{\ell}^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\ell,x^{*}}} + \mathbf{w}_{\text{end}}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}.$$

By the property  $\mathbf{f}_{\ell,x^*} = \mathbf{f}$  (see Lemma 5), we can see that  $\mathsf{sk}_\Gamma^{\ell,*}[2]$  can be simulated using  $\alpha + s_\ell^{-1}\Delta$ , which means the secret key perfectly hides  $\alpha = \mathbf{a}_2\mathbf{k}^\top$ . Therefore, the unique term involving  $\mathbf{k}$  in  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^\ell$ , i.e.,  $[\mathbf{s}_\ell\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{k}^\top + s_\ell\mathbf{a}_2\mathbf{k}^\top]_T$ , is independently and uniformly distributed and thus statistically hides message  $m_\beta$ .

# <span id="page-24-0"></span>5 Adaptively Secure ABE for $\mathcal{E}_{\textit{O}}$ -restricted NFA $^{\oplus_{\textit{p}}}$ and DFA

In this section, we present our adaptively secure ABE for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NFA<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup>. By our transformation from DFA to  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NFA<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> (cf. Lemma 1), this readily gives us an adaptively secure ABE for DFA. We defer the concrete construction to Appendix **F**.

**Overview.** Our starting point is the selectively secure ABE scheme in Section 4. To achieve adaptive security, we handle key queries one by one following standard dual system method [20]; for each key, we carry out the one-key selective proof in Section 4 with piecewise guessing framework [15]. However this does not work immediately, we will make some changes to the scheme and proof in Section 4.

Recall that, in the one-key setting, the (selective) proof in Section 4 roughly tells us

<span id="page-24-3"></span>
$$(\mathsf{mpk}, \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}, \mathsf{ct}_{x^*}) \approx_c (\mathsf{mpk}, \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{\ell,*}), \mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{\ell}). \tag{25}$$

The two-key setting, for example, is expected to be handled by hybrid arguments:

$$(\mathsf{mpk}, \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma_1}, \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma_2}, \mathsf{ct}_{x^*}) \approx_c (\mathsf{mpk}, \boxed{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma_1}^{\ell,*}}, \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma_2}, \boxed{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{\ell}}) \approx_c (\mathsf{mpk}, \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma_1}^{\ell,*}, \boxed{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma_2}^{\ell,*}}, \mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{\ell})$$

<span id="page-24-2"></span> $<sup>\</sup>overline{^{10}}$  Handling all key queries simultaneously as in the selective model will cause a security loss exponential in the number of queries.

The first step seems to be feasible with some natural extension but the second one is problematic. Since we can not switch the challenge ciphertext back to  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}$  due to the presence of  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma_1}^{\ell,*}$ , the argument (25) can not be applied to the second key  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma_2}$  literally. In more detail, recall that

<span id="page-25-0"></span>
$$\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{\ell}[2] = \left( [s_{\ell} \mathbf{w}_{x_{\ell}^*, \bar{\ell}}]_1, [s_{\ell}]_1, [s_{\ell} \mathbf{w}_{\text{end}}]_1 \right) \tag{26}$$

leaks information of  $\mathbf{w}_{x_{\ell}^*,\bar{\ell}}$  and  $\mathbf{w}_{end}$  while we need them to be hidden in some steps of the one-key proof; for example, Lemma 4.7 for  $\mathsf{G}_{2.i.2} \approx_c \mathsf{G}_{2.i.3}$ . We quickly argue that the natural solution of adding an extra subspace for fresh copies of  $\mathbf{w}_{x_{\ell}^*,\bar{\ell}}$  and  $\mathbf{w}_{end}$  blows up the ciphertext and key sizes (see Section 1.1 for discussion).

Our approach reuses the existing  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components as in [8]. Recall that, our one-key proof (25) uses a series of hybrids with random coins  $s_0, s_1, \ldots$  and finally stops at a hybrid with  $s_\ell$  (cf. (25) and (26)). Roughly, we change the scheme by adding an extra random coin s into the ciphertext and move one more step in the proof so that we finally stop at a new hybrid with the new s only. This allows us to release  $s_\ell$  and reuse  $\mathbf{w}_{x_\ell^*, \bar{\ell}}, \mathbf{w}_{\text{end}}$  for the next key. More concretely, starting with the scheme in Section 4.2, we introduce a new component  $[\mathbf{W}]_1 \in G_1^{(2k+1)\times k}$  into mpk:

– during encryption, we pick one more random coin  $\mathbf{s} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  and replace the last three components in  $\mathsf{ct}_x$  with

$$[\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1]_1$$
,  $[\mathbf{s}_{\ell}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} + \mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{W}]_1$ ,  $[\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T \cdot m$ ;

this connects the last random coin  $\mathbf{s}_{\ell}$  with the newly introduced  $\mathbf{s}$ ; and  $\mathbf{s}$  corresponds to s in the proof;

– during key generation, we replace the last two components in  $\mathsf{sk}_\Gamma$  with

$$[-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{f} + \mathbf{W}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2;$$

the decryption will recover  $[\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{f} - \mathbf{s}_{\ell}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{D}]_T$  instead of  $[\mathbf{s}_{\ell}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{f} - \mathbf{s}_{\ell}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{D}]_T$ ;

- during the proof, we extend the proof in Section 4.3 by one more step (see the dashed box):

$$(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma},\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}) \overset{\S^{4.3}}{\approx_c} (\mathsf{mpk}, \boxed{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{\ell,*}}, \boxed{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{\ell}}) \boxed{\approx_c (\mathsf{mpk}, \boxed{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^*}, \boxed{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*})}$$

so that  $ct_{r^*}^*[2]$  is in the following form:

$$\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*[2] = ([s\mathbf{w}]_1, [s]_1, [s\alpha]_1 \cdot m_\beta)$$

which leaks  $\mathbf{w} = \mathbf{a}_2 \mathbf{W}$  instead of  $\mathbf{w}_{x_\ell^*, \bar{\ell}}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{end}$ ; by this, we can carry out the one-key proof (25) for the next key (with some natural extensions).

Conceptually, we can interpret this as letting the NFA move to a specific dummy state whenever it accepts the input. Such a modification has been mentioned in [4] for simplifying the description rather than improving security and efficiency. In our formal description below, we will rename  $\mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}$ ,  $\mathbf{s}$ ,  $\mathbf{s}$  as  $\mathbf{Z}_{\text{end}}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\text{end}}$ ,  $\mathbf{s}_{\text{end}}$ , respectively.

### <span id="page-25-1"></span>5.1 Scheme

Our adaptively secure ABE for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NFA<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> in prime-order groups use the same basis as described in Section 4.1 and is described as follows:

– Setup $(1^{\lambda}, \Sigma)$ : Run  $\mathbb{G} = (p, G_1, G_2, G_T, e) \leftarrow \mathcal{G}(1^{\lambda})$ . Sample

$$\mathbf{A}_1 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times (2k+1)}, \mathbf{k} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times (2k+1)} \quad \text{and} \quad \mathbf{W}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{Z}_0, \mathbf{Z}_1, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1}, \mathbf{Z}_{\text{end}}, \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(2k+1) \times k}, \ \forall \sigma \in \Sigma.$$

Output

$$\begin{aligned} & \mathsf{mpk} = \left( \left[ \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{start}, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{Z}_0, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{Z}_1, \left\{ \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1} \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{Z}_{end}, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{end} \right]_1, \left[ \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}} \right]_T \right) \\ & \mathsf{msk} = \left( \mathbf{k}, \mathbf{W}_{start}, \mathbf{Z}_0, \mathbf{Z}_1, \left\{ \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1} \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{Z}_{end}, \mathbf{W}_{end} \right). \end{aligned}$$

- Enc(mpk, x, m): Let  $x = (x_1, ..., x_\ell) \in \Sigma^\ell$  and  $m \in G_T$ . Pick  $\mathbf{s}_0, \mathbf{s}_1, ..., \mathbf{s}_\ell, \mathbf{s}_{\mathrm{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  and output

$$\mathsf{ct}_{x} = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{s}_{0}\mathbf{A}_{1}]_{1}, [\mathbf{s}_{0}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}}]_{1} \\ \{[\mathbf{s}_{j}\mathbf{A}_{1}]_{1}, [\mathbf{s}_{j-1}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{Z}_{j \bmod 2} + \mathbf{s}_{j}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{x_{j}, j \bmod 2}]_{1}\}_{j \in [\ell]} \\ [\mathbf{s}_{\mathsf{end}}\mathbf{A}_{1}]_{1}, [\mathbf{s}_{\ell}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{Z}_{\mathsf{end}} + \mathbf{s}_{\mathsf{end}}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{end}}]_{1}, [\mathbf{s}_{\mathsf{end}}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{T} \cdot m \end{pmatrix}.$$

- KeyGen(mpk, msk,  $\Gamma$ ): Let  $\Gamma = (Q, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_{\sigma}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f})$ . Pick  $\mathbf{D} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(2k+1) \times Q}$ ,  $\mathbf{R} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times Q}$  and output

$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma} = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{D}\mathbf{u}^{\top} + \mathbf{W}_{start}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2} \\ \{[-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{Z}_{b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{D}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0,1\}} \\ [-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{Z}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{k}^{\top}\mathbf{f} + \mathbf{W}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}.$$

– Dec(mpk,  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}$ ,  $\mathsf{ct}_x$ ): Parse ciphertext for  $x = (x_1, \dots, x_\ell)$  and key for  $\Gamma = (Q, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_\sigma\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f})$  as

$$\mathsf{ct}_{x} = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{c}_{0,1}]_{1}, [\mathbf{c}_{0,2}]_{1} \\ \left\{ [\mathbf{c}_{j,1}]_{1}, [\mathbf{c}_{j,2}]_{1} \right\}_{j} \\ [\mathbf{c}_{\mathrm{end},1}]_{1}, [\mathbf{c}_{\mathrm{end},2}]_{1}, C \end{pmatrix} \quad \text{and} \quad \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma} = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{k}_{0}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{r}_{0}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \left\{ [\mathbf{K}_{b}]_{2}, [\mathbf{K}_{\sigma,b}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \right\}_{\sigma,b} \\ [\mathbf{K}_{\mathrm{end},1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{K}_{\mathrm{end},2}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}$$

We define  $\mathbf{u}_{i,x}^{\mathsf{T}}$  for all  $j \in [0,\ell]$  as (11) in Section 4.2 and proceed as follows:

1. Compute

$$B_0 = e([\mathbf{c}_{0,1}]_1, [\mathbf{k}_0^{\mathsf{T}}]_2) \cdot e([\mathbf{c}_{0,2}]_1, [\mathbf{r}_0^{\mathsf{T}}]_2)^{-1};$$

2. For all  $j \in [\ell]$ , compute

$$[\mathbf{b}_j]_T = e([\mathbf{c}_{j-1,1}]_1, [\mathbf{K}_{j \mod 2}]_2) \cdot e([\mathbf{c}_{j,1}]_1, [\mathbf{K}_{x_i, j \mod 2}]_2) \cdot e([-\mathbf{c}_{j,2}]_1, [\mathbf{R}]_2)$$
 and  $B_j = [\mathbf{b}_j \mathbf{u}_{j-1,x}^\top]_T$ ;

3. Compute

$$[\mathbf{b}_{\text{end}}]_T = e([\mathbf{c}_{\ell,1}]_1, [\mathbf{K}_{\text{end},1}]_2) \cdot e([\mathbf{c}_{\text{end},1}]_1, [\mathbf{K}_{\text{end},2}]_2) \cdot e([-\mathbf{c}_{\text{end},2}]_1, [\mathbf{R}]_2) \quad \text{and} \quad B_{\text{end}} = [\mathbf{b}_{\text{end}}\mathbf{u}_{\ell,x}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T;$$

4. Compute

$$B_{\text{all}} = B_0 \cdot \prod_{j=1}^{\ell} B_j \cdot B_{\text{end}}$$
 and  $B = B_{\text{all}}^{(\mathbf{fu}_{\ell,x}^{\mathsf{T}})^{-1}}$ 

and output the message  $m' \leftarrow C \cdot B^{-1}$ .

It is direct to verify the correctness as in Section 4.2. See Appendix E.1 for more details.

**Security.** We prove the following theorem stating the adaptive security of the above ABE for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NFA $^{\oplus_p}$ . This readily implies our adaptively secure ABE for DFA thanks to Lemma 1.

<span id="page-26-0"></span>**Theorem 2** (Adaptively seucre ABE for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NFA $^{\oplus p}$ ). The ABE scheme for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NFA $^{\oplus p}$  in prime-order bilinear groups described above is adaptively secure (cf. Section 2.1) under the k-Lin assumption with security loss  $O(q \cdot \ell \cdot |\Sigma|^3 \cdot Q^2)$ . Here  $\ell$  is the length of the challenge input  $x^*$  and q is the number of key queries.

### <span id="page-26-1"></span>5.2 Proof of Main Theorem

From a high level, we employ the standard dual system proof switching the challenge ciphertext and keys into semi-functional forms in a one-by-one manner. To switch a secret key, we employ the proof technique for one-key selective setting in Section 4 in the piecewise guessing framework [15,14]. We will capture this by a core lemma. Let  $x^* \in \Sigma^{\ell}$  denote the adaptive challenge. We begin with auxiliary distributions and use the notation for  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components in Section 4.3.

**Auxiliary distributions.** We sample  $s_{\text{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ ,  $\Delta \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and define semi-functional ciphertext and key:

- $ct_{x^*}^*$  is the same as  $ct_{x^*}$  except we replace  $s_{end}A_1$  with  $s_{end}A_1 + s_{end}a_2$ ;
- $\ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^* \ \text{is the same as} \ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma} \ \text{except we replace} \ \mathbf{k}^{\!\top} \ \text{with} \ \mathbf{k}^{\!\top} + \mathbf{a}_2^{\!\parallel} \cdot s_{end}^{-1} \Delta \ \text{in the term} \ [\mathbf{k}^{\!\top} \mathbf{f} + \mathbf{W}_{end} \mathbf{R}]_2.$

That is, we have:

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*[2] &= \left( [s_{\mathrm{end}} \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}}]_1, [s_{\mathrm{end}}]_1, [s_{\mathrm{end}} \alpha]_T \cdot m_\beta \right) \\ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^*[2] &= \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d} \mathbf{u}^\top + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{start}} \mathbf{R} \mathbf{u}^\top]_2, [\mathbf{R} \mathbf{u}^\top]_2 \\ \left\{ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_b \mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{d} \mathbf{M}_\sigma + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,b} \mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0,1\}} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{\mathrm{end}} \mathbf{R}]_2, [\alpha \mathbf{f} + \boxed{s_{\mathrm{end}}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}} \mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \end{pmatrix} \end{split}$$

**Game sequence and core lemma.** We prove Theorem 2 via a series of games following standard dual system method [20]:

- G<sub>0</sub>: Identical to the real game.
- $G_1$ : Identical to  $G_0$  except that the challenge ciphertext is semi-functional, i.e.,  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*$ .
- $G_{2.\kappa}$  for  $\kappa \in [0, q]$ : Identical to  $G_1$  except that the first  $\kappa$  secret keys are semi-functional, i.e.,  $sk_{\Gamma}^*$ .
- $G_3$ : Identical to  $G_{2,q}$  except that the challenge ciphertext is an encryption of a random message.

Here we have  $G_{2.0} = G_1$ . It is standard to prove  $G_0 \approx_c G_1$ ,  $G_{2.q} \approx_s G_3$  and show that adversary in  $G_3$  has no advantage. We sketch the proofs in Appendix E.2. To prove  $G_{2.\kappa-1} \approx_c G_{2.\kappa}$  for all  $\kappa \in [q]$ , we use core lemma:

<span id="page-27-0"></span>**Lemma 19** (Core lemma). For all A, there exists B with  $Time(B) \approx Time(A)$  and

$$\mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{CORE}}_{\mathcal{A}}(\lambda) = \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_0 \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_1 \rangle = 1] \leq O(\ell \cdot |\Sigma|^3 \cdot Q^2) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}^{k\text{-Lin}}_{\mathcal{B}}(\lambda)$$

where, for all  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ , we define:

$$\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_b \rangle := \{ b' \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathsf{OEnc}(\cdot), \mathsf{OKey}(\cdot)}(\mathsf{mpk}, \mathsf{aux}_1, \mathsf{aux}_2) \}$$

where

$$\begin{aligned} & \mathsf{mpk} = \left( [\mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\textit{start}}, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{Z}_0, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{Z}_1, \{\mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{Z}_{\textit{end}}, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\textit{end}}]_1, [\mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T \right) \\ & \mathsf{aux}_1 = \left( [\mathbf{k}, \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{W}_{\textit{start}} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{Z}_0 \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{Z}_1 \mathbf{B}, \{\mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{B}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{Z}_{\textit{end}} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{W}_{\textit{end}} \mathbf{B}]_2 \right) \\ & \mathsf{aux}_2 = \left( [\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}, \mathbf{W}_{\textit{start}} \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}, \mathbf{Z}_0 \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}, \mathbf{Z}_1 \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}, \{\mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{Z}_{\textit{end}} \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}, \mathbf{a}_2^{\mathsf{I}} \cdot s_{\textit{end}}^{-1} \Delta + \mathbf{W}_{\textit{end}} \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_2 \right) \end{aligned}$$

with  $\mathbf{W}_{start}$ ,  $\mathbf{Z}_0$ ,  $\mathbf{Z}_1$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1}$ ,  $\mathbf{Z}_{end}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{end} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(2k+1)\times k}$ ,  $\mathbf{B} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}$ ,  $\mathbf{r} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1\times k}$ ,  $s_{end}$ ,  $\Delta \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and the two oracles work as follows:

- $OEnc(x^*, m)$ : output  $ct_{x^*}^*$  using  $s_{end}$  in  $aux_2$ ;
- $\ \mathsf{OKey}(\Gamma) : output \ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma} \ if \ b = 0; output \ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^* \ using \ \Delta \ and \ s_{end} \ in \ \mathsf{aux}_2 \ if \ b = 1;$

with the restrictions that (1) A makes only one query to each oracle; (2) queries  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$  satisfy  $\Gamma(x^*) = 0$ .

It is direct to see that the core lemma implies  $G_{2,\kappa-1} \approx_c G_{2,\kappa}$ ; here  $\mathsf{aux}_1$  and  $\mathsf{aux}_2$  are sufficient to simulate other q-1 keys which are either  $\mathsf{sk}_\Gamma$  or  $\mathsf{sk}_\Gamma^*$ , see Appendix E.2 for more details. The remaining of this section will be devoted to the proof of the core lemma, which completes the proof of Theorem 2.

### **5.3 Piecewise guessing framework**

We briefly review the piecewise guessing framework [\[15\]](#page-44-9) we will use in the proof of core lemma. Suppose we have two adaptive games H<sup>0</sup> and H<sup>1</sup> which we would like to show to be indistinguishable. In both games, an adversary A makes some adaptive choice *z* <sup>∗</sup> ∈ {0, 1}*<sup>R</sup>* . Informally, the piecewise guessing framework tells us that if we can show that H0,H<sup>1</sup> are *²*-indistinguishable in the selective setting where (1) all choices *z* ∗ are committed to in advance via a series of *L* + 1 hybrids and (2) each hybrid depends only on at most *R* <sup>0</sup> ¿ *R* bits of information about *z* ∗ , then H0,H<sup>1</sup> are 22*<sup>R</sup>* 0 ·*L* · *²*-indistinguishable in the adaptive setting. More formally, we define

- **–** a family of games {H *u* } *<sup>u</sup>*∈{0,1}*R*<sup>0</sup> where the messages sent to the adversary depend on *u*;
- **–** a family of *h*-functions *h*0,...,*h<sup>L</sup>* : {0, 1}*<sup>R</sup>* 7→ {0, 1}*<sup>R</sup>* 0 which describes the hybrids;

the piecewise guessing framework ensures that H<sup>0</sup> ≈*<sup>c</sup>* H<sup>1</sup> if {H *u* } *<sup>u</sup>*∈{0,1}*R*<sup>0</sup> and *h*0,...,*h<sup>L</sup>* satisfy

**–** end-point equivalence, which means:

$$\mathsf{H}_0 = \mathsf{H}^{h_0(z^*)}, \ \mathsf{H}_1 = \mathsf{H}^{h_L(z^*)} \quad \forall z^* \in \{0,1\}^R;$$

**–** neighbor indistinguishability, which means:

$$\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_{i,0}(u_0,u_1)\approx_c \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_{i,1}(u_0,u_1) \quad \forall i\in [L], u_0,u_1\in \{0,1\}^{R'}$$

where H<sup>b</sup> *<sup>i</sup>*,*b*(*u*0,*u*1) is the same as H *<sup>u</sup><sup>b</sup>* except we output 0 whenever (*hi*−1(*z* ∗ ),*hi*(*z* ∗ )) 6= (*u*0,*u*1).

<span id="page-28-0"></span>This is captured by the *adaptive security lemma* in [\[15\]](#page-44-9):

**Lemma 20 (adaptive security lemma [\[15\]](#page-44-9)).** *Fix* H0,H<sup>1</sup> *along with h*0,*h*1,...,*h<sup>L</sup>* : {0, 1}*<sup>R</sup>* → {0, 1}*<sup>R</sup>* 0 *and* {H *u* } *<sup>u</sup>*∈{0,1}*R*<sup>0</sup> *such that*

$$\forall z^* \in \{0,1\}^R : \mathsf{H}^{h_0(z^*)} = \mathsf{H}_0, \; \mathsf{H}^{h_L(z^*)} = \mathsf{H}_1$$

*Suppose there exists an adversary* A *such that*

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_0 \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_1 \rangle = 1] \ge \epsilon$$

*then there exists i* ∈ [*L*] *and u*0,*u*<sup>1</sup> ∈ {0, 1}*<sup>R</sup>* 0 *such that*

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_{i,0}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_{i,1}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] \geq \frac{\epsilon}{2^{2R'}L}.$$

### <span id="page-28-1"></span>**5.4 Proof of Core Lemma**

Observe that the core lemma roughly captures the one-key adaptive setting with mpk, key and ciphertext similar to our selectively secure ABE in [4.2.](#page-11-1) We prove the core lemma, Lemma [19,](#page-27-0) by combining the proof for one-key selective security in Section [4.3](#page-13-0) with the piecewise guessing framework reviewed above. In particular, we will use a family of hybrids, defined by H *u* and *h*-functions, analogous to those in Section [4.3.](#page-13-0) Let *`*¯ = *`* mod 2 and assume *`* > 1, we begin with more auxiliary distributions.

**More auxiliary distributions.** The auxiliary distributions we use here are motivated by those in Section [4.3.](#page-13-0)

*Ciphertext distributions.* We sample  $s_0, s_1, ..., s_\ell \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and define:

- for  $i \in [0,\ell]$ :  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^i$  is the same as  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{\mathsf{r}}$  except we replace  $\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1$  with  $\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1 + s_i \mathbf{a}_2$ ; for  $i \in [\ell]$ :  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1,i}$  is the same as  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{\mathsf{r}}$  except we replace  $\mathbf{s}_{i-1} \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1$  with  $\mathbf{s}_{i-1} \mathbf{A}_1 + s_{i-1} \mathbf{a}_2, \mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1 + s_i \mathbf{a}_2$ .

That is, we have: writing  $\tau = i \mod 2$ ,

$$\begin{split} \operatorname{ct}_{x^*}^i[2] &= \begin{cases} [s_0 \mathbf{w}_{\operatorname{start}}]_1, [s_0]_1, [s_0 \mathbf{z}_1]_1, \left[ [s_{\operatorname{end}} \mathbf{w}_{\operatorname{end}}]_1, [s_{\operatorname{end}} \alpha]_T \cdot m \right] & \text{if } i = 0 \\ [s_i \mathbf{w}_{x_i^*, \tau}]_1, [s_i]_1, [s_i \mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}]_1, \left[ [s_{\operatorname{end}} \mathbf{w}_{\operatorname{end}}]_1, [s_{\operatorname{end}} \alpha]_T \cdot m \right] & \text{if } i \in [\ell-1] \\ [s_\ell \mathbf{w}_{x_\ell^*, \ell}]_1, [s_\ell]_1, [s_\ell \mathbf{z}_{\operatorname{end}} + \left[ s_{\operatorname{end}} \mathbf{w}_{\operatorname{end}} \right]_1, \left[ [s_{\operatorname{end}} \alpha]_T \cdot m \right] & \text{if } i = \ell \end{cases} \\ \operatorname{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1, i}[2] &= \begin{cases} [s_0 \mathbf{w}_{\operatorname{start}}]_1, [s_0]_1, [s_0 \mathbf{z}_1 + s_1 \mathbf{w}_{x_1^*, 1}]_1, [s_1]_1, [s_1 \mathbf{z}_0]_1, \left[ [s_{\operatorname{end}} \mathbf{w}_{\operatorname{end}}]_1, \left[ [s_{\operatorname{end}} \alpha]_T \cdot m \right] & \text{if } i = 1 \\ [s_{i-1} \mathbf{w}_{x_{i-1}^*, 1-\tau}]_1, [s_{i-1}]_1, [s_{i-1} \mathbf{z}_T + s_i \mathbf{w}_{x_i^*, \tau}]_1, [s_i]_1, [s_i \mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}]_1, \left[ [s_{\operatorname{end}} \mathbf{w}_{\operatorname{end}}]_1, \left[ [s_{\operatorname{end}} \alpha]_T \cdot m \right] & \text{if } i \in [2, \ell-1] \\ [s_{\ell-1} \mathbf{w}_{x_{\ell-1}^*, 1-\ell}]_1, [s_{\ell-1}]_1, [s_{\ell-1} \mathbf{z}_{\ell} + s_\ell \mathbf{w}_{x_\ell^*, \ell}]_1, [s_\ell]_1, [s_\ell \mathbf{z}_{\operatorname{end}} + \left[ s_{\operatorname{end}} \mathbf{w}_{\operatorname{end}} \right]_1, \left[ [s_{\operatorname{end}} \alpha]_T \cdot m \right] & \text{if } i \in [\ell-1] \end{cases} \end{cases}$$

The auxiliary ciphertext distributions here are analogous to those in Section 4.3 except that they have extra terms  $[s_{\text{end}}\mathbf{w}_{\text{end}}]_1$ ,  $[s_{\text{end}}]_1$ ,  $[s_{\text{end}}\alpha]_T \cdot m$  inherited from  $\text{ct}_{x^*}^*$ . We highlighted the differences by dashed boxes.

Secret key distributions. Recall that a query to OKey is  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NFA $^{\oplus p}$ . For all  $i \in [\ell]$ ,  $\chi \in \Sigma$  and  $\mathbf{p} \in \mathcal{E}_Q$ , we define:

- $\begin{array}{l} -\ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{p}}^0 \ \mathrm{is}\ \mathrm{the}\ \mathsf{same}\ \mathsf{as}\ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}\ \mathsf{except}\ \mathsf{we}\ \mathsf{replace}\ \mathbf{D}\ \mathsf{with}\ \mathbf{D} + \mathbf{a}_2^{\mathbb{I}}\cdot s_0^{-1}\Delta\cdot\mathbf{p}\ \mathrm{in}\ \mathsf{the}\ \mathsf{term}\ [\mathbf{D}\mathbf{u}^{\!\top} + \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\!\top}]_2; \\ -\ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\chi,\mathbf{p}}^i \ \mathsf{is}\ \mathsf{the}\ \mathsf{same}\ \mathsf{as}\ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}\ \mathsf{except}\ \mathsf{we}\ \mathsf{replace}\ \mathbf{D}\ \mathsf{with}\ \mathbf{D} + \mathbf{a}_2^{\mathbb{I}}\cdot s_i^{-1}\Delta\cdot\mathbf{p}\ \mathsf{in}\ \mathsf{the}\ \mathsf{term}\ [\mathbf{D}\mathbf{M}_{\chi} + \mathbf{W}_{\chi,i\ \mathrm{mod}\ 2}\mathbf{R}]_2; \\ -\ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{p}}^{i-1,i} \ \mathsf{is}\ \mathsf{the}\ \mathsf{same}\ \mathsf{as}\ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}\ \mathsf{except}\ \mathsf{we}\ \mathsf{replace}\ -\mathbf{D}\ \mathsf{with}\ -\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{a}_2^{\mathbb{I}}\cdot s_{i-1}^{-1}\Delta\cdot\mathbf{p}\ \mathsf{in}\ \mathsf{the}\ \mathsf{term}\ [-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{Z}_{i\ \mathrm{mod}\ 2}\mathbf{R}]_2; \\ -\ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{\ell,*} \ \mathsf{is}\ \mathsf{the}\ \mathsf{same}\ \mathsf{as}\ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}\ \mathsf{except}\ \mathsf{we}\ \mathsf{replace}\ -\mathbf{D}\ \mathsf{with}\ -\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{a}_2^{\mathbb{I}}\cdot s_{\ell}^{-1}\Delta\cdot\mathbf{f}\ \mathsf{in}\ \mathsf{the}\ \mathsf{term}\ [-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{Z}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{R}]_2. \end{array}$

That is, we have: writing  $\tau = i \mod 2$ ,

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{p}}^{0}[2] &= \begin{pmatrix} [(\mathbf{d} + \boxed{s_{0}^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{p}})\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0,1\}} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{end}}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\alpha \mathbf{f} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{end}}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix} \\ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\chi,\mathbf{p}}^{i}[2] &= \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [(\mathbf{d} + \begin{bmatrix} \mathbf{s}_{i}^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{p} \end{bmatrix})\mathbf{M}_{\chi} + \mathbf{w}_{\chi,\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \} \\ \{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{end}}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\alpha \mathbf{f} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{end}}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \end{pmatrix} \\ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{p}}^{i-1,i}[2] &= \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{end}}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\alpha \mathbf{f} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{end}}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{end}}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\alpha \mathbf{f} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{end}}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}_{\sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0,1\}} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}_{\sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0,1\}} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}_{\sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0,1\}} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}_{\sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0,1\}} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}_{\sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0,1\}} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}_{\sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0,1\}} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}_{\sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0,1\}} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}_{\sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0,1\}} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{R}]_{2$$

The auxiliary secret key distributions here are analogous to those in Section 4.3 except that we use general  $\chi$  and  $\mathbf{p}$  in the place of  $x_i^*$  and  $\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}$ . Note that these correspond to the piecewise information we need to guess in the proof.

**Hybrids**  $\{H^u\}_u$  and h-functions. We are ready to define  $\{H^u\}_u$  and h-functions in the adaptive security lemma (Lemma 20).

*Defining u and*  $H^u$ . For our setting, we require u to determine the forms of ciphertext (output by OEnc) and key (output by OKey) in a hybrid, this includes the superscripts of key and ciphertext and piecewise information  $\chi$  and  $\mathbf{p}$ . For this purpose, we define

$$u \in I \times I \times \Sigma \times \mathcal{E}_O$$

where

$$I = \{0, 1, \dots, \ell, *\} \cup \{(0, 1), (1, 2), \dots, (\ell - 1, \ell), (\ell, *)\}$$

is the set of superscripts of auxiliary keys and ciphertexts,  $\Sigma$  and  $\mathcal{E}_Q$  includes all possibilities of  $\chi$  and  $\mathbf{p}$ , respectively. We allow a special symbol " $\bot$ " at any positions indicating an empty output. Then, for all  $u = (c, s, \chi, \mathbf{p}) \in I \times I \times \Sigma \times \mathcal{E}_Q$ , we define hybrid  $H^{c,s,\chi,\mathbf{p}}$  to be identical to  $H_0$  (or  $H_1$ ) except that

- oracle  $\mathsf{OEnc}(x^*, m)$  returns  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{\mathbb{C}}$ ;
- oracle  $\mathsf{OKey}(\Gamma)$  returns  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathsf{VVV}}^s$  with yyy depending on s or  $\mathsf{sk}_\Gamma$  when  $s=\bot.$

Here we always assume that C and S indicate well-defined auxiliary ciphertext and key distributions and yyy is always provided in u (i.e., not " $\perp$ ").

*Defining h-functions*. In both  $H_0$  and  $H_1$ , the adversary A adaptively chooses  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$ , therefore we employ a family of functions

$$h_{\times\times\times}: NFA^{\oplus p} \times \Sigma^* \to I \times I \times \Sigma \times \mathcal{E}_O$$

with the first input being  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted. Recall that, for an input  $x^*$  of length  $\ell$  and a  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NFA $^{\oplus p}$   $\Gamma$ , we can define  $\mathbf{f}_{0,x^*},\ldots,\mathbf{f}_{\ell,x^*}\in\mathcal{E}_Q$  as (22) in Section 4.3. We define h-functions as below which describes a series of hybrids analogous to those for selective security in Section 4.3. We show the corresponding selective game for each function as a remark.

$$\begin{array}{llllllllllllllllllllllllllllllllllll$$

Note that we have  $h_{2.i.0} = h_{2.i-1.4}$  for all  $i \in [2, \ell]$  and  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*$ ,  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^*$  are shown in Section 5.2. Fix  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$ , we summarize all h-functions by showing hybrids  $\mathsf{H}^{h_{\mathsf{XXX}}(\Gamma, x^*)}$  in Fig 8 (which is analogous to Fig 6 in Section 4.3).

**Outline of the proof.** Roughly, the adaptive security lemma [15] (see Lemma 20) says that we only need to check (1) end-point equivalence and (2) neighbor indistinguishability.

*End-point equivalence.* It is clear that our hybrids  $\{H^u\}_u$  and h-functions satisfy the end-point equivalence. This follows from the fact that  $h_0$  and  $h_5$  are constant functions which indicate the same types of ciphertext and key as in  $H_0$  and  $H_1$ , respectively. Formally, we give the following lemma.

**Lemma 21** (End-point equivalence). For all  $(\Gamma, x^*) \in \{0, 1\}^R$ , we have

<span id="page-30-0"></span>
$$H^{h_0(\Gamma,x^*)} = H_0$$
 and  $H^{h_5(\Gamma,x^*)} = H_1$ .

<span id="page-31-0"></span>

| $h_{XXX}$      | $ct^{\scriptscriptstyle{\mathrm{C}}}_{x^*}$ |                                                                                                        |                                                                               |                                                                              | $sk^{\mathrm{S}}_{\Gamma,\pmb{\chi},\pmb{p}}[2]$                       |                                                                    |                                                               |                                                    | Remark                                                                                             |
|----------------|---------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------|---------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|                |                                             |                                                                                                        | $? \cdot \mathbf{u}^{\top} + \mathbf{w}_{start} \mathbf{R} \mathbf{u}^{\top}$ | $? \cdot \mathbf{M}_{x_{i-1}^*} + \mathbf{w}_{x_{i-1}^*, 1-\tau} \mathbf{R}$ | $? + \mathbf{z}_{\tau} \mathbf{R}$                                     | $? \cdot \mathbf{M}_{x_i^*} + \mathbf{w}_{x_i^*, \tau} \mathbf{R}$ | $? + \mathbf{z}_{end}\mathbf{R}$                              | $? \cdot \mathbf{f} + \mathbf{w}_{end} \mathbf{R}$ |                                                                                                    |
| 0              | $ct^*_{x^*}$                                | $sk_\Gamma$                                                                                            | d                                                                             | d                                                                            | -d                                                                     | d                                                                  | -d                                                            | α                                                  | real game                                                                                          |
