| 2.i.4          | $ct^i_{x^*}$                                | $sk^i_{\Gamma,x_i^*,\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}}$                                                               | d                                                                             | d                                                                            | <b>−d</b>                                                              | $\mathbf{d} + s_i^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}$            |                                                               | $\alpha$                                           | switching lemma                                                                                    |
| 3              | $ct^\ell_{x^*}$                             | $sk_\Gamma^{\ell,*}$                                                                                   | d                                                                             | d                                                                            | <b>−d</b>                                                              | d                                                                  | $-\mathbf{d} + \boxed{s_{\ell}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}}$ | α                                                  | change of variables, DDH, $\mathbf{f}_{\ell,\chi^*} = \mathbf{f}$ (Lemma 5)                        |
| 4              | $ct^\ell_{x^*}$                             | $sk_\Gamma^*$                                                                                          | d                                                                             | d                                                                            | $-\mathbf{d}$                                                          | d                                                                  | -d                                                            |                                                    | transition lemma                                                                                   |
| 5              | $ct^*_{x^*}$                                | $sk_\Gamma^*$                                                                                          | d                                                                             | d                                                                            | -d                                                                     | d                                                                  | -d                                                            | $\alpha + s_{\text{end}}^{-1} \Delta$              | switching lemma                                                                                    |

**Fig. 8.** Definition of h-functions with  $i \in [\ell]$ . In the table, we show both ciphertext and key in  $\mathsf{H}^{h_{\mathsf{XXX}}(\Gamma,x^*)}$ ; as in Fig 6, we only describe the  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components of the key. In the **Remark** column, "DDH" indicates DDH $_{1,Q}^{G_2}$  assumption.

*Neighbor indistinguishability.* We first define several pairs of hybrids with  $b \in \{0,1\}$ :

-  $\hat{\mathsf{H}}_0^b(u_0,u_1)$  is the same as  $\mathsf{H}^{u_b}$  except that we output 0 whenever

$$(h_0(\Gamma, x^*), h_1(\Gamma, x^*)) \neq (u_0, u_1).$$

-  $\hat{H}_1^b(u_0, u_1)$  is the same as  $H^{u_b}$  except that we output 0 whenever

$$(h_1(\Gamma, x^*), h_{2.1.0}(\Gamma, x^*)) \neq (u_0, u_1).$$

 $-\widehat{H}^b_{2\;i\;i'}(u_0,u_1)$ , for  $i\in[\ell]$  and  $i'\in[4]$ , is the same as  $H^{u_b}$  except that we output 0 whenever

$$(h_{2.i.i'-1}(\Gamma, x^*), h_{2.i,i'}(\Gamma, x^*)) \neq (u_0, u_1).$$

-  $\hat{H}_{3}^{b}(u_0, u_1)$  is the same as  $H^{u_b}$  except that we output 0 whenever

$$(h_{2,\ell,4}(\Gamma, x^*), h_3(\Gamma, x^*)) \neq (u_0, u_1).$$

-  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_4^b(u_0,u_1)$  is the same as  $\mathsf{H}^{u_b}$  except that we output 0 whenever

$$(h_3(\Gamma, x^*), h_4(\Gamma, x^*)) \neq (u_0, u_1).$$

-  $\hat{H}_{5}^{b}(u_0, u_1)$  is the same as  $H^{u_b}$  except that we output 0 whenever

$$(h_4(\Gamma, x^*), h_5(\Gamma, x^*)) \neq (u_0, u_1).$$

We will prove that each pair of hybrids are indistinguishable for all  $u_0$ ,  $u_1 \in I \times I \times \Sigma \times \mathcal{E}_Q$ . Straightforward extensions of the proofs in Section 4 are sufficient for the proof, we formally describe the lemma and defer all details to Appendix E.3.

<span id="page-32-1"></span>**Lemma 22** (Neighbor indistinguishability). For all  $\times \times \times \in \{0, 1, 3, 4, 5\} \cup \{2.i.i' : i \in [\ell], i' \in [4]\}$ ,  $u_0, u_1 \in I \times I \times \Sigma \times \mathcal{E}_Q$  and all A, there exists B with  $\mathsf{Time}(B) \approx \mathsf{Time}(A)$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^0_{\times\!\times\!\times}(u_0,u_1)\rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^1_{\times\!\times\!\times}(u_0,u_1)\rangle = 1] \leq O(|\Sigma|) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}^{k\text{-Lin}}_{\mathcal{B}}(\lambda).$$

*Summary.* By the adaptive security lemma (Lemma 20), Lemma 21 and Lemma 22 imply the core lemma, Lemma 19, with the following two facts:

- all our h-functions have range of size at most  $O(|\Sigma|Q)$  since the first two outputs are constant and  $|\mathcal{E}_Q| = Q$ ; that is, we have  $R' = O(\log |\Sigma|) + O(\log Q)$ ;
- our proof employs  $O(\ell)$  *h*-functions; that is we have  $L = O(\ell)$ .

## <span id="page-32-0"></span>6 Compact Adaptively Secure ABE for Branching Programs

In this section, we present our compact adaptively secure ABE for branching programs. We follow the same technical line as that for our adaptively secure ABE for DFA from Section 3 to Section 5. In particular, we construct a semi-adaptively secure ABE for NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup>, which is an analogue of NFA $^{\oplus p}$ ; then prove that the same scheme is adaptively secure for a subclass of NBP $^{\oplus p}$  in the piecewise guessing framework. This is sufficient to derive our scheme for branching program. Before that, we begin with various notions of branching programs and their relationship.

### <span id="page-32-2"></span>6.1 (Layered) Branching Programs: Notions and Relationship

Recall that p is a global parameter and  $\mathcal{E}_Q = \{\mathbf{e}_1, \dots, \mathbf{e}_Q\}$  is the set of all elementary row vectors of dimension Q. In this section, we focus on *layered* branching programs.

**Branching Programs.** As in Section 3, we use vector-matrix notation  $\Gamma = (Q, \ell_{BP}, \ell, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma}\}_{j \in [\ell_{BP}], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \rho, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f})$  to describe branching program (BP for short), nondeterministic branching program (NBP for short), p-bounded NBP (NBP<sup>< p</sup> for short) and mod-p NBP (NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> for short) where width  $Q \in \mathbb{N}$  corresponds to the number states in NFA,  $\ell_{\text{BP}}, \ell \in \mathbb{N}$ describe program and input length,  $\Sigma$  is the alphabet,  $\mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f} \in \{0,1\}^Q$  correspond to the start and accept states in NFA;  $\mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma} \in \{0,1\}^{Q \times Q}$  and  $\rho : [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}] \to [\ell]$  describe the transition function and index-to-input map. Let  $x = (x_1, \dots, x_\ell)$  denote an input, then,

- for BP  $\Gamma$ , we have  $\mathbf{u} \in \mathcal{E}_O$ , each column in every matrix  $\mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma}$  is an elementary column vector (i.e., contains exactly one 1) and  $\Gamma(x) = 1 \iff \mathbf{f} \mathbf{M}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}, x_{\rho(\ell_{\mathrm{BP}})}} \cdots \mathbf{M}_{1, x_{\rho(1)}} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} = 1;$
- for NBP  $\Gamma$ , we have  $\Gamma(x) = 1 \iff \mathbf{f} \mathbf{M}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}, x_{\rho(\ell_{\mathrm{BP}})}} \cdots \mathbf{M}_{1, x_{\rho(1)}} \mathbf{u}^{\top} \ge 1;$  for NBP<sup><p</sup>  $\Gamma$ , we have  $\mathbf{f} \mathbf{M}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}, x_{\rho(\ell_{\mathrm{BP}})}} \cdots \mathbf{M}_{1, x_{\rho(1)}} \mathbf{u}^{\top}$
- for NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup>  $\Gamma$ , we have  $\Gamma(x) = 1 \iff \mathbf{fM}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}, x_{\rho(\ell_{\mathrm{RP}})}} \cdots \mathbf{M}_{1, x_{\rho(1)}} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} \neq 0 \bmod p$ .

As various notions of DFA and NFA, we have:  $BP \subset NBP^{< p} \subset NBP \cap NBP^{\oplus p}$ .

 $\mathcal{E}_{Q}$ -restricted NBP $^{\oplus p}$ . We introduce the notion of  $\mathcal{E}_{Q}$ -restricted NBP $^{\oplus p}$  which is analogous to that of  $\mathcal{E}_{Q}$ -restricted NFA<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> in Section 3. An NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup>  $\Gamma = (Q, \ell_{BP}, \ell, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma}\}_{j \in [\ell_{BP}], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \rho, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f})$  is  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted if for all  $x \in \Sigma^\ell$ , it holds that

$$\mathbf{f}_{i,x} := \mathbf{f} \mathbf{M}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}, x_{\rho(\ell_{\mathrm{RP}})}} \cdots \mathbf{M}_{i+1, x_{\rho(i+1)}} \in \mathcal{E}_{Q}, \forall i \in [0, \ell].$$

Here  $\mathbf{M}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}},x_{\varrho(\ell_{\mathrm{BP}})}}\cdots\mathbf{M}_{i+1,x_{\varrho(i+1)}}$  for  $i=\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}$  refers to **I** of size  $Q\times Q$ .

**Transforming BP to**  $\mathcal{E}_{O}$ -restricted NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup>. In general, a BP is not necessarily a  $\mathcal{E}_{O}$ -restricted NBP $^{\oplus p}$ . The next lemma says that we can nonetheless transform any BP into a  $\mathcal{E}_O$ -restricted NBP $^{\oplus p}$ :

<span id="page-33-2"></span>**Lemma 23** (BP to  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup>). For each branching program  $\Gamma = (Q, \ell_{BP}, \ell, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma}\}_{j \in [\ell_{BP}], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \rho, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f}), we$ have  $NBP^{\oplus_p}$   $\Gamma^{\top} = (Q, \ell_{BP}, \ell, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_{\tau(j), \sigma}^{\top}\}_{j \in [\ell_{BP}], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \rho \circ \tau, \mathbf{f}, \mathbf{u})$  with  $\tau(j) = \ell_{BP} + 1 - j$  for all  $j \in [\ell_{BP}]$  such that

- 1.  $\Gamma^{\mathsf{T}}$  is  $\mathcal{E}_{Q}$ -restricted;
- 2. for all  $x \in \Sigma^{\ell}$ , it holds that

<span id="page-33-1"></span>
$$\Gamma(x) = \Gamma^{\top}(x). \tag{27}$$

*Proof.* Recall that the definition of BP implies two properties:

$$\mathbf{f} \in \{0,1\}^Q \tag{28}$$

<span id="page-33-0"></span>and 
$$(\mathbf{M}_{i,x_{\rho(i)}}\cdots\mathbf{M}_{1,x_{\rho(1)}}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}})^{\mathsf{T}}\in\mathcal{E}_{Q}, \quad \forall i\in[0,\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}].$$
 (29)

Property (29) comes from the facts that  $\mathbf{u} \in \mathcal{E}_Q$  and each column in every matrix  $\mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma}$  is an elementary column vector. We prove the two parts of the lemma as below.

–  $\Gamma^{\mathsf{T}}$  is  $\mathcal{E}_{O}$ -restricted since we have

$$\mathbf{u}\mathbf{M}_{\tau(\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}),x_{\rho\circ\tau(\ell_{\mathrm{BP}})}}^{\top}\cdots\mathbf{M}_{\tau(i+1),x_{\rho\circ\tau(i+1)}}^{\top}=(\mathbf{M}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}-i,x_{\rho(\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}-i)}}\cdots\mathbf{M}_{1,x_{\rho(1)}}\mathbf{u}^{\top})^{\top}\in\mathcal{E}_{Q},\quad\forall\,i\in[0,\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}]$$

where the equality is implied by the structure of  $\Gamma^{\mathsf{T}}$  and we use property (29).

- To prove (27), we rely on the fact

$$\begin{split} \Gamma(x) &= 1 \iff \mathbf{f} \mathbf{M}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}, x_{\rho(\ell_{\mathrm{BP}})}} \cdots \mathbf{M}_{1, x_{\rho(1)}} \mathbf{u}^{\top} = 1 \\ &\iff \mathbf{f} \mathbf{M}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}, x_{\rho(\ell_{\mathrm{BP}})}} \cdots \mathbf{M}_{1, x_{\rho(1)}} \mathbf{u}^{\top} \neq 0 \bmod p \\ &\iff \mathbf{u} \mathbf{M}_{\tau(\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}), x_{\rho \circ \tau(\ell_{\mathrm{BP}})}}^{\top} \cdots \mathbf{M}_{\tau(1), x_{\rho \circ \tau(1)}}^{\top} \mathbf{f}^{\top} \neq 0 \bmod p \\ &\iff \Gamma^{\top}(x) = 1. \end{split}$$

The second  $\iff$  follows from the fact that  $\mathbf{f}\mathbf{M}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}},x_{\rho(\ell_{\mathrm{RP}})}}\cdots\mathbf{M}_{1,x_{\rho(1)}}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}\in\{0,1\}$  which is implied by property (28) and (29) while the third  $\iff$  is implied by the structure of  $\Gamma^{\mathsf{T}}$ . 

#### <span id="page-34-0"></span>**6.2** Our ABE scheme for NBP $^{\oplus p}$

In this section, we describe our ABE scheme for NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> in the prime-order group which is motivated by our ABE scheme for NFA<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> in Section 4. We will prove that this scheme is semi-adaptively secure under k-Lin assumption (see Section 6.3) and adaptively secure if the policy is  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted under the same assumption (see Section 6.4). We remark that our scheme and proofs work for a more general form of NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> where  $\mathbf{u}$ ,  $\mathbf{f}$ ,  $\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma}$  are over  $\mathbb{Z}_p$  instead of  $\{0,1\}$ .

**Overview.** Thanks to the similarity between NFA<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> and NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> (cf. Section 3 and Section 6.1), we build our ABE for NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> following the same paradigm as the ABE for NFA<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> in Section 4. In particular, we pick  $\mathbf{W}_{\eta,\sigma}$  for each  $\eta \in \ell$  and  $\sigma \in \Sigma$  and pick  $\mathbf{D}_i$  for each  $j \in [0, \ell_{\mathrm{BP}}]$ .

- During the key generation, we encode each  $\mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma}$  as follows, which follows the spirit of our ABE for NFA<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup>:

$$[\mathbf{D}_{j}\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma}-\mathbf{D}_{j-1}+\mathbf{W}_{\rho(j),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2},\,[\mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2};$$

– During the encryption of  $x = (x_1, ..., x_\ell) \in \Sigma^\ell$ , we have the following terms in the ciphertext as common ABEs:

$$[\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1]_1, \{[\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{W}_{\eta, x_{\eta}}]_1\}_{\eta \in [\ell]}, [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T \cdot m.$$

In contrast to ABE for NFA<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup>, we use fresh random coin  $\mathbf{R}_j$  for each j in secret keys. This is crucial to handle non-injective  $\rho$ , see Appendix G.1 for an attack in the case of sharing random coins.

**Basis.** We will use the following basis used in [7,15] (which is distinct from that in Section 4 and 5):

$$\mathbf{A}_1 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times (k+1)}, \quad \mathbf{a}_2 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times (k+1)}$$

and use  $(\mathbf{A}_1^{\parallel} \mid \mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel})^{\top}$  to denote its dual basis. The assumption  $\mathrm{SD}_{\mathbf{A}_1 \mapsto \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{a}_2}^{G_1}$  and  $\mathrm{DDH}_{d,Q}^{G_2}$  can be defined as in Section 4.1.

**Scheme.** Our ABE for  $NBP^{\oplus p}$  in prime-order groups is described as follows:

– Setup $(1^{\lambda}, \ell, \Sigma)$ : Run  $\mathbb{G} = (p, G_1, G_2, G_T, e) \leftarrow \mathcal{G}(1^{\lambda})$ . Sample

$$\mathbf{A}_1 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times (k+1)}, \mathbf{k} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times (k+1)} \quad \text{and} \quad \mathbf{W}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{W}_{\eta, \sigma}, \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+1) \times k} \text{ for all } \eta \in [\ell], \sigma \in \Sigma.$$

Output

$$\begin{aligned} & \mathsf{mpk} = \left( \left[ \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}}, \left\{ \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\eta, \sigma} \right\}_{\eta \in [\ell], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{end} \right]_1, \left[ \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{k}^\top \right]_T \right) \\ & \mathsf{msk} = \left( \mathbf{k}, \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}}, \left\{ \mathbf{W}_{\eta, \sigma} \right\}_{\eta \in [\ell], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{W}_{end} \right). \end{aligned}$$

– Enc(mpk, x, m): Let  $x = (x_1, ..., x_\ell) \in \Sigma^\ell$  and  $m \in G_T$ . Pick  $\mathbf{s} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  and output

$$\mathsf{ct}_{x} = \left( [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_{1}]_{1}, [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}}]_{1}, \left\{ [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{\eta, x_{\eta}}]_{1} \right\}_{\eta \in [\ell]}, [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{end}}]_{1}, [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{T} \cdot m \right).$$

- KeyGen(mpk, msk,  $\Gamma$ ): Let  $\Gamma = (Q, \ell_{BP}, \ell, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma}\}_{j \in [\ell_{BP}], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \rho, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f})$ . Pick

$$\mathbf{D}_0, \mathbf{D}_1, \dots, \mathbf{D}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+1) \times Q}, \, \mathbf{R}_1, \dots, \mathbf{R}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}}, \mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times Q}, \, \mathbf{r} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$$

and output

$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma} = \left( \begin{aligned} [\mathbf{D}_0 \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{W}_{start} \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_2, [\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_2 \\ \left\{ [\mathbf{D}_j \mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{D}_{j-1} + \mathbf{W}_{\rho(j),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_j]_2, [\mathbf{R}_j]_2 \right\}_{j \in [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}], \sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{D}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{W}_{\mathrm{end}} \mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2 \end{aligned} \right).$$

- Dec(mpk, sk $_{\Gamma}$ , ct $_{x}$ ): Parse ciphertext for  $x = (x_{1}, \dots, x_{\ell})$  and key for  $\Gamma = (Q, \ell_{\mathrm{BP}}, \ell, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma}\}_{j \in [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \rho, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f})$  as:

$$\mathsf{ct}_x = \left( [\mathbf{c}]_1, [\mathbf{c}_{\mathsf{start}}]_1, \left\{ [\mathbf{c}_{\eta}]_1 \right\}_{\eta}, [\mathbf{c}_{\mathsf{end}}]_1, C \right) \quad \mathsf{and} \quad \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma} = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{k}_{\mathsf{start}}^{\mathsf{T}}]_2, [\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_2 \\ \left\{ [\mathbf{K}_{j,\sigma}]_2, [\mathbf{R}_j]_2 \right\}_{j,\sigma} \\ [\mathbf{K}_{\mathsf{end}}]_2, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathsf{end}}]_2 \end{pmatrix}$$

We define

<span id="page-35-1"></span>
$$\mathbf{u}_{j,x}^{\mathsf{T}} = \mathbf{M}_{j,x_{\rho(j)}} \cdots \mathbf{M}_{1,x_{\rho(1)}} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} \bmod p, \ \forall j \in [0,\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}]$$
(30)

which are analogous to (11) for NFA $^{\oplus p}$  in Section 4.2 and proceed as follows:

1. Compute

$$B_{\text{start}} = e([\mathbf{c}]_1, [\mathbf{k}_{\text{start}}^{\top}]_2) \cdot e([\mathbf{c}_{\text{start}}]_1, [\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2)^{-1};$$

2. For all  $j = 1, ..., \ell_{BP}$ , compute

$$[\mathbf{b}_j]_T = e([\mathbf{c}]_1, [\mathbf{K}_{j,x_{\rho(j)}}]_2) \cdot e([-\mathbf{c}_{\rho(j)}]_1, [\mathbf{R}_j]_2) \quad \text{and} \quad B_j = [\mathbf{b}_j \mathbf{u}_{j-1,x}^\top]_T;$$

3. Compute

$$[\mathbf{b}_{\mathrm{end}}]_T = e([\mathbf{c}]_1, [\mathbf{K}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2) \cdot e([-\mathbf{c}_{\mathrm{end}}]_1, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2)$$
 and  $B_{\mathrm{end}} = [\mathbf{b}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{u}_{\ell_{\mathrm{RP}}, x}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T$ ;

4. Compute

$$B_{\text{all}} = B_{\text{start}} \cdot \prod_{j=1}^{\ell_{\text{BP}}} B_j \cdot B_{\text{end}}$$
 and  $B = B_{\text{all}}^{(\mathbf{f} \mathbf{u}_{\ell_{\text{BP}},x}^{\top})^{-1}}$ 

and output the message  $m' \leftarrow C \cdot B^{-1}$ .

**Correctness.** For  $x = (x_1, ..., x_\ell)$  and  $\Gamma = (Q, \ell_{BP}, \ell, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma}\}_{j \in [\ell_{BP}], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \rho, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f})$  such that  $\Gamma(x) = 1$ , we have:

<span id="page-35-0"></span>
$$B_{\text{start}} = [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{D}_0\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T = [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{D}_0\mathbf{u}_{0,x}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T$$
(31)

$$\mathbf{b}_{j} = \mathbf{s} \mathbf{A}_{1} \mathbf{D}_{j} \mathbf{M}_{j, x_{o(j)}} - \mathbf{s} \mathbf{A}_{1} \mathbf{D}_{j-1}$$
(32)

$$B_j = [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{D}_j\mathbf{u}_{j,x}^{\top} - \mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{D}_{j-1}\mathbf{u}_{j-1,x}^{\top}]_T$$
(33)

$$\mathbf{b}_{\text{end}} = \mathbf{s} \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{s} \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{D}_{\ell_{\text{BP}}}$$
 (34)

$$B_{\text{end}} = [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{f}\mathbf{u}_{\ell_{\text{BP}},x}^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{D}_{\ell_{\text{BP}}}\mathbf{u}_{\ell_{\text{BP}},x}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{T}$$
(35)

$$B_{\text{all}} = [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{f}\mathbf{u}_{\ell_{\text{RP}},x}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T \tag{36}$$

$$B = [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T \tag{37}$$

Here (35) is trivial; (33) and (37) follow from facts

<span id="page-35-2"></span>
$$\mathbf{u}_{j,x}^{\top} = \mathbf{M}_{j,x_{\rho(j)}} \mathbf{u}_{j-1,x}^{\top} \bmod p, \ \forall j \in [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}] \quad \text{and} \quad \Gamma(x) = 1 \Longleftrightarrow \mathbf{f} \mathbf{u}_{\ell_{\mathrm{RP}},x}^{\top} \neq 0 \bmod p$$
(38)

by the definition in (30), the remaining equalities follow from:

$$\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{D}_{0}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} = \mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_{1} \cdot (\mathbf{D}_{0}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{W}_{start}\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}) - \mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{start} \cdot \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}$$

$$(\textbf{32}) \ \ \textbf{s} \\ \textbf{A}_{1} \\ \textbf{D}_{j} \\ \textbf{M}_{j,x_{\rho(j)}} \\ - \ \textbf{s} \\ \textbf{A}_{1} \\ \textbf{D}_{j-1} \\ = \ \ \textbf{s} \\ \textbf{A}_{1} \cdot (\textbf{D}_{j} \\ \textbf{M}_{j,x_{\rho(j)}} \\ - \ \textbf{D}_{j-1} \\ + \ \textbf{W}_{\rho(j),x_{\rho(j)}} \\ \textbf{R}_{j}) \\ - \ \textbf{s} \\ \textbf{A}_{1} \\ \textbf{W}_{\rho(j),x_{\rho(j)}} \cdot \\ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{S} \\ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{S} \\ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{S} \\ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{S} \\ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{S} \\ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{S} \\ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{S} \\ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{S} \\ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{S} \\ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{S} \\ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{S} \\ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{S} \\ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{S} \\ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{S} \\ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{S} \\ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{S} \\ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{S} \\ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{S} \\ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ + \ \textbf{R}_{j} \\ +$$

$$(\mathbf{34}) \hspace{1cm} \mathbf{s} \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{k}^{\top} \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{s} \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{D}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} = \hspace{1cm} \mathbf{s} \mathbf{A}_1 \cdot (\mathbf{k}^{\top} \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{D}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{W}_{end} \mathbf{R}_{end}) - \mathbf{s} \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{end} \cdot \mathbf{R}_{end}$$

$$\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{f}\mathbf{u}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}},x}^{\mathsf{T}} = \mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{D}_{0}\mathbf{u}_{0,x}^{\mathsf{T}} + \sum_{j=1}^{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}}(\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{D}_{j}\mathbf{u}_{j,x}^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{D}_{j-1}\mathbf{u}_{j-1,x}^{\mathsf{T}}) + (\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{f}\mathbf{u}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}},x}^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{D}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}}\mathbf{u}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}},x}^{\mathsf{T}}).$$

Correctness follows readily.

### <span id="page-36-0"></span>6.3 Semi-adaptive Security Security

We have the following theorem stating that the scheme in Section 6.2 is selectively secure. We remark that the proof described in this subsection can be naturally extended to prove semi-adaptive security.

<span id="page-36-1"></span>**Theorem 3** (Selectively secure ABE for NBP $^{\oplus p}$ ). The ABE scheme for NBP $^{\oplus p}$  in prime-order bilinear groups described above is selectively secure (cf. Section 2.1) under the k-Lin assumption with security loss  $O(q \cdot \ell_{BP} \cdot |\Sigma|)$ . Here  $\ell_{BP}$  are maximal length of all NBPs in adversary's key queries and q is the number of key queries.

We will give the proof in the one-key setting which is sufficient to motivate adaptive proof in Section 6.4 where we will handle multiple key queries. Due to the similarity between NBP $^{\oplus p}$  and NFA $^{\oplus p}$ , our proof technique for NBP $^{\oplus p}$  in this section is borrowed from that for NFA $^{\oplus p}$  in Section 4. We begin with auxiliary distributions.

**Auxiliary distributions.** Let  $x^* \in \Sigma^{\ell}$  denote the selective challenge and assume  $\ell_{BP} > 1$ . We describe the auxiliary ciphertext and key distributions that we use in the proof of security. Throughout, the distributions are the same as the original distributions except for the  $a_2$ -components which are defined analogous to Section 4.3; we will use the same notation for them.

*Ciphertext distribution.* We sample  $s \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and define:

-  $ct_{x^*}^*$  is the same as  $ct_{x^*}$  except we replace  $sA_1$  with  $sA_1 + sa_2$ .

That is, we have:

$$\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*[2] = \big( [s]_1, [s\mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}]_1, \big\{ [s\mathbf{w}_{\eta, x_{\eta}}]_1 \big\}_{\eta \in [\ell]}, [s\mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{end}}]_1, [s\alpha]_T \cdot m_{\beta} \big).$$

Secret key distributions. For any  $\Gamma = (Q, \ell_{BP}, \ell, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma}\}_{i \in [\ell_{BP}], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \rho, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f})$ , we define

<span id="page-36-2"></span>
$$\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} = \mathbf{f} \mathbf{M}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}, x_{\rho(\ell_{\mathrm{BP}})}^*} \cdots \mathbf{M}_{i+1, x_{\rho(i+1)}^*} \bmod p, \ \forall i \in [0, \ell_{\mathrm{BP}}]$$
(39)

analogous to (22) for NFA<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> in Section 4.3. For all  $i \in [\ell_{BP}]$ , we sample  $\Delta \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and define:

- $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^0 \text{ is the same as } \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma} \text{ except we replace } \mathbf{D}_0 \text{ with } \mathbf{D}_0 + \mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*} \text{ in the term } [\mathbf{D}_0 \mathbf{u}^{\top} + \mathbf{W}_{start} \mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2;$
- $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^i$  is the same as  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}$  except we replace  $\mathbf{D}_i$  with  $\mathbf{D}_i + \mathbf{a}_2^{\mathbb{I}} \cdot \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}$  in the term  $[\mathbf{D}_i \mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma} \mathbf{D}_{i-1} + \mathbf{W}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_i]_2$  for all  $\sigma \in \Sigma$ ;  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i-1,i}$  is the same as  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}$  except we replace  $-\mathbf{D}_{i-1}$  with  $-\mathbf{D}_{i-1} + \mathbf{a}_2^{\mathbb{I}} \cdot \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}$  in the term  $[\mathbf{D}_i \mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma} \mathbf{D}_{i-1} + \mathbf{W}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_i]_2$
- $\ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^* \ \text{is the same as} \ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma} \ \text{except we replace} \\ \mathbf{D}_{\ell_{BP}} \ \text{with} \\ \mathbf{D}_{\ell_{BP}} + \mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f} \ \text{to the term} \ [\mathbf{k}^{\!\top} \mathbf{f} \mathbf{D}_{\ell_{BP}} + \mathbf{W}_{end} \mathbf{R}_{end}]_2.$

That is, we have:

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{0}[2] &= \begin{pmatrix} [(\mathbf{d}_{0} + \boxed{\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^{*}}}) \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}} \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \{[\mathbf{d}_{j} \mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2}\}_{j \in [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}], \sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}} \mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_{2} \end{pmatrix} \\ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i}[2] &= \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}_{0} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}} \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \{[\mathbf{d}_{i} + \boxed{\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^{*}}}] \mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{i-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_{i}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{i}]_{2}\}_{j \neq i,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \{[\mathbf{d}_{j} \mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2}\}_{j \neq i,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}} \mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{i}]_{2}\}_{j \neq i,\sigma \in \Sigma} \end{pmatrix} \\ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i-1,i}[2] &= \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}_{i} \mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{i-1} + \boxed{\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^{*}}} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_{i}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{i}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \{[\mathbf{d}_{j} \mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2}\}_{j \neq i,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}} \mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_{2} \end{pmatrix} \end{split}$$

<span id="page-37-0"></span>
$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^*[2] = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}_0 \mathbf{u}^\mathsf{T} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}]_2, [\mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}]_2 \\ \big\{ [\mathbf{d}_j \mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_j]_2, [\mathbf{R}_j]_2 \big\}_{j \in [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}], \sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} + \underline{\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}}] - \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}} \mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2 \end{pmatrix}.$$

The definition for keys for NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> follows the spirit of those for NFA<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> in Section 4.3.

**Game sequence.** We prove Theorem 3 via a series of games summarized in Fig 9:

- G<sub>0</sub>: Identical to the real game.
- $G_1$ : Identical to  $G_0$  except that the challenge ciphertext is  $ct^*_{r^*}$ .
- −  $G_{2.i.0}$ ,  $i \in [\ell_{BP}]$ : In this game, the challenge ciphertext is  $ct_{r^*}^*$  and the secret key is  $sk_{\Gamma}^{i-1}$ .
- $G_{2.i.1}$ ,  $i \in [\ell_{BP}]$ : Identical to  $G_{2.i.0}$  except that the secret key is  $sk_{\Gamma}^{i-1,i}$ .
- $G_{2.i.2}$ ,  $i \in [\ell_{BP}]$ : Identical to  $G_{2.i.1}$  except that the secret key is  $sk_{\Gamma}^{\tilde{i}}$ .
- $G_3$ : Identical to  $G_{2.\ell_{RP},2}$  except that the secret key is  $sk_{\Gamma}^*$ .

Here we have  $G_{2.1.0} = G_1$  and  $G_{2.i.0} = G_{2.i-1.2}$  for  $i \in [2, \ell_{BP}]$ . We note that the game sequence is quite similar to that in Section 4.3: the games listed above roughly correspond to  $G_0$ ,  $G_1$ ,  $G_{2.i.0}$ ,  $G_{2.i.1}$ ,  $G_{2.i.3}$  and  $G_3$  there, respectively, and we only change the ciphertext distribution once for all. Furthermore, we will borrow the proof technique from Section 4 to show the indistinguishability of each pair of adjacent games. The distinction is that we crucially use the property of  $\mathbf{f}_{0,x^*},\ldots,\mathbf{f}_{\ell_{BP},x^*}$  defined in (39), which will be captured by the following lemma.

**Useful Lemma.** We describe the lemma which is analogous to Lemma 5.

<span id="page-37-1"></span>**Lemma 24** (Property of  $\{\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}\}_{i\in[0,\ell_{\mathbf{BP}}]}$ ). For any  $\Gamma=(Q,\ell_{BP},\ell,\Sigma,\{\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma}\}_{j\in[\ell_{BP}],\sigma\in\Sigma},\rho,\mathbf{u},\mathbf{f})$  and  $x^*\in\Sigma^\ell$ , we have:

- 1.  $\Gamma(x^*) = 0 \iff \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}\mathbf{u}^\top = 0 \mod p$ ;
- 2.  $\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} = \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{M}_{i,x^*_{\rho(i)}} \mod p \ for \ all \ i \in [\ell_{BP}];$
- 3.  $\mathbf{f}_{\ell_{RP},\chi^*} = \mathbf{f}$

*Proof.* The lemma directly follows from the definitions of NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> in Section 6.1 and  $\mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}, \dots, \mathbf{f}_{\ell_{\mathrm{RP}},x^*}$  in (39).

**Initializing & Finalizing.** It is standard to prove that  $G_0 \approx_c G_1$  and  $\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, G_3 \rangle = 1] = 1/2$ . (See Appendix G.2 for details.) We prove the following lemma stating that  $G_1 \approx_c G_{2.1.0}$ , which is analogous to Lemma 6.

<span id="page-37-2"></span>**Lemma 25.** For all A, we have

$$Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_1 \rangle = 1] = Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2,1,0} \rangle = 1]$$

Proof. Roughly, we will prove that

$$\left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{ct}_{\chi^*}^*, \boxed{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}}\right) = \left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{ct}_{\chi^*}^*, \boxed{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^0}\right)$$

where we have

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}[2] &= \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}_0 \mathbf{u}^{\top}] + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}} \mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2, [\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2 \\ \{[\mathbf{d}_j \mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_j]_2, [\mathbf{R}_j]_2\}_{j \in [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}], \sigma \in \Sigma} \end{pmatrix}, \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}} \mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2 \\ \\ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^0[2] &= \begin{pmatrix} [(\mathbf{d}_0 + \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}) \mathbf{u}^{\top} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}} \mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2, [\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2 \\ \{[\mathbf{d}_j \mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_j]_2, [\mathbf{R}_j]_2\}_{j \in [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}], \sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}} \mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2 \end{pmatrix} \end{split}$$

and

$$\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*[2] = \big([s]_1, [s\mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}]_1, \big\{[s\mathbf{w}_{\eta, x_\eta}]_1\big\}_{\eta \in [\ell]}, [s\mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{end}}]_1, [s\alpha]_T \cdot m_\beta\big).$$

<span id="page-38-0"></span>

| Game  | $ct_{x^*}$   |                     |                                                                    | $sk_\Gamma[2]$                                                                                           | Remark                                                                         |                                                                        |                                                                                               |
|-------|--------------|---------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
|       |              |                     | $? \cdot \mathbf{u}^{\top} + \mathbf{w}_{start} \mathbf{r}^{\top}$ | $\mathbf{P} \cdot \mathbf{M}_{i-1,\sigma} + \mathbf{P} + \mathbf{W}_{\rho(i-1),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_{i-1}$ | $? \cdot \mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma} + ? + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_i$ | $\alpha$ <b>f</b> +? + <b>w</b> <sub>end</sub> <b>R</b> <sub>end</sub> | -                                                                                             |
| 0     | $ct_{x^*}$   | $sk_\Gamma$         | $\mathbf{d}_0$                                                     | $\mathbf{d}_{i-1}$ , $-\mathbf{d}_{i-2}$                                                                 | $\mathbf{d}_i, -\mathbf{d}_{i-1}$                                              | $-\mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}}$                                     | Real game                                                                                     |
| 1     | $ct_{x^*}^*$ | $sk_\Gamma$         | $\mathbf{d}_0$                                                     | $\mathbf{d}_{i-1}, -\mathbf{d}_{i-2}$                                                                    | $\mathbf{d}_i, -\mathbf{d}_{i-1}$                                              | $-\mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}}$                                     | SD                                                                                            |
| 2.1.0 | $ct^*_{x^*}$ | $sk_\Gamma^0$       | $\mathbf{d}_0 + \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}$                   | $\mathbf{d}_{i-1}$ , $-\mathbf{d}_{i-2}$                                                                 | $\mathbf{d}_i$ , $-\mathbf{d}_{i-1}$                                           | $-\mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}}$                                     | $\mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}\mathbf{u}^{T} = 0 \bmod p$ (Lemma 24)                                     |
| 2.i.0 | $ct^*_{x^*}$ | $sk_\Gamma^{i-1}$   | $\mathbf{d}_0$                                                     | $\mathbf{d}_{i-1} + \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}$ , $-\mathbf{d}_{i-2}$                             | $\mathbf{d}_i$ , $-\mathbf{d}_{i-1}$                                           | $-\mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}}$                                     | $i \in [2,\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}]$                                                                |
| 2.i.1 | $ct^*_{x^*}$ | $sk_\Gamma^{i-1,i}$ | $\mathbf{d}_0$                                                     | $\mathbf{d}_{i-1}$ , $-\mathbf{d}_{i-2}$                                                                 | $\mathbf{d}_i$ , $-\mathbf{d}_{i-1} + \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}$       | $-\mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}}$                                     | change of variables                                                                           |
| 2.i.2 | $ct^*_{x^*}$ | $sk^i_\Gamma$       | $\mathbf{d}_0$                                                     | $\mathbf{d}_{i-1}$ , $-\mathbf{d}_{i-2}$                                                                 | $\mathbf{d}_{i} + \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}$ , $-\mathbf{d}_{i-1}$       | $-\mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}}$                                     | DDH, $\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} = \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{M}_{i,x_{\rho(i)}} \mod p$ (Lemma 24) |
| 3     | $ct^*_{x^*}$ | $sk^*_\Gamma$       | $\mathbf{d}_0$                                                     | $\mathbf{d}_{i-1}$ , $-\mathbf{d}_{i-2}$                                                                 | $\mathbf{d}_i$ , $-\mathbf{d}_{i-1}$                                           | $-\mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}$           | change of variables, $\mathbf{f}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}},x^*} = \mathbf{f}$ (Lemma 24)            |

Fig. 9. Game sequence for selectively secure ABE for NBP<sup>⊕</sup> $_P$  with  $i \in [\ell_{BP}]$ . We focus on the  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components of  $\mathsf{sk}_\Gamma$  and all terms in the fifth and sixth columns are quantified over  $\sigma \in \Sigma$ . In the **Remark** column, "SD" and "DDH" indicate  $\mathsf{SD}^{G_1}_{\mathbf{A}_1 \to \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{a}_2}$  and  $\mathsf{DDH}^{G_2}_{1,Q}$  assumption, respectively.

This follows from the statement:

$$\underbrace{\{ \boxed{\boldsymbol{d}_0 \boldsymbol{u}^\top} + \boldsymbol{w}_{start} \boldsymbol{r}^\top, \boldsymbol{r}^\top \}}_{\text{sk}_{\Gamma}^{[2]}} = \underbrace{\{ \boxed{(\boldsymbol{d}_0 + \boldsymbol{\Delta} \cdot \boldsymbol{f}_{0,x^*}) \boldsymbol{u}^\top} + \boldsymbol{w}_{start} \boldsymbol{r}^\top, \boldsymbol{r}^\top \}}_{\text{start}} \quad \text{given} \quad \underbrace{\boldsymbol{d}_0, \boldsymbol{w}_{start}^*}_{\boldsymbol{w}^*} [2]$$

which is implied by the fact  $\Gamma(x^*) = 0 \iff \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*} \mathbf{u}^\top = 0 \mod p$ , see Lemma 24.

**Key switching I.** We will prove that  $G_{2.i.0} \approx_s G_{2.i.1}$  for all  $i \in [\ell_{BP}]$  and  $G_{2.\ell_{BP}.2} \approx_s G_3$ . The proofs of them are similar. We begin with the following lemma stating that  $G_{2.1.0} \approx_s G_{2.1.1}$ , which is analogous to Lemma 7, and sketch the proofs for remaining statements.

<span id="page-39-0"></span>**Lemma 26.** For all A, we have

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.1.0} \rangle = 1] \approx \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.1.1} \rangle = 1].$$

*Proof.* Roughly, we will prove that

$$\left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*, \overline{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^0}\right) \approx_{\mathit{S}} \left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*, \overline{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{0,1}}\right)$$

By Lemma 4, this means that

$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{0}[2] = \begin{pmatrix} \begin{bmatrix} [\mathbf{d}_{0} + \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^{*}}] \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}} \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \{ [\mathbf{d}_{1} \mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}] - \mathbf{d}_{0} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2} \}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \{ [\mathbf{d}_{j} \mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2} \}_{j \neq 1,\sigma \in \Sigma} \end{pmatrix} \approx_{s} \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}_{0} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}} \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \{ [\mathbf{d}_{1} \mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}] - \mathbf{d}_{0} + \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^{*}} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2} \}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \{ [\mathbf{d}_{j} \mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2} \}_{j \neq 1,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}} \mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_{2} \end{pmatrix} = \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{0,1}[2]$$

given

$$\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*[2] = \big([s]_1, [s\mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}]_1, \big\{[s\mathbf{w}_{\eta, x_\eta}]_1\big\}_{\eta \in [\ell]}, [s\mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{end}}]_1, [s\alpha]_T \cdot m_\beta\big).$$

This immediately follows from change of variables  $\mathbf{d}_0 \mapsto \mathbf{d}_0 - \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}$ . Here we use the fact that  $\mathbf{d}_0$  does not appear elsewhere.

Via the same proof idea, we can prove the following two lemmas stating that  $G_{2.i.0} \approx_c G_{2.i.1}$  for all  $i \in [2, \ell_{BP}]$  and  $G_{2.\ell_{BP}.2} \approx_c G_3$ , respectively. The first lemma relies on change of variable  $\mathbf{d}_{i-1} \mapsto \mathbf{d}_{i-1} - \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}$ ; while the second lemma relies on change of variable  $\mathbf{d}_{\ell_{BP}} \mapsto \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{BP}} - \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\ell_{BP},x^*}$  and the fact that  $\mathbf{f}_{\ell_{BP},x^*} = \mathbf{f}$ , see Lemma 24. We give the lemmas and omit the proofs.

**Lemma 27.** For all  $i \in [2, \ell_{BP}]$  and all A, we have

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2,i,0} \rangle = 1] \approx \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2,i,1} \rangle = 1].$$

**Lemma 28.** For all A, we have

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2,\ell_{RP},2} \rangle = 1] \approx \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{3} \rangle = 1].$$

**Key switching II.** We prove the following lemma stating that  $G_{2.i.1} \approx_c G_{2.i.2}$  for all  $i \in [\ell_{BP}]$ , which is analogous to Lemma 17 and relies on the property of  $\mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}, \dots, \mathbf{f}_{\ell_{BP},x^*}$ , see Lemma 24.

<span id="page-39-1"></span>**Lemma 29.** For all  $i \in [\ell_{BP}]$  and all A, there exists  $\mathcal{B}$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}) \approx \mathsf{Time}(A)$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.i.1} \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.i.2} \rangle = 1] \leq O(|\Sigma|) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathrm{DDH}_{1,Q}^{G_2}}(\lambda).$$

Overview. Roughly, we are proving

$$\left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*, \left\lceil \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i-1,i} \right\rceil \right) \approx_{\mathit{c}} \left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*, \left\lceil \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i} \right\rceil \right)$$

More concretely, we want to prove the following statement over  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components:

$$\underbrace{\left\{ \left[ \mathbf{d}_{i} \mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{i-1} + \Delta \cdot \left[ \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^{*}} \right] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_{i} \right]_{2}, \left[ \mathbf{R}_{i} \right]_{2} \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}}_{\mathsf{S} \in \Sigma} \approx_{c} \underbrace{\left\{ \left[ \mathbf{d}_{i} \mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{i-1} + \Delta \cdot \left[ \mathbf{f}_{i,x^{*}} \mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma} \right] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_{i} \right]_{2}, \left[ \mathbf{R}_{i} \right]_{2} \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}}_{\mathsf{S} \in \Sigma}$$

given  $\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),x_{\rho(i)}^*}$  leaked by  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*[2]$  and  $\mathbf{d}_i,\mathbf{d}_{i-1}$  appeared in other subkeys. Then,

- we handle terms with  $\sigma \neq x_{\rho(i)}^*$  using  $DDH_{1,Q}^{G_2}$  assumption w.r.t.  $\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}$ ; this relies on the fact that  $\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}$  with  $\sigma \neq x_{\rho(i)}^*$  are not leaked;
- we handle the remaining term, i.e., one with  $\sigma = x_{\rho(i)}^*$ , by the fact that  $\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} = \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{M}_{i,x_{\rho(i)}^*} \mod p$ , see Lemma 24; note that we cannot use  $\mathrm{DDH}_{1,Q}^{G_2}$  assumption for this case since  $\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),x_{\rho(i)}^*}$  is leaked via  $\mathrm{ct}_{x^*}^*$  [2].

*Proof.* By Lemma 4, it suffices to prove the lemma over  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components which roughly means:

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i-1,i}[2] \; &= \; \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}_0\mathbf{u}^\top + \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}\mathbf{r}^\top]_2, [\mathbf{r}^\top]_2 \\ \big\{ [\mathbf{d}_i\mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{i-1} + \boxed{\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_i]_2, [\mathbf{R}_i]_2 \big\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \big\{ [\mathbf{d}_j\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_j]_2, [\mathbf{R}_j]_2 \big\}_{j \neq i,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2 \end{pmatrix} \\ \approx_c \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}_0\mathbf{u}^\top + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{start}}\mathbf{r}^\top]_2, [\mathbf{r}^\top]_2 \\ \big\{ [\mathbf{d}_i\mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{i-1} + \boxed{\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}\mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma}} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_i]_2, [\mathbf{R}_i]_2 \big\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \big\{ [\mathbf{d}_j\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_j]_2, [\mathbf{R}_j]_2 \big\}_{j \neq i,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \big[ \alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2 \end{pmatrix} = \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^i[2] \end{split}$$

in the presence of

$$\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*[2] = \big([s]_1, [s\mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}]_1, \big\{[s\mathbf{w}_{\eta, x_\eta}]_1\big\}_{\eta \in [\ell]}, [s\mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{end}}]_1, [s\alpha]_T \cdot m_\beta\big).$$

One can sample basis  $\mathbf{A}_1$ ,  $\mathbf{a}_2$ ,  $\mathbf{A}_1^{\parallel}$ ,  $\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel}$  and trivially simulate mpk,  $\operatorname{ct}_{x^*}^*$  and secret key using terms given out above. Furthermore, we prove this using the following statement implied by  $\operatorname{DDH}_{1,O}^{G_2}$  assumption: for all  $\Delta \in \mathbb{Z}_p$ , we have

$$\left\{ [\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}\mathbf{B}]_2, [\mathbf{B}]_2, [\Delta \cdot \boxed{\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_i]_2, [\mathbf{R}_i]_2 \right\}_{\sigma \neq x^*_{\rho(i)}} \approx_c \left\{ [\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}\mathbf{B}]_2, [\mathbf{B}]_2, [\Delta \cdot \boxed{\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}\mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma}} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_i]_2, [\mathbf{R}_i]_2 \right\}_{\sigma \neq x^*_{\rho(i)}}$$

 $\text{where } \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1\times k}, \mathbf{B} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k} \text{ and } \mathbf{R}_i \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times Q}. \text{ On input } \left\{ [\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}\mathbf{B}]_2, [\mathbf{B}]_2, [\mathbf{E}_\sigma]_2, [\mathbf{R}_i]_2 \right\}_{\sigma \neq x_{\rho(i)}^*} \text{ where } \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1\times k}, \mathbf{B} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times R} \text{ and } \mathbf{R}_i \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times Q}.$ 

$$\mathbf{t}_{\sigma} = \Delta \cdot \boxed{\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_i \text{ or } \mathbf{t}_{\sigma} = \Delta \cdot \boxed{\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma}} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_i,$$

we sample  $\alpha \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),x_{\rho(i)}^*}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\text{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  and  $\mathbf{w}_{\eta,\sigma} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  for all  $\eta \neq \rho(i)$ ,  $\sigma \in \Sigma$  and proceed as follows:

(Simulating the ciphertext) On input  $(m_0, m_1)$ , we sample  $s \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and simulate  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*[2]$  using the knowledge of  $\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),x_{\rho(i)}^*}$  and  $\{\mathbf{w}_{\eta,x_{\eta}^*}\}_{\eta \neq \rho(i)}$ . Here we use the fact that the ciphertext does not involve  $\{\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}\}_{\sigma \neq x_{\rho(i)}^*}$ .

(Simulating the secret key) On input  $\Gamma$ , we want to simulate secret key for  $\Gamma$  in the following form:

$$\begin{cases} [\mathbf{d}_{0}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \left\{ [\mathbf{d}_{i}\mathbf{M}_{i,x_{\rho(i)}^{*}} - \mathbf{d}_{i-1} + \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^{*}} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),x_{\rho(i)}^{*}}\mathbf{R}_{i}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{i}]_{2} \right\} \\ \left\{ [\mathbf{d}_{i}\mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{i-1} + \mathbf{t}_{\sigma}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{i}]_{2} \right\}_{\sigma \neq x_{\rho(i)}^{*}} \\ \left\{ [\mathbf{d}_{j}\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2} \right\}_{j \neq i,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_{2} \end{cases}$$

Observe that,

- when  $\mathbf{t}_{\sigma} = \Delta \cdot |\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}| + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_i$ , the distribution is identical to  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i-1,i}[2]$ ;
- when  $\mathbf{t}_{\sigma} = \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_i$ , the distribution is identical to  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^i[2]$  since  $\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} = \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{M}_{i,x^*_{\rho(i)}} \bmod p$ , see Lemma 24.

We sample  $\mathbf{d}_0, \dots, \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{RP}}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times Q}$  and simulate the key as follows:

- We simulate the terms in the second row using  $[\mathbf{R}_i]_2$  and  $\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),x_{\alpha(i)}^*}$ ;
- We simulate the terms in the third row using  $[\mathbf{t}_{\sigma}]_2$  and  $[\mathbf{R}_i]_2$ ;
- All remaining terms can be simulated using  $\{\mathbf{w}_{\eta,\sigma}\}_{\eta\neq\rho(i),\sigma\in\Sigma}$ ,  $\{[\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}\mathbf{B}]_2\}_{\sigma\neq x^*_{\rho(i)}}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),x^*_{\rho(i)}}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\text{end}}$  and  $[\mathbf{B}]_2$ .

Observe that, when  $\mathbf{t}_{\sigma} = \Delta \cdot \boxed{\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_i$ , the secret key is  $\boxed{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i-1,i}[2]}$  and the simulation is identical to  $\mathsf{G}_{2.i.1}$ ; when  $\mathbf{t}_{\sigma} = \Delta \cdot \boxed{\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma}} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_i$ , the secret key is  $\boxed{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{i}[2]}$  and the simulation is identical to  $\mathsf{G}_{2.i.2}$ . This completes the proof.

## <span id="page-41-0"></span>**6.4** Adaptive Security for $\mathcal{E}_{Q}$ -restricted NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup>

In this subsection, we prove that the scheme in Section 6.2 is adaptively secure for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup>. By Lemma 23, this immediately gives us our compact adaptively secure ABE for branching program. We prove the following theorem for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NBP $^{\oplus p}$  and defer the resultant concrete construction of ABE for branching programs to Appendix H.

<span id="page-41-1"></span>**Theorem 4** (Adaptively secure ABE for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup>). The ABE scheme for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NBP $^{\oplus p}$  in prime-order bilinear groups described in Section 6.2 is adaptively secure (cf. Section 2.1) under the k-Lin assumption with security loss  $O(q \cdot \ell_{BP} \cdot |\Sigma|^2 \cdot Q^2)$ . Here  $\ell_{BP}$  are maximal length of all NBPs in adversary's key queries and q is the number of key queries.

We will prove the theorem using the proof technique for the one-key selective security in Section 6.3 and the piecewise guessing framework [15]. This is analogous to the proof in Section 5. Let  $x^* \in \Sigma^{\ell}$  denote the adaptive challenge. Without loss of generality, we assume  $\ell_{BP} > 1$ .

Game sequence. We prove Theorem 4 via a series of games following the standard dual system method [20]:

- G<sub>0</sub>: Identical to the real game.
- $G_1$ : Identical to  $G_0$  except that the challenge ciphertext is  $ct_{v^*}^*$ .
- −  $G_{2,\kappa}$  for  $\kappa \in [0,q]$ : Identical to  $G_1$  except that the first  $\kappa$  secret keys are  $sk_{\Gamma}^*$ .
- G<sub>3</sub>: Identical to G<sub>2.q</sub> except that the challenge ciphertext is an encryption of a random message.

Here we have  $G_{2.0} = G_1$ . It is standard to prove  $G_0 \approx_c G_1$ ,  $G_{2.q} \approx_c G_3$  and show that adversary in  $G_3$  has no advantage. To prove  $G_{2.\kappa-1} \approx_c G_{2.\kappa}$  for all  $\kappa \in [q]$ , we use the following core lemma.

<span id="page-41-2"></span>**Lemma 30** (Core lemma). For all A, there exists B with  $Time(B) \approx Time(A)$  and

$$\mathsf{Adv}^{^{\mathrm{CORE}}}_{\mathcal{A}}(\lambda) = \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_0 \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_1 \rangle = 1] \leq O(\ell \cdot |\Sigma|^2 \cdot Q^2) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}^{k\text{-Lin}}_{\mathcal{B}}(\lambda)$$

where, for all  $b \in \{0,1\}$ , we define:

$$\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_b \rangle := \left\{ b' \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathsf{OEnc}(\cdot), \mathsf{OKey}(\cdot)}(\mathsf{aux}) \right\}$$

where

$$\mathsf{aux} = \left( \, [\mathbf{B}, \{\mathbf{w}_{j,\sigma}\mathbf{B}\}_{j \in [\ell], \sigma \in \Sigma}]_2, \alpha, \Delta, \mathbf{w}_{start}, \mathbf{w}_{end} \, \right)$$

with  $\mathbf{w}_{start}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{end}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{j,\sigma} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$ ,  $\mathbf{B} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times k}$ ,  $\Delta \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and the two oracles work as follows:

-  $\mathsf{OEnc}(x^*)$ :  $output\{\mathbf{w}_{\eta,x_n^*}\}_{\eta\in[\ell]}$ ;

-  $\mathsf{OKey}(\Gamma)$ :  $output \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}[2]$  if b = 0;  $output \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^*[2]$   $using \Delta$   $in \mathsf{aux}$  if b = 1;

with the restrictions that (1) A makes only one query to each oracle; (2) queries  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$  satisfy  $\Gamma(x^*) = 0$ .

It is direct to see that the core lemma implies  $G_{2,\kappa-1} \approx_c G_{2,\kappa}$ ; here aux are used to simulate other q-1 keys. (See Appendix G.3 for details.) In the remaining of this section, we will focus on proving the core lemma, which completes the proof of Theorem 4. For this purpose, we employ the piecewise guessing framework along with a series of hybrids, defined by  $H^u$  and h-functions, analogous to Section 6.3. We begin with more auxiliary distributions.

**More auxiliary distributions.** Recall that the query to OKey is  $\mathcal{E}_O$ -restricted. For all  $i \in [\ell_{BP}]$  and  $\mathbf{p} \in \mathcal{E}_O$ , we define:

- $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{p}}^0[2]$  is the same as  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}[2]$  except we replace  $\mathbf{d}_0$  with  $\mathbf{d}_0 + \Delta \cdot \mathbf{p}$  in the term  $[\mathbf{d}_0\mathbf{u}^\mathsf{T} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}\mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}]_2$ ;  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{p}}^i[2]$  is the same as  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}[2]$  except we replace  $\mathbf{d}_i$  with  $\mathbf{d}_i + \Delta \cdot \mathbf{p}$  in the term  $[\mathbf{d}_i\mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma} \mathbf{d}_{i-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_i]_2$  for all  $\sigma \in \Sigma$ ;  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{p}}^{i-1,i}[2]$  is the same as  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}[2]$  except we replace  $-\mathbf{d}_{i-1}$  with  $-\mathbf{d}_{i-1} + \Delta \cdot \mathbf{p}$  in the term  $[\mathbf{d}_i\mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma} \mathbf{d}_{i-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_i]_2$  for

That is, we have:

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{p}}^{0}[2] &= \begin{pmatrix} [(\mathbf{d}_{0} + \boxed{\Delta \cdot \mathbf{p}}) \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}} \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \{[\mathbf{d}_{j} \mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2}\}_{j \in [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}],\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}} \mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_{2} \end{pmatrix} \\ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{p}}^{i}[2] &= \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}_{0} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}} \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \{[\mathbf{d}_{i} + \boxed{\Delta \cdot \mathbf{p}}] \mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{i-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_{i}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{i}]_{2}\}_{j \neq i,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \{[\mathbf{d}_{j} \mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2}\}_{j \neq i,\sigma \in \Sigma} \end{pmatrix} \\ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{p}}^{i-1,i}[2] &= \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}_{0} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}} \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \{[\mathbf{d}_{i} \mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{i-1} + \boxed{\Delta \cdot \mathbf{p}}] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_{i}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{i}]_{2}\}_{j \neq i,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \{[\mathbf{d}_{j} \mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2}\}_{j \neq i,\sigma \in \Sigma} \end{pmatrix} . \\ &= [\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}} \mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}. \end{split}$$

The auxiliary distributions here are analogous to those in Section 6.3 except that we use general **p** in the place of  $\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}$ . Note that this corresponds to the piecewise information we need to guess in the proof.

**Hybrids**  $\{H^u\}_u$  and h-functions. We are ready to define  $\{H^u\}_u$  and h-functions in the adaptive security lemma (Lemma 20).

Defining u and  $H^u$ . For our setting, we require u to determine the forms of key (output by OKey) in a hybrid, this includes the superscript of key and piecewise information p. For this purpose, we define

$$u \in I \times \mathcal{E}_O$$

where

$$I = \{0, 1, \dots, \ell_{BP}, *\} \cup \{(0, 1), (1, 2), \dots, (\ell_{BP} - 1, \ell_{BP})\}$$

is the set of superscripts of auxiliary keys and  $\mathcal{E}_Q$  includes all possibilities of **p**. Again, we allow a special symbol " $\perp$ " at any positions indicating an empty output. Then, for all  $u = (s, \mathbf{p}) \in I \times \mathcal{E}_O$ , we define hybrid  $H^{s,\mathbf{p}}$  to be identical to  $H_0$ (or H<sub>1</sub>) except that

– oracle  $\mathsf{OKey}(\Gamma)$  returns  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathsf{yyy}}^S[2]$  with yyy depending on s or  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}[2]$  when  $s=\bot$ .

*Defining h-functions.* In both  $H_0$  and  $H_1$ , the adversary A adaptively chooses  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$ , therefore we employ a family of functions

$$h_{\mathsf{XXX}}: \mathsf{NBP}^{\oplus_p} \times \Sigma^* \to I \times \mathcal{E}_O$$

with the first input being  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted. Recall that, for  $x^*$  and a  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup>  $\Gamma$  of length  $\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}$ , we can define  $\mathbf{f}_{0,x^*},\ldots,\mathbf{f}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}},x^*}\in\mathcal{E}_Q$  as (39) as in Section 6.3. We define h-functions as below which describes a series of hybrids analogous to that for selective security. We show the corresponding selective game for each function as a remark.

$$\begin{array}{lll} h_0 & : (\Gamma, x^*) \longmapsto (\bot, & \bot & ); & // \, \mathsf{G}_1 \\ h_{1.i.0} : (\Gamma, x^*) \longmapsto (\{i-1\}, & \mathbf{f}_{i-1, x^*} \;); \, \forall \, i \in [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}]; & // \, \mathsf{G}_{2.i.0} \\ h_{1.i.1} : (\Gamma, x^*) \longmapsto (\{i-1, i\}, \, \mathbf{f}_{i-1, x^*} \;); \, \forall \, i \in [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}]; & // \, \mathsf{G}_{2.i.1} \\ h_{1.i.2} : (\Gamma, x^*) \longmapsto (\{i\}, & \mathbf{f}_{i, x^*} \;); \, \forall \, i \in [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}]; & // \, \mathsf{G}_{2.i.2} \\ h_2 & : (\Gamma, x^*) \longmapsto (\{*\}, & \bot \;); & // \, \mathsf{G}_3 \end{array}$$

Note that we have  $h_{1.i.0} = h_{1.i-1.2}$  for all  $i \in [2, \ell_{BP}]$  and  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^*$  is shown in Section 6.3.

Proving the core lemma. As in Section 5.4, we check (1) end-point equivalence and (2) neighbor indistinguishability.

*End-point equivalence.* It is clear that our hybrids  $\{H^u\}_u$  and h-functions satisfy the end-point equivalence. This follows from the fact that  $h_0$  and  $h_2$  are constant functions which indicate the same types of keys as in  $H^0$  and  $H^1$ , respectively. Formally, we give the following lemma.

**Lemma 31** (End-point equivalence). For all  $(\Gamma, x^*) \in I \times \mathcal{E}_O$ , we have

<span id="page-43-0"></span>
$$H^{h_0(\Gamma,x^*)} = H_0$$
 and  $H^{h_2(\Gamma,x^*)} = H_1$ .

*Neighbor indistinguishability.* We first define several pairs of hybrids with  $b \in \{0, 1\}$ :

 $-\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_0^b(u_0,u_1)$  is the same as  $\mathsf{H}^{u_b}$  except that we output 0 whenever

$$(h_0(\Gamma, x^*), h_{1,1,0}(\Gamma, x^*)) \neq (u_0, u_1).$$

 $-\widehat{\mathsf{H}}^b_{1,i,i'}(u_0,u_1)$ , for  $i\in[\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}]$  and  $i'\in[2]$ , is the same as  $\mathsf{H}^{u_b}$  except that we output 0 whenever

$$(h_{1,i,i'-1}(\Gamma, x^*), h_{1,i,i'}(\Gamma, x^*)) \neq (u_0, u_1).$$

-  $\hat{H}_{2}^{b}(u_{0}, u_{1})$  is the same as  $H^{u_{b}}$  except that we output 0 whenever

$$(h_{1,\ell_{\text{RD}},2}(\Gamma, x^*), h_2(\Gamma, x^*)) \neq (u_0, u_1).$$

and claim that each pair of hybrids are indistinguishable for all  $u_0, u_1 \in I \times \mathcal{E}_Q$ . Formally, we have the following lemma. The proof essentially follows those in Section 6.3. (See Appendix G.4 for more details.)

<span id="page-43-1"></span>**Lemma 32** (Neighbor indistinguishability). For all  $xxx \in \{0,2\} \cup \{1.i.i': i \in [\ell_{BP}], i' \in [2]\}$ ,  $u_0, u_1 \in I \times \mathcal{E}_Q$  and all  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists  $\mathcal{B}$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{A})$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^0_{\mathsf{XXX}}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^1_{\mathsf{XXX}}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] \leq O(|\Sigma|^2) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}^{k\text{-Lin}}_{\mathcal{B}}(\lambda).$$

*Summary.* By the adaptive security lemma (Lemma 20), we have that Lemma 31 and Lemma 32 imply the core lemma, Lemma 30, with the following two facts:

- all our h-functions have range of size at most O(Q) since the first output is constant and  $|\mathcal{E}_Q| = Q$ ; that is, we have  $R' = O(\log Q)$ ;
- our proof employs  $O(\ell_{BP})$  *h*-functions; that is we have  $L = O(\ell_{BP})$ .

**Acknowledgments.** We thank Brent Waters for insightful discussions on adaptive security, as well as the anonymous reviewers for constructive feedback on our write-up.
