# **Appendix**

## <span id="page-45-0"></span>A An Example for Back-tracking Attack

We assume an (asymmetric) bilinear group  $\mathbb{G} = (p, G_1, G_2, G_T, e)$  of prime order p and use  $[\cdot]_1, [\cdot]_2, [\cdot]_T$  to denote componentwise exponentiations in respective groups  $G_1, G_2, G_T$  [10]. The natural NFA extension of Waters' ABE for DFA [21] mentioned in Section 1.1 can be formally described as follows:

<span id="page-45-1"></span>
$$\begin{aligned} & \mathsf{msk} = \left( w_{\mathsf{start}}, w_{\mathsf{end}}, z, \{ w_{\sigma} \}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \alpha \right) \\ & \mathsf{mpk} = \left( [w_{\mathsf{start}}]_1, [w_{\mathsf{end}}]_1, [z]_1, \left\{ [w_{\sigma}]_1 \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, [\alpha]_T \right) \\ & \mathsf{ct}_x = \begin{pmatrix} [s_0]_1, [s_0 w_{\mathsf{start}}]_1 \\ \{ [s_j]_1, [s_j - 1z + s_j w_{x_j}]_1 \}_{j \in [\ell]} \\ [s_\ell]_1, [s_\ell w_{\mathsf{end}}]_1, [s_\ell \alpha]_T \cdot m \end{pmatrix} \\ & \mathsf{sk}_\Gamma = \begin{pmatrix} \{ [d_u + w_{\mathsf{start}} r_{\mathsf{start}}, u]_2, [r_{\mathsf{start}}, u]_2 \}_{u \in S} \\ \{ [-d_u + z r_{u,\sigma,v}]_2, [d_v + w_{\sigma} r_{u,\sigma,v}]_2, [r_{u,\sigma,v}]_2 \}_{u \in [Q], \sigma \in \Sigma, v \in \delta(u,\sigma)} \\ \{ [\alpha - d_u + w_{\mathsf{end}} r_{\mathsf{end}}, u]_2, [r_{\mathsf{end}}, u]_2 \}_{u \in F} \end{pmatrix} \end{aligned}$$

where  $\Sigma$  is the alphabet,  $S, F \subseteq [Q]$  are the sets of start states and accept states, respectively, and  $\delta : [Q] \times \Sigma \to 2^{[Q]}$  is the NFA transition function. Clearly, as (2) in Section 1.1, ct<sub>x</sub> and sk<sub>\Gamma</sub> allow us to compute quantities:

<span id="page-45-2"></span>
$$[s_i d_v - s_{i-1} d_u]_T, \ \forall j \in [\ell], u \in [Q], v \in \delta(u, x_i) \subseteq [Q].$$
 (41)

We illustrate the back-tracking attack against (40) by an example. Consider a concrete NFA  $\Gamma$  defined by  $Q = 4, \Sigma = \{0\}, S = \{1\}, F = \{4\} \text{ and } \delta$  describing two nondeterministic transitions:  $1 \stackrel{0}{\rightarrow} \{1,2\}$  and  $3 \stackrel{0}{\rightarrow} \{2,4\}$ , whose key will be

$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma} = \begin{pmatrix} [d_1 + w_{\mathsf{start}} r_0]_2, [r_0]_2 \\ [-d_1 + z r_1]_2, [d_1 + w r_1]_2, [r_1]_2 \\ [-d_1 + z r_2]_2, [d_2 + w r_2]_2, [r_2]_2 \\ [-d_3 + z r_3]_2, [d_2 + w r_3]_2, [r_3]_2 \\ [-d_3 + z r_4]_2, [d_4 + w r_4]_2, [r_4]_2 \\ [\alpha - d_4 + w_{\mathsf{end}} r]_2, [r]_2 \end{pmatrix}$$

and input x being a single 0, whose ciphertext will be

$$\mathsf{ct}_{x} = \begin{pmatrix} [s_{0}]_{1}, [s_{0}w_{\mathsf{start}}]_{1} \\ [s_{1}]_{1}, [s_{0}z + s_{1}w]_{1} \\ [s_{1}]_{1}, [s_{1}w_{\mathsf{end}}]_{1}, [s_{1}\alpha]_{T} \cdot m \end{pmatrix}$$

Clearly, since the NFA  $\Gamma$  does not accept x = 0, the key  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}$  is not supposed to decrypt the ciphertext  $\mathsf{ct}_x$ . However this is not the case for (40). Following (41), we can recover the following quantities:

$$D_0 = [s_0d_1]_T$$
,  $D_1 = [s_1d_2 - s_0d_1]_T$ ,  $D_2 = [s_1d_2 - s_0d_3]_T$ ,  $D_3 = [s_1d_4 - s_0d_3]_T$ ,  $D_4 = [s_1\alpha - s_1d_4]_T$ 

and compute the masking value:

$$[s_1\alpha]_T = D_0 \cdot D_1 \cdot D_2^{-1} \cdot D_3 \cdot D_4.$$

Intuitively, this corresponds to running the NFA normally with transition  $1 \stackrel{0}{\mapsto} 2$ , and back-tracking along the transition  $3 \stackrel{0}{\mapsto} 2$ , which allows us to restart from state 3 and finally reaching the accept state 4 by transition  $3 \stackrel{0}{\mapsto} 4$ .

### <span id="page-46-0"></span>B Basic ABE for NFA $^{\oplus p}$ from $\ell$ -EBDHE assumption

In this section, we describe our basic ABE scheme for NFA<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> from (asymmetric) bilinear group  $\mathbb{G} = (p, G_1, G_2, G_T, e)$  of prime order p. We assume that respective generators for every groups are described in  $\mathbb{G}$  and use  $[\cdot]_1, [\cdot]_2, [\cdot]_T$  to denote component-wise exponentiations in the prime-order groups  $G_1, G_2, G_T$  [10]. The scheme is selectively secure under  $\ell$ -EBDHE assumption (in the asymmetric prime-order bilinear groups). The proof is an extension of Waters' proof for the ABE for DFA in [21] based on the same assumption. We review the  $\ell$ -EBDHE assumption [21] in the asymmetric bilinear group of prime order.

**Assumption 2** ( $\ell$ -**EBDHE assumption**) We say that the  $\ell$ -EBDHE assumption holds if for all PPT adversaries A, the following advantage function is negligible in  $\lambda$ .

<span id="page-46-1"></span>
$$\mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{A}}^{\ell\text{-EBDHE}}(\lambda) := \left| \Pr[\mathcal{A}(\mathbb{G}, [D]_1, [D]_2, [t_0]_T) = 1] - \Pr[\mathcal{A}(\mathbb{G}, [D]_1, [D]_2, [t_1]_T) = 1] \right|$$

where  $\mathbb{G} = (p, G_1, G_2, G_T, e) \leftarrow \mathfrak{G}(1^{\lambda})$  and

$$D = \begin{pmatrix} a, b, ab/d, b/d \\ a^{i}s, a^{i}bs/c_{j} & \forall i \in [0, 2\ell+1] \setminus \{\ell+1\}, j \in [0, \ell+1] \\ a^{i}b/c_{i}, c_{i}, a^{i}d, abc_{i}/d, bc_{i}/d & \forall i \in [0, \ell+1] \\ a^{i}bd/c_{j} & \forall i \in [0, 2\ell+1], j \in [0, \ell+1] \\ a^{i}bc_{j}/c_{i} & \forall i, j \in [0, \ell+1], i \neq j \end{pmatrix} \quad and \quad t_{0} = a^{\ell+1}bs, t_{1} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_{p}$$

with  $a, b, c_0, \ldots, c_\ell, d, s \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_n$ .

**Scheme.** Our basic ABE for NFA $^{\oplus p}$  in the asymmetric bilinear groups is as follows:

- Setup $(1^{\lambda}, \Sigma)$ : Run  $\mathbb{G} = (p, G_1, G_2, G_T, e) \leftarrow \mathcal{G}(1^{\lambda})$ . Sample

$$\alpha$$
,  $w_{\text{start}}$ ,  $w_{\text{end}}$ ,  $z$ ,  $w_{\sigma} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ ,  $\forall \sigma \in \Sigma$ .

Output

$$\begin{aligned} \mathsf{mpk} &= \left( [w_{\mathsf{start}}]_1, [w_{\mathsf{end}}]_1, [z]_1, \left\{ [w_{\sigma}]_1 \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, [\alpha]_T \right) \\ \mathsf{msk} &= \left( w_{\mathsf{start}}, w_{\mathsf{end}}, z, \{w_{\sigma}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \alpha \right). \end{aligned}$$

- Enc(mpk, x, m): Let  $x = (x_1, ..., x_\ell) \in \Sigma^\ell$  and  $m \in G_T$ . Pick  $s_0, s_1, ..., s_\ell \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and output

$$\mathsf{ct}_{x} = \begin{pmatrix} [s_{0}]_{1}, [s_{0} w_{\mathsf{start}}]_{1} \\ \{[s_{j}]_{1}, [s_{j-1}z + s_{j} w_{x_{j}}]_{1}\}_{j \in [\ell]} \\ [s_{\ell}]_{1}, [s_{\ell} w_{\mathsf{end}}]_{1}, [s_{\ell} \alpha]_{T} \cdot m \end{pmatrix}.$$

- KeyGen(mpk, msk,  $\Gamma$ ): Let  $\Gamma = (Q, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_{\sigma}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f})$ . Pick  $\mathbf{d} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times Q}$ ,  $r_{\text{start}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ ,  $\mathbf{r}_{\sigma}$ ,  $\mathbf{r}_{\text{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times Q}$  for all  $\sigma \in \Sigma$  and output

$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma} = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + w_{\mathsf{start}} r_{\mathsf{start}}]_{2}, [r_{\mathsf{start}}]_{2} \\ \{ [-\mathbf{d} + z \mathbf{r}_{\sigma}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + w_{\sigma} \mathbf{r}_{\sigma}]_{2}, [\mathbf{r}_{\sigma}]_{2} \}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \end{pmatrix}.$$
$$[\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d} + w_{\mathsf{end}} \mathbf{r}_{\mathsf{end}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{r}_{\mathsf{end}}]_{2}$$

- Dec(mpk,  $\operatorname{sk}_{\Gamma}$ ,  $\operatorname{ct}_{x}$ ): Parse ciphertext for  $x = (x_{1}, \dots, x_{\ell})$  and key for  $\Gamma = (Q, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_{\sigma}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f})$  as

$$\mathsf{ct}_{x} = \begin{pmatrix} [s_{0}]_{1}, [c_{0}]_{1} \\ \big\{ [s_{j}]_{1}, [c_{j}]_{1} \big\}_{j} \\ [s_{\ell}]_{1}, [c_{\text{end}}]_{1}, C \end{pmatrix} \quad \text{and} \quad \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma} = \begin{pmatrix} [k_{\text{start}}]_{2}, [r_{\text{start}}]_{2} \\ \big\{ [\mathbf{k}_{\sigma,1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{k}_{\sigma,2}]_{2}, [\mathbf{r}_{\sigma}]_{2} \big\}_{\sigma} \\ [\mathbf{k}_{\text{end}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{r}_{\text{end}}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}$$

We define

$$\mathbf{u}_{j,x}^{\top} = \mathbf{M}_{x_j} \cdots \mathbf{M}_{x_1} \mathbf{u}^{\top} \bmod p, \ \forall j \in [\ell]$$

as (11) and proceed as follows:

1. Compute

$$B_0 = e([s_0]_1, [k_{\text{start}}]_2) \cdot e([c_0]_1, [r_{\text{start}}]_2)^{-1};$$

2. For all  $j \in [\ell]$ , compute

$$[\mathbf{b}_j]_T = e([s_{j-1}]_1, [\mathbf{k}_{x_j,1}]_2) \cdot e([s_j]_1, [\mathbf{k}_{x_j,2}]_2) \cdot e([-c_j]_1, [\mathbf{r}_{x_j}]_2)$$
 and  $B_j = [\mathbf{b}_j \mathbf{u}_{j-1,x}^\top]_T$ 

3. Compute

$$[\mathbf{b}_{\mathrm{end}}]_T = e([s_\ell]_1, [\mathbf{k}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2) \cdot e([-c_{\mathrm{end}}]_1, [\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2)$$
 and  $B_{\mathrm{end}} = [\mathbf{b}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{u}_{\ell, x}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T$ 

4. Compute

$$B_{\text{all}} = B_0 \cdot \prod_{j=1}^{\ell} B_j \cdot B_{\text{end}}$$
 and  $B = B_{\text{all}}^{(\mathbf{fu}_{\ell,x}^{\mathsf{T}})^{-1}}$ 

and output the message  $m' \leftarrow C \cdot B^{-1}$ .

The correctness is direct.

**Selective security.** We prove the following theorem.

**Theorem 5.** The above ABE scheme for NFA<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> in the asymmetric bilinear groups of prime order p is selectively secure under the  $\ell$ -EBDHE assumption (cf. Assumption 2). Here  $\ell$  is the length of the challenge input  $x^*$ .

*Proof.* Let  $x^*$  be the selective challenge input of length  $\ell$ , we use  $\ell$ -EBDHE assumption. For convenience, we artificially set  $x_0^* = x_{\ell+1}^* = \bot \notin \Sigma$ . On input  $(\mathbb{G}, [D]_1, [D]_2, [t]_T)$  where either  $t = a^{\ell+1}bs$  or  $t \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ , the reduction works as follows:

(Simulating mpk) We sample  $\tilde{w}_{\text{start}}$ ,  $\tilde{w}_{\text{end}}$ ,  $\tilde{z}$ ,  $\tilde{w}_{\sigma} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  for all  $\sigma \in \Sigma$  and implicitly set

$$\begin{split} \alpha &= ab, \quad w_{\text{start}} = \tilde{w}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} \, b/c_{\ell+1-i}, \quad w_{\text{end}} = \tilde{w}_{\text{end}} - \sum_{i \in [0,\ell-1]} a^{\ell+1-i} \, b/c_{\ell+1-i} \\ z &= \tilde{z} + ab/d, \quad w_{\sigma} = \tilde{w}_{\sigma} - b/d - \sum_{i \in [0,\ell+1], \sigma \neq x_i^*} a^{\ell+1-i} \, b/c_{\ell+1-i}, \, \forall \sigma \in \Sigma \end{split}$$

Then terms in mpk can be simulated using  $[a, b, ab/d, b/d, \{a^ib/c_i\}_{i \in [0, \ell+1]}]_1$  provided in  $[D]_1$ .

(Simulating challenge ciphertext) On input  $(m_0, m_1)$ , we sample  $\tilde{s}_0, \dots, \tilde{s}_\ell \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p, \beta \leftarrow \{0, 1\}$  and implicitly set

$$s_i = \tilde{s}_\ell + a^i s, \forall i \in [0, \ell]$$

and want to simulate a challenge ciphertext in the following form

$$\begin{pmatrix}
[s_0]_1, [s_0 w_{\text{start}}]_1 \\
\{[s_i]_1, [s_{i-1}z + s_i w_{x_i}]_1\}_{i \in [\ell]} \\
[s_\ell]_1, [s_\ell w_{\text{end}}]_1, [t]_T \cdot e([a]_1, [b]_2)^{\tilde{s}_\ell} \cdot m_\beta
\end{pmatrix}$$

Observe that, when  $t = a^{\ell+1}bs$ , the ciphertext is identical to the real one; when  $t \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ , the ciphertext perfectly hides  $\beta$ . We proceed to simulate each term in the challenge ciphertext as below:

- We can simulate  $[s_i]_1 = [\tilde{s}_i]_1 \cdot [a^i s]_1$  for all  $i \in [0, \ell]$  using  $\{[a^i s]_1\}_{i \in [0, \ell]}$  from  $[D]_1$ .
- We can simulate  $[s_0 w_{\text{start}}]_1$  where

$$s_0 w_{\text{start}} = (\tilde{s}_0 + s) \cdot \left( \tilde{w}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i} \right),$$

using  $[s, \{a^ib/c_i, a^ibs/c_i\}_{i \in [\ell]}]_1$  in  $[D]_1$ .

- We can simulate  $[s_{\ell} w_{\text{end}}]_1$  where

$$s_{\ell} w_{\text{end}} = (\tilde{s} + a^{\ell} s) \cdot \left( \tilde{w}_{\text{end}} - \sum_{i \in [0, \ell-1]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i} \right)$$

using  $[a^{\ell}s, \{a^{i}b/c_{i}, a^{\ell+i}bs/c_{i}\}_{i \in [2, \ell+1]}]_{1}$  in  $[D]_{1}$ .

– For all  $j \in [\ell]$ , we can simulate  $[s_{j-1}z + s_j w_{x_i^*}]_1$  where

$$s_{j-1}z + s_j w_{x_j^*} = (\tilde{s}_{j-1} + a^{j-1}s) \cdot (\tilde{z} + ab/d) + (\tilde{s}_j + a^j s) \cdot \left(\tilde{w}_\sigma - b/d - \sum_{i \in [0,\ell+1], x_i^* \neq x_i^*} a^{\ell+1-i}b/c_{\ell+1-i}\right)$$

using  $[a^{j-1}s, a^js, b/d, \{a^ib/c_i, a^{i+j}bs/c_i\}_{i \in [0,\ell+1], i+j \neq \ell+1}]_1$  from  $[D]_1$ . This follows from  $a^{j-1}s \cdot ab/d - a^js \cdot b/d = 0$ .

(Simulating secret key) On input  $\Gamma$ , we compute  $\{\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}\}_{i\in[0,\ell]}$  as in Section 1.2 (also see (22) in Section 4.3) and artificially set  $\mathbf{f}_{-1,x^*} = \mathbf{f}_{\ell+1,x^*} = \mathbf{0}$ . We sample  $\tilde{\mathbf{d}}, \tilde{\mathbf{r}}_{\sigma}, \tilde{\mathbf{r}}_{\mathrm{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1\times Q}, \tilde{r}_{\mathrm{start}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  for all  $\sigma \in \Sigma$  and implicitly set

$$\begin{split} \mathbf{d} &= \tilde{\mathbf{d}} + \sum_{i \in [0,\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \\ r_{\text{start}} &= \tilde{r}_{\text{start}} + \sum_{i \in [\ell]} c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{u}^{\top} \\ \mathbf{r}_{\sigma} &= \tilde{\mathbf{r}}_{\sigma} + \sum_{i \in [0,\ell]} a^{\ell-i} d \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} + \sum_{i \in [0,\ell+1]} c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot (\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} - \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}), \, \forall \sigma \in \Sigma \\ \mathbf{r}_{\text{end}} &= \tilde{\mathbf{r}}_{\text{end}} + \sum_{i \in [0,\ell-1]} c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \end{split}$$

We proceed to simulate each term in the secret key as below:

- We can simulate  $[r_{\text{start}}]_2$ ,  $[\mathbf{r}_{\sigma}]_2$ ,  $[\mathbf{r}_{\text{end}}]_2$  from  $[\{c_i\}_{i\in[0,\ell+1]}, \{a^id\}_{i\in[0,\ell]}]_2$  provided in  $[D]_2$ .
- We can simulate  $[\mathbf{du}^{\mathsf{T}} + w_{\text{start}} r_{\text{start}}]_2$  where

$$\mathbf{d}\mathbf{u}^{\top} + w_{\text{start}} r_{\text{start}} = \left(\tilde{\mathbf{d}} + \sum_{i \in [0,\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{u}^{\top}\right) + \left(\tilde{w}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} + \sum_{i \in [\ell]} c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{u}^{\top}\right) + \left(\tilde{w}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} + \sum_{i \in [\ell]} c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{u}^{\top}\right) + \left(\tilde{w}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} + \sum_{i \in [\ell]} c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{u}^{\top}\right) + \left(\tilde{w}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} + \sum_{i \in [\ell]} c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{u}^{\top}\right) + \left(\tilde{w}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} + \sum_{i \in [\ell]} c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{u}^{\top}\right) + \left(\tilde{w}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} + \sum_{i \in [\ell]} c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{u}^{\top}\right) + \left(\tilde{w}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{r}_{\text{start$$

using  $[\{c_i\}_{i \in [\ell]}, \{a^ib/c_i\}_{i \in [\ell]}, \{a^ibc_j/c_i\}_{i,j \in [\ell], i \neq j}]_2$  from  $[D]_2$ . This follows from

$$\begin{split} &\sum_{i \in [0,\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot \sum_{i \in [\ell]} c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} \\ &= \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} - \sum_{i \in [\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot \sum_{i \in [\ell]} c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} \\ &= - \sum_{i,j \in [\ell], i \neq j} a^{\ell+1-i} b c_{\ell+1-j} / c_{\ell+1-i} \mathbf{f}_{j,x^*} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} \end{split}$$

in which all terms of the form  $a^i b$  are canceled out. Here the first equality uses the fact that  $\mathbf{f}_{0,x^*} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} = 0 \bmod p$ .

- We can simulate  $[\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d} + w_{\text{end}} \mathbf{r}_{\text{end}}]_2$  where

$$\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d} + w_{\text{end}} \mathbf{r}_{\text{end}} = ab \cdot \mathbf{f} - \left( \tilde{\mathbf{d}} + \sum_{i \in [0,\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i}b \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \right) + \left( \tilde{w}_{\text{end}} - \sum_{i \in [0,\ell-1]} a^{\ell+1-i}b / c_{\ell+1-i} \right) \cdot \left( \tilde{\mathbf{r}}_{\text{end}} + \sum_{i \in [0,\ell-1]} c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \right)$$

using  $[\{c_i\}_{i\in[2,\ell+1]}, \{a^ib/c_i\}_{i\in[2,\ell+1]}, \{a^ibc_j/c_i\}_{i,j\in[2,\ell+1],i\neq j}]_2$  from  $[D]_2$ . This follows form

$$\begin{split} ab \cdot \mathbf{f} - \sum_{i \in [0,\ell-1]} a^{\ell+1-i} b \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} - \sum_{i \in [0,\ell-1]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot \sum_{i \in [0,\ell-1]} c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \\ &= - \sum_{i \in [0,\ell-1]} a^{\ell+1-i} b \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} - \sum_{i \in [0,\ell-1]} a^{\ell+1-i} b / c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot \sum_{i \in [0,\ell-1]} c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \\ &= - \sum_{i,j \in [0,\ell-1], i \neq j} a^{\ell+1-i} b c_{\ell+1-j} / c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \end{split}$$

in which all terms of the form  $a^ib$  are canceled out. Here the first equality utilizes the definition  $\mathbf{f}_{\ell,x^*} = \mathbf{f}$ .

- For all  $\sigma$ , we can simulate  $[-\mathbf{d} + z\mathbf{r}_{\sigma}]_2$  where

$$-\mathbf{d} + z\mathbf{r}_{\sigma} = -\left(\tilde{\mathbf{d}} + \sum_{i \in [0,\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i}b \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}\right) + (\tilde{z} + ab/d) \cdot \left(\tilde{\mathbf{r}}_{\sigma} + \sum_{i \in [0,\ell]} a^{\ell-i}d \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} + \sum_{i \in [0,\ell+1]} c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot (\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} - \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*})\right)$$

using  $[ab/d, \{a^id\}_{i\in[0,\ell]}, \{c_i\}_{i\in[0,\ell+1]}, \{abc_i/d\}_{i\in[0,\ell+1]}]_2$  from  $[D_2]$ . This follows from

$$-\sum_{i\in[0,\ell]}a^{\ell+1-i}b\cdot\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}+ab/d\cdot\sum_{i\in[0,\ell]}a^{\ell-i}d\cdot\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}=-\sum_{i\in[0,\ell]}a^{\ell+1-i}b\cdot\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}+\sum_{i\in[0,\ell]}a^{\ell+1-i}b\cdot\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}=\mathbf{0}.$$

- For all  $\sigma$ , we can simulate  $[\mathbf{dM}_{\sigma} + w_{\sigma}\mathbf{r}_{\sigma}]_2$  where

$$\begin{split} &\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + w_{\sigma}\mathbf{r}_{\sigma} \\ &= \left(\tilde{\mathbf{d}} + \sum_{i \in [0,\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{M}_{\sigma}\right) \\ &\quad + \left(\tilde{w}_{\sigma} - b/d - \sum_{i \in [0,\ell+1], \sigma \neq x_i^*} a^{\ell+1-i} b/c_{\ell+1-i}\right) \cdot \left(\tilde{\mathbf{r}}_{\sigma} + \sum_{i \in [0,\ell]} a^{\ell-i} d \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} + \sum_{i \in [0,\ell+1]} c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot (\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} - \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*})\right) \end{split}$$

using  $[b/d, \{a^id\}_{i \in [0,\ell]}, \{c_i\}_{i \in [0,\ell+1]}, \{bc_i/d\}_{i \in [0,\ell+1]}, \{a^{i+j-1}bd/c_i\}_{i,j \in [\ell+1]}]_2$  and  $\{a^ibc_j/c_i\}_{i,j \in [0,\ell+1], i \neq j}]_2$  from  $[D]_2$ . This follows from

$$\begin{split} &\sum_{i \in [0,\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} - b/d \cdot \sum_{i \in [0,\ell]} a^{\ell-i} d \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} - \sum_{i \in [0,\ell+1],\sigma \neq x^*_i} a^{\ell+1-i} b/c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot \sum_{i \in [0,\ell+1]} c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot (\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} - \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}) \\ &= \sum_{i \in [0,\ell]} a^{\ell+1-i} b \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} - \sum_{i \in [1,\ell+1]} a^{\ell+1-i} b \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} - \sum_{i \in [0,\ell+1],\sigma \neq x^*_i} a^{\ell+1-i} b/c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot \sum_{i \in [0,\ell+1]} c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot (\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} - \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}) \\ &= \sum_{i \in [0,\ell+1],\sigma \neq x^*_i} a^{\ell+1-i} b \cdot (\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} - \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}) - \sum_{i \in [0,\ell+1],\sigma \neq x^*_i} a^{\ell+1-i} b/c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot \sum_{i \in [0,\ell+1]} c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot (\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} - \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}) \\ &= - \sum_{i,j \in [0,\ell+1],i \neq j,\sigma \neq x^*_i} a^{\ell+1-i} b c_{\ell+1-j} / c_{\ell+1-i} \cdot (\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} - \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}) \end{split}$$

in which all terms of the form  $a^ib$  are canceled out. Here the second equality utilizes the fact that  $\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}\mathbf{M}_{x_i^*} = \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} \mod p$ , see Lemma 5.

Observe that, when  $t = a^{\ell+1}bs$ , the simulation is identical to the real game; when  $t \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ , the simulation hides  $\beta$  perfectly and adversary's advantage is 0. This readily proves the lemma.

### <span id="page-49-0"></span>C An Example for Reversing DFA

In this section, we give an example showing the idea of reversing DFA. Consider the regular language  $01\{0,1\}^*$  recognized by DFA  $\Gamma$  with Q = 3,  $\Sigma = \{0,1\}$ ,  $F = \{3\}$  and  $\delta$  describing transitions:

$$1 \stackrel{0}{\mapsto} 2$$
,  $2 \stackrel{1}{\mapsto} 3$ ,  $3 \stackrel{0/1}{\mapsto} 3$ .

On input x = 0100, the sets  $U_i$  of states reachable from start state after reading the first i bits and the sets  $F_i$  of states reachable by back-tracking from accept states after reading the last i bits are as follows:

$$U_0 = \{1\}, U_1 = \{2\}, U_2 = \{3\}, U_3 = \{3\}, U_4 = \{3\}$$

$$F_0 = \{3\}, F_1 = \{3\}, F_2 = \{3\}, F_3 = \{2, 3\}, F_4 = \{1, 3\}$$

Clearly,  $\Gamma$  is *not*  $\mathcal{E}_3$ -restricted; since  $|F_3| > 1$  and  $|F_4| > 1$ , we cannot use elementary row vectors in  $\mathcal{E}_3$  to express them. The reversed DFA  $\Gamma^{\mathsf{T}}$  is defined by the same Q and  $\Sigma$  but with set of start states  $U = \{3\}$ , set of accept states  $F = \{1\}$  and  $\delta$  describing transitions:

$$3 \stackrel{0}{\mapsto} \{3\}, \quad 3 \stackrel{1}{\mapsto} \{2,3\}, \quad 2 \stackrel{0}{\mapsto} \{1\}.$$

Here we have a transition  $u \stackrel{\sigma}{\mapsto} v$  whenever there is a transition  $v \stackrel{\sigma}{\mapsto} u$  in the original DFA. For correctness, we also reverse the input as  $x^{T} = 0010$ ; note that the original x = 0100 will be rejected by  $\Gamma^{T}$ . Then we have

$$U_0 = \{3\}, U_1 = \{3\}, U_2 = \{3\}, U_3 = \{2,3\}, U_4 = \{1,3\}$$

$$F_0 = \{1\}, F_1 = \{2\}, F_2 = \{3\}, F_3 = \{3\}, F_4 = \{3\}$$

One can see that  $\Gamma^{\top}$  is an NFA due to the nondeterministic transition on input bit 1, but now we indeed have  $|F_i| = 1$  for all i = 0, 1, 2, 3, 4 that is desirable for the proof. In fact this holds for all inputs and  $\Gamma^{\top}$  is  $\mathcal{E}_3$ -restricted (see Section 3 for formal proof). Roughly, by reversing DFA, we exchange the role of  $U_i$  and  $F_i$  and the  $\mathcal{E}_3$ -restriction of the reversed DFA immediately comes from the determinism of the original DFA which ensures that  $|U_i| = 1$  (for DFA).

## <span id="page-50-0"></span>D Missing Material from Section 4

### <span id="page-50-2"></span>D.1 Initializing

<span id="page-50-3"></span>In this section, we sketch the proof of  $G_0 \approx_c G_1$ .

**Lemma 33** ( $G_0 \approx_c G_1$ ). For all A, there exists B with  $Time(B) \approx Time(A)$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_0 \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_1 \rangle = 1] \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathrm{SD}_{A_1 - A_1, a_2}}(\lambda).$$

*Proof* (sketch). Roughly, we will prove that

$$(\mathsf{mpk}, \mathsf{ct}_{x^*}), \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}) \approx_c (\mathsf{mpk}, \mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^0, \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}).$$

Recall that, we have  $[\mathbf{s_0}\mathbf{A}_1]_1$  in  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}$  while  $[\mathbf{s_0}\mathbf{A}_1 + s_0\mathbf{a}_2]_1$  in  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^0$ . This relies on  $\mathsf{SD}_{\mathbf{A}_1 \mapsto \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{a}_2}^{G_1}$  assumption which implies

$$([\mathbf{A}_1]_1, [\mathbf{s}_0 \mathbf{A}_1]_1) \approx_c ([\mathbf{A}_1]_1, [\mathbf{s}_0 \mathbf{A}_1 + s_0 \mathbf{a}_2]_1)$$

where  $\mathbf{s}_0 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  and  $s_0 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ . Let  $x^*$  be the selective challenge, the reduction algorithm is sketched as follows:

- we sample  $\mathbf{k}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\text{start}}$ ,  $\mathbf{Z}_0$ ,  $\mathbf{Z}_1$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}$  for all  $\sigma \in \Sigma$  and create (mpk, msk) honestly using [A<sub>1</sub>]<sub>1</sub>.
- − on input key query  $\Gamma$ , we honestly run  $sk_{\Gamma}$  ← KeyGen(mpk, msk,  $\Gamma$ ) using mpk and msk;
- on input challenge query  $(m_0, m_1)$ , we sample  $\beta, \mathbf{s}_1, \mathbf{s}_2, \dots, \mathbf{s}_\ell$  and create the challenge ciphertext for  $x^*$  using the term given out in the statement above.

### <span id="page-50-1"></span>D.2 Selective Security in Many-key Setting

Our proof for selective security in Section 4 can be extended to the many-key setting in a straight-forward way as in [11]. Without loss of generality, we assume that all key queries  $\Gamma_1, \ldots, \Gamma_q$  share the same state space [Q] and alphabet  $\Sigma$ , and extend notations  $\mathbf{d}, \mathbf{R}, \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}$  for  $\Gamma_{\kappa}$  with an additional subscript  $\kappa$ . Then we sketch the changes that are needed to handle the many-key setting:

Game sequence. We employ the game sequence described in Section 4.3 except that

- $-\text{ secret keys in }\mathsf{G}_{2.i.0},\,\mathsf{G}_{2.i.1},\,\mathsf{G}_{2.i.3}\text{ and }\mathsf{G}_{3}\text{ are }\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma_{\kappa}}^{i-1},\,\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma_{\kappa}}^{i-1,i},\,\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma_{\kappa}}^{i}\text{ and }\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma_{\kappa}}^{\ell,*},\,\mathsf{respectively, for }\mathit{all }\kappa\in[q];$
- in each game, *all q* secret keys share the same  $\Delta \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ .

Lemmas and Proofs. Lemma 33,6,7,11,12,14,15,17,18 hold in the many-key setting:

- The proof for Lemma 33,6 can be trivially extended to the many-key setting.
- The proofs for Lemma 7,11,12 can work in the many-key setting due to the fact that
  - $\mathbf{d}_{\kappa}$  are fresh for each  $\kappa \in [q]$ ; this ensures that all changes of variables still hold with multiple keys;
  - $\mathbf{R}_{\kappa}$  are fresh for each  $\kappa \in [q]$ ; this ensures that all DDH-based arguments still hold with multiple keys.
- The proofs for Lemma 14,15 and Lemma 17 can be extended to the many-key setting using (**s**, **W**)-switching lemma and (**z**, **w**)-transition lemma, respectively.
- To prove Lemma 18 with many keys, we argue that *all q* secret keys  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma_1}^{\ell,*},\ldots,\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma_q}^{\ell,*}$  only leak  $\alpha+s_\ell^{-1}\Delta$ ; here we use the fact that  $\mathbf{f}_\kappa=\mathbf{f}_{\ell,x^*,\kappa}$  for all  $\kappa\in[q]$ .

#### <span id="page-51-2"></span>E.2 Missing Proofs in Section 5.2

In this section, we prove  $G_0 \approx_c G_1$ ,  $G_{2.\kappa-1} \approx_c G_{2.\kappa}$  (from the core lemma, Lemma 19),  $G_{2.q} \approx_s G_3$  and show that adversary in  $G_3$  has no advantage. All games are defined in Section 5.2.

**Lemma 34**  $(G_0 \approx_c G_1)$ . For all A, there exists B with  $Time(B) \approx Time(A)$  such that

$$Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_0 \rangle = 1] - Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_1 \rangle = 1] \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathrm{SD}_{A_1 \mapsto A_1, a_2}}(\lambda).$$

*Proof* (sketch). This relies on  $SD_{\mathbf{A}_1 \mapsto \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{a}_2}^{G_1}$  assumption which implies

$$\left( \left[ \mathbf{A}_1 \right]_1, \left[ \left[ \mathbf{s}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{A}_1 \right]_1 \right] \right) \approx_c \left( \left[ \mathbf{A}_1 \right]_1, \left[ \left[ \mathbf{s}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{A}_1 + s_{\text{end}} \mathbf{a}_2 \right]_1 \right)$$

where  $\mathbf{s}_{\text{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  and  $s_{\text{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ . The reduction algorithm is sketched as follows:

- we sample  $\mathbf{k}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{start}$ ,  $\mathbf{Z}_0$ ,  $\mathbf{Z}_1$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1}$ ,  $\mathbf{Z}_{end}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{end}$  for all  $\sigma \in \Sigma$  and create (mpk, msk) honestly using [A<sub>1</sub>]<sub>1</sub>.
- on key query Γ, we honestly run  $sk_Γ$  ← KeyGen(mpk, msk, Γ) using mpk and msk;

- on input challenge query ( $x^*$ ,  $m_0$ ,  $m_1$ ), we sample β,  $\mathbf{s}_0$ ,  $\mathbf{s}_1$ ,  $\mathbf{s}_2$ ,..., $\mathbf{s}_\ell$  and create the challenge ciphertext using the term given out in the statement above. □

**Lemma 35** (**Lemma 19**  $\Rightarrow$   $G_{2,\kappa-1} \approx_c G_{2,\kappa}$ ). For all  $\kappa \in [q]$  and all A, there exists B with  $Time(B) \approx Time(A)$  and

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa-1} \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa} \rangle = 1] \leq \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{CORE}}_{\mathcal{B}}(\lambda)$$

where  $\mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{CORE}}_{\mathfrak{B}}(\lambda)$  is defined in Lemma 19.

*Proof* (*sketch*). On input (mpk,  $aux_1$ ,  $aux_2$ ), we sketch the reduction  $\mathcal{B}$  as follows:

- Forward mpk to  $\mathcal{A}$ .
- On input  $\Gamma$ , proceed as follows:
  - for the first  $\kappa 1$  queries  $\Gamma$ , output  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^*$  which can be created from  $\mathsf{aux}_1$  and  $\mathsf{aux}_2$ ;
  - for the  $\kappa$ 'th query  $\Gamma$ , forward the result of  $\mathsf{OKey}(\Gamma)$  to  $\mathcal{A}$ ;
  - $\circ$  for the remaining query  $\Gamma$ , output  $\mathsf{sk}_\Gamma$  which can be created from  $\mathsf{aux}_1$ ;
- On input  $(x^*, m_0, m_1)$ , pick  $\beta$  ← {0, 1} and forward the result of  $OEnc(x^*, m_\beta)$  to A.

Observe that, if  $\mathsf{OKey}(\Gamma)$  outputs  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}$ , the simulation is identical to  $\mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa-1}$ ; if  $\mathsf{OKey}(\Gamma)$  outputs  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^*$ , the simulation is identical to  $\mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa}$ . This completes the proof.

**Lemma 36** ( $G_{2,q} \approx_s G_3$ ). For all A, we have

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2,a} \rangle = 1] \approx \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_3 \rangle = 1].$$

*Proof.* First, we argue that all q secret keys perfectly hide the  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -component of  $\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}$ , i.e.,  $\alpha = \mathbf{a}_2 \mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}$ . Recall that  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components of all q secret keys are in the following form:

$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^*[2] = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{u}^\top + \mathbf{w}_{start}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^\top]_2, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^\top]_2 \\ \left\{ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_b\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,b}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0,1\}} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\alpha \mathbf{f} + \boxed{s_{end}^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}} + \mathbf{w}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \end{pmatrix}$$

we can simulate all of them using  $\alpha + s_{\mathrm{end}}^{-1} \Delta$  which means all secret keys perfectly hides  $\alpha = \mathbf{a}_2 \mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}$ . Therefore, the unique term involving  $\mathbf{k}$  in  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*$ , i.e.,  $[\mathbf{s}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}} + s_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{a}_2\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T$ , is independently and uniformly distributed and thus statistically hides message  $m_\beta$ .

**Lemma 37** (Advantage in  $G_3$ ). For all A, we have

$$Pr[\langle A, G_3 \rangle = 1] = 1/2.$$

*Proof* (*sketch*). This follows from the fact that the challenge ciphertext is independent of  $\beta$  in  $G_3$ .

### <span id="page-52-0"></span>E.3 Detailed Proofs of Neighbor Indistinguishability in Section 5.4

This section provides the detailed for proving Lemma 22 (in Section 5.4) restated below.

**Lemma 38** (Neighbor indistinguishability). For all  $\times \times \times \in \{0,1,3,4,5\} \cup \{2.i.i': i \in [\ell], i' \in [4]\}$ ,  $u_0,u_1 \in I \times I \times \Sigma \times \mathcal{E}_Q$  and all  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists  $\mathcal{B}$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{A})$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^0_{\mathsf{XXX}}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^1_{\mathsf{XXX}}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] \leq O(|\Sigma|) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}^{k\text{-Lin}}_{\mathcal{B}}(\lambda).$$

All proofs essentially follows those for the selective security of our ABE for NFA<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> in Section 4. We will also employ the notation of  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components described in Section 4.3; in particular, the  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components of  $\mathsf{aux}_1$  and  $\mathsf{aux}_2$  are defined analogously to  $\mathsf{sk}_\Gamma$  and denoted by  $\mathsf{aux}_1[2]$  and  $\mathsf{aux}_2[2]$ , respectively.

**Initializing & Finalizing.** We show that  $\widehat{H}_0^0(u_0, u_1) \approx_c \widehat{H}_0^1(u_0, u_1)$ ,  $\widehat{H}_5^0(u_0, u_1) \approx_c \widehat{H}_5^1(u_0, u_1)$  and  $\widehat{H}_1^0(u_0, u_1) \approx_s \widehat{H}_1^1(u_0, u_1)$  for all  $u_0, u_1$ . The proofs for the former two are similar. We begin with the following lemma stating that  $\widehat{H}_0^0(u_0, u_1) \approx_c \widehat{H}_0^1(u_0, u_1)$  for all  $u_0, u_1$  and sketch the proof for the other one.

<span id="page-53-0"></span>**Lemma 39.** For all  $u_0, u_1 \in I \times I \times \Sigma \times \mathcal{E}_Q$  and all  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists  $\mathcal{B}$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{A})$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_0^0(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_0^1(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] \leq \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{SWITCH}}_{\mathcal{B}}(\lambda).$$

*Overview.* Fix  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$ , we will prove that

$$\left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{aux}_1,\mathsf{aux}_2,\boxed{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*},\mathsf{sk}_\Gamma\right)\approx_{\mathit{c}}\left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{aux}_1,\mathsf{aux}_2,\boxed{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^0},\mathsf{sk}_\Gamma\right)$$

which roughly means that

$$\underbrace{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*}_{[\mathbf{s_0}\mathbf{A}_1]_1} \approx_c \underbrace{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^0}_{\mathbf{s_0}\mathbf{A}_1 + s_0\mathbf{a}_2]_1} \quad \text{given} \quad \underbrace{[\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot s_{\mathrm{end}}^{-1} \Delta + \mathbf{W}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2, [\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2}_{}.$$

This is similar to Lemma 14 stating that  $G_{2.i.1} \approx_c G_{2.i.2}$ ; therefore we prove the lemma analogously but using  $(\mathbf{s}_0, \mathbf{W}_{end})$ -switching lemma instead of  $(\mathbf{s}_i, \mathbf{Z}_{\tau})$ -switching lemma so that we can simulate the challenge ciphertext from the challenge term in the lemma and simulate  $\mathsf{aux}_2$  using the auxiliary terms given out in the lemma.

*Proof.* We prove the lemma for the case

$$u_0 = ( \boxed{\{*\}}, \bot, \bot, \bot), \quad u_1 = ( \boxed{\{0\}}, \bot, \bot, \bot)$$

with all  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$  adaptively chosen by  $\mathcal{A}$ ; the lemma trivially holds in all other cases. Recall that the difference between the two games lies in  $\mathsf{OEnc}(x^*,m)$ : the former returns  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*$  and the latter returns  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^0$ ; oracle  $\mathsf{OKey}(\Gamma)$  always returns  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}$ . We prove the lemma using  $(\mathbf{s}_0,\mathbf{W}_{\mathrm{end}})$ -switching lemma (see Lemma 13). On input

aux, 
$$[\mathbf{c}_0]_1$$
,  $[\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \bar{\Delta} + \mathbf{W}_{end} \mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2$ ,  $[\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2$ 

 $\text{where aux} = ([\mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{a}_2, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}, \mathbf{a}_2 \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}]_1, [\mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{B}]_2) \text{ and } \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(2k+1)\times k}, \mathbf{B} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \mathbf{r} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p \text{ and } \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(2k+1)\times k}, \mathbf{B} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \mathbf{r} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \mathbf{r} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \mathbf{r} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \mathbf{r} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \mathbf{r} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \mathbf{r} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \mathbf{r} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \bar{\Delta}$ 

$$\mathbf{c}_0 = \boxed{\mathbf{s}_0 \mathbf{A}_1}$$
 or  $\mathbf{c}_0 = \boxed{\mathbf{s}_0 \mathbf{A}_1 + s_0 \mathbf{a}_2}$ ,  $\mathbf{s}_0 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^k, s_0 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ 

the reduction works as follows:

(Simulating mpk and  $\mathsf{aux}_1$ ) We sample  $\mathbf{k} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times (2k+1)}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{start}$ ,  $\mathbf{Z}_0$ ,  $\mathbf{Z}_1$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1}$ ,  $\mathbf{Z}_{end} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(2k+1) \times k}$  for all  $\sigma \in \Sigma$ . Then we can trivially simulate mpk with  $[\mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{end}]_1$  and simulate  $\mathsf{aux}_1$  with  $[\mathbf{B}, \mathbf{W}_{end} \mathbf{B}]_2$ .

(**Simulating**  $aux_2$ ) We sample  $s_{end} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and implicitly set

$$\Delta = s_{\rm end}\bar{\Delta}$$
.

Then we can rewrite aux2 as

$$[\boldsymbol{r}^{\top}]_2, [\boldsymbol{W}_{start}\boldsymbol{r}^{\top}]_2, [\boldsymbol{Z}_0\boldsymbol{r}^{\top}]_2, [\boldsymbol{Z}_1\boldsymbol{r}^{\top}]_2, \left\{[\boldsymbol{W}_{\sigma,0}\boldsymbol{r}^{\top}]_2, [\boldsymbol{W}_{\sigma,1}\boldsymbol{r}^{\top}]_2\right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, [\boldsymbol{Z}_{end}\boldsymbol{r}^{\top}]_2, [\boldsymbol{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \bar{\Delta} + \boldsymbol{W}_{end}\boldsymbol{r}^{\top}]_2$$

which can be trivially simulated with  $[\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \bar{\Delta} + \mathbf{W}_{end} \mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2$ ,  $[\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2$  given out in the lemma and  $\mathbf{W}_{start}, \mathbf{Z}_0, \mathbf{Z}_1, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1}, \mathbf{Z}_{end}$ .

(Answering OKey) On input  $\Gamma$ , we return  $sk_{\Gamma}$  which can be generated using  $aux_1$ .

(Answering OEnc) On input  $(x^*, m)$ , we want to create a ciphertext in the following form, which is either  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*$  or  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^0$  depending on  $\mathbf{c}_0$ :

$$\begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{c}_0]_1, [\mathbf{c}_0 \mathbf{W}_{\text{start}}]_1 \\ \{ [\mathbf{c}_j]_1, [\mathbf{c}_{j-1} \mathbf{Z}_{j \text{ mod } 2}]_1 \cdot [\mathbf{c}_j \mathbf{W}_{x_j^*, j \text{ mod } 2}]_1 \}_{j \in [\ell]} \\ [\mathbf{c}_{\text{end}}]_1, [\mathbf{c}_\ell \mathbf{Z}_{\text{end}}]_1 \cdot [[\underline{\mathbf{c}}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}]_1]_1 \cdot [\mathbf{c}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{k}^\top]_T \cdot m \end{pmatrix} \text{ where } \begin{cases} \mathbf{c}_0 \in \{ [\mathbf{s}_0 \mathbf{A}_1], \mathbf{s}_0 \mathbf{A}_1 + s_0 \mathbf{a}_2 \} \\ \mathbf{c}_j = \mathbf{s}_j \mathbf{A}_1 \text{ for all } j \in [\ell] \\ \mathbf{c}_{\text{end}} = \mathbf{s}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{A}_1 + s_{\text{end}} \mathbf{a}_2 \end{pmatrix}$$

Observe that,

- when  $\mathbf{c}_0 = \boxed{\mathbf{s}_0 \mathbf{A}_1}$ , the distribution is identical to  $\boxed{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*}$ ;
- when  $\mathbf{c}_0 = \mathbf{s}_0 \mathbf{A}_1 + s_0 \mathbf{a}_2$ , the distribution is identical to  $\mathsf{ct}_{r^*}^0$

We proceed to create the ciphertext as follows:

- We sample  $\mathbf{s}_1, \dots, \mathbf{s}_\ell, \mathbf{s}_{\text{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$ ,  $s_{\text{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and simulate  $\{[\mathbf{c}_j]_1\}_{j \in [\ell]}$  and  $[\mathbf{c}_{\text{end}}]_1$  using  $[\mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{a}_2]_1$ ; note that  $[\mathbf{c}_0]_1$  is given out in the lemma as the challenge term.
- We rewrite the term in the dashed box as:

$$[\mathbf{c}_{\text{end}}\mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}]_1 = [\mathbf{s}_{\text{end}}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}]_1 \cdot [s_{\text{end}}\mathbf{a}_2\mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}]_1$$

which can be simulated using  $\mathbf{s}_{end}$ ,  $s_{end}$  and  $[\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{W}_{end}, \mathbf{a}_2\mathbf{W}_{end}]_1$ ; here we use the fact that we do not have any terms involving  $[\mathbf{s}_0\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{W}_{end}]_1$  in the ciphertext.

- We simulate all remaining terms using  $\{[\mathbf{c}_j]_1\}_{j\in[0,\ell]}, [\mathbf{c}_{end}]_1$  and  $\mathbf{k}, \mathbf{W}_{start}, \mathbf{Z}_0, \mathbf{Z}_1, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1}, \mathbf{Z}_{end}.$ 

Observe that, when  $\mathbf{c}_0 = \boxed{\mathbf{s}_0 \mathbf{A}_1}$ , oracle  $\mathsf{OEnc}(x^*, m)$  returns  $\boxed{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*}$  and the simulation is identical to  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_0^0(u_0, u_1)$ ; when  $\mathbf{c}_0 = \boxed{\mathbf{s}_0 \mathbf{A}_1 + s_0 \mathbf{a}_2}$ , oracle  $\mathsf{OEnc}(x^*, m)$  returns  $\boxed{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^0}$  and the simulation is identical to  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_0^1(u_0, u_1)$ . This completes the proof.

Via the same proof idea, we can prove the following lemma stating that  $\widehat{H}_5^0(u_0, u_1) \approx_c \widehat{H}_5^1(u_0, u_1)$  for all  $u_0, u_1$ . We only sketch the proof.

**Lemma 40.** For all  $u_0, u_1 \in I \times I \times \Sigma \times \mathcal{E}_Q$  and all  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists  $\mathcal{B}$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{A})$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_5^0(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_5^1(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{SWITCH}}(\lambda).$$

Proof (sketch). We prove the lemma for the case

$$u_0 = ( \boxed{\{\ell\}}, \{*\}, \bot, \bot), \quad u_1 = ( \boxed{\{*\}}, \{*\}, \bot, \bot)$$

with all  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$  adaptively chosen by  $\mathcal{A}$ ; the lemma trivially holds in all other cases. Namely, we will prove that

$$\left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{aux}_1,\mathsf{aux}_2,\boxed{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^\ell},\mathsf{sk}_\Gamma^*\right) \approx_c \left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{aux}_1,\mathsf{aux}_2,\boxed{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*},\mathsf{sk}_\Gamma^*\right)$$

which roughly means that

$$\underbrace{\mathsf{ct}_{\boldsymbol{x}^*}^{\ell}}_{[\mathbf{s}_{\ell}\mathbf{A}_1 + s_{\ell}\mathbf{a}_2]_1} \approx_{c} \underbrace{\mathsf{ct}_{\boldsymbol{x}^*}^*}_{[\mathbf{s}_{\ell}\mathbf{A}_1]_1} \quad \text{given} \quad \underbrace{[\mathbf{a}_{2}^{\parallel} \cdot s_{\text{end}}^{-1} \Delta + \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_{2}, [\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_{2}}_{\text{aux}_{2}, \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{*}}$$

Then the proof is analogous to that for Lemma 39 except that we use  $(\mathbf{s}_{\ell}, \mathbf{W}_{end})$ - instead of  $(\mathbf{s}_{0}, \mathbf{W}_{end})$ -switching lemma and we need  $\mathsf{aux}_{2}$  to answer OKey query; in particular,

- we simulate mpk,  $aux_1$ ,  $aux_2$  as in the proof of Lemma 39;
- we answer  $\mathsf{OKey}(\Gamma)$  by generating  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^*$  using both  $\mathsf{aux}_1$  and  $\mathsf{aux}_2$ .

- we answer  $\mathsf{OEnc}(x^*, m)$  using the challenge term in the lemma analogously; but we rely on the fact that there is no term with  $[\mathbf{s}_{\ell}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{W}_{\mathrm{end}}]_1$ .

We finally prove the lemma stating that  $\widehat{H}_1^0(u_0, u_1) \approx_c \widehat{H}_1^1(u_0, u_1)$  for all  $u_0, u_1$ , which is analogous to Lemma 6.

**Lemma 41.** For all  $u_0$ ,  $u_1 \in I \times I \times \Sigma \times \mathcal{E}_O$  and all A, we have

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_1^0(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] = \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_1^1(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1]$$

*Proof* (sketch). We consider the case that the adversary adaptively chooses  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$  in the hybrids parameterized by

$$u_0 = (\{0\}, \boxed{\bot, \bot, \bot}), \ u_1 = (\{0\}, \boxed{\{0\}, \bot, \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}});$$

the lemma trivially holds in all other cases. This roughly means that

$$\left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{aux}_1,\mathsf{aux}_2,\mathsf{ct}^0_{x^*},\boxed{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}}\right) \approx_c \left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{aux}_1,\mathsf{aux}_2,\mathsf{ct}^0_{x^*},\boxed{\mathsf{sk}^0_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}}}\right)$$

where

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}[2] &= \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{u}^{\top}] + \mathbf{w}_{start}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2} \\ \{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0,1\}} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\alpha\mathbf{f} + \mathbf{w}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}, \\ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{0,x^{*}}}^{0}[2] &= \begin{pmatrix} [(\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{s}_{0}^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^{*}})\mathbf{u}^{\top} + \mathbf{w}_{start}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2} \\ \{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0,1\}} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\alpha\mathbf{f} + \mathbf{w}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix} \end{split}$$

with

$$\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2] = \left([s_0 \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}]_1, [s_0]_1, [s_0 \mathbf{z}_1]_1, [s_{\mathsf{end}} \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{end}}]_1, [s_{\mathsf{end}}]_1, [s_{\mathsf{end}} \alpha]_T \cdot m\right)$$

and

$$\begin{aligned} &\mathsf{aux}_1[2] = \left( [\alpha, \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{start} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{z}_0 \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{z}_1 \mathbf{B}, \{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{B}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{z}_{end} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{end} \mathbf{B}]_2 \right) \\ &\mathsf{aux}_2[2] = \left( [\mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{w}_{start} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{z}_0 \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{z}_1 \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{z}_{end} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, s_{end}^{-1} \Delta + \mathbf{w}_{end} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}]_2 \right). \end{aligned}$$

This immediately follows from the fact  $\Gamma(x^*) = 0 \iff \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*} \mathbf{u}^\top = 0 \mod p$  (see Lemma 5).

**Switching secret keys I.** We show that  $\widehat{H}_{2.i.1}^0(u_0,u_1) \approx_c \widehat{H}_{2.i.1}^1(u_0,u_1)$ ,  $\widehat{H}_3^0(u_0,u_1) \approx_c \widehat{H}_3^1(u_0,u_1)$  for all  $i \in [\ell]$  and all  $u_0,u_1$ . The proofs for them are similar. We begin with the following lemma stating that  $\widehat{H}_{2.1.1}^0(u_0,u_1) \approx_c \widehat{H}_{2.1.1}^1(u_0,u_1)$  for all  $u_0,u_1$ , which is analogous to Lemma 7, and sketch the proofs for remaining statements.

<span id="page-55-0"></span>**Lemma 42.** For all  $u_0, u_1 \in I \times I \times \Sigma \times \mathcal{E}_O$ , there exists  $\mathcal{B}$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{A})$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^0_{2.1.1}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^1_{2.1.1}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] \leq O(|\Sigma|) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathrm{DDH}^{G_2}_{1,Q}}_{\mathcal{B}}(\lambda).$$

*Overview.* Fix  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$ , we will prove that

$$\left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{aux}_1,\mathsf{aux}_2,\mathsf{ct}^0_{x^*},\boxed{\mathsf{sk}^0_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}}}\right) \approx_{\mathit{c}} \left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{aux}_1,\mathsf{aux}_2,\mathsf{ct}^0_{x^*},\boxed{\mathsf{sk}^{0,1}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}}}\right).$$

By Lemma 4, we focus on the  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components and prove:

$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}}^{0}[2] = \begin{pmatrix} [(\boxed{\mathbf{d} + s_{0}^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}}]\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{start}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \{[\boxed{-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{0}\mathbf{R}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{0}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\alpha\mathbf{f} + \mathbf{w}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix} \approx c \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{start}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \{[-\mathbf{d} + s_{0}^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^{*}} + \mathbf{z}_{1}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{0}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\alpha\mathbf{f} + \mathbf{w}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix} = \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{0,x^{*}}}^{0,1}$$

given

$$\operatorname{ct}_{r^*}^0[2] = ([s_0 \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}]_1, [s_0]_1, [s_0 \mathbf{z}_1]_1, [s_{\text{end}} \mathbf{w}_{\text{end}}]_1, [s_{\text{end}}]_1, [s_{\text{end}} \alpha]_T \cdot m)$$

and

$$\begin{aligned} &\mathsf{aux}_1[2] = \left( [\alpha, \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{start} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{z}_0 \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{z}_1 \mathbf{B}, \{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{B}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{z}_{end} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{end} \mathbf{B}]_2 \right) \\ &\mathsf{aux}_2[2] = \left( [\mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{w}_{start} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{z}_0 \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{z}_1 \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{z}_{end} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, s_{end}^{-1} \Delta + \mathbf{w}_{end} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}]_2 \right). \end{aligned}$$

Clearly, change of variables  $\mathbf{d} \mapsto \mathbf{d} - s_0^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}$  is at the core of the above statement, which ensures that, for all  $s_0$  and  $\Delta$ , we have

$$\underbrace{ \left\{ (\mathbf{d} + s_0^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}) \mathbf{u}^\top + \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}} \mathbf{R} \mathbf{u}^\top, -\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_1 \mathbf{R}, \mathbf{R} \right\}}_{\text{s} \approx s} \underbrace{ \left\{ \mathbf{d} \, \mathbf{u}^\top + \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}} \mathbf{R} \mathbf{u}^\top, -\mathbf{d} + s_0^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*} + \mathbf{z}_1 \mathbf{R}, \mathbf{R} \right\}}_{\text{c} \text{given}} \underbrace{ \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_1} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_2} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_2} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_2} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_2} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_2} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_2} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_2} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_2} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_2} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]}_{\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{z}_2} \underbrace{ \mathbf{ct}_$$

As in the proof of Lemma 7, we need to hide all irrelevant  $\mathbf{d}$ 's via  $\mathrm{DDH}_{1,Q}^{G_2}$  assumption before and after the change of variable via  $\mathrm{DDH}_{1,Q}^{G_2}$  assumption. Note that, besides  $\mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{start}}$  and  $\mathbf{z}_1$ ,  $\mathrm{ct}_{x^*}^0[2]$  also leaks  $\mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}}$ , which means we cannot apply  $\mathrm{DDH}_{1,Q}^{G_2}$  assumption w.r.t.  $\mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}}$ ; however the term  $[\alpha \mathbf{f} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}} \mathbf{R}]_2$  does not contain  $\mathbf{d}$  either and will not interfere in the change of variable with respect to  $\mathbf{d}$ .

*Auxiliary hybrids*. Formally, fix  $u_0 = (\{0\}, \{0\}, \bot, \mathbf{p})$  and  $u_1 = (\{0\}, \{0, 1\}, \bot, \mathbf{p})$ , we define two more auxiliary hybrids:

–  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}^0_{2.1.1.a}(u_0,u_1)$  is the same as  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}^0_{2.1.1}(u_0,u_1)$  except that  $\mathsf{OKey}(\Gamma)$  outputs

$$\begin{pmatrix} [(\mathbf{d} + s_0^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{p}) \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}} \mathbf{R} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_2, [\mathbf{R} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_2 \\ \{ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_1 \mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{0}] \cdot \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \{ [\mathbf{0}] + \mathbf{z}_0 \mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{0}] \cdot \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\mathbf{0}] + \mathbf{z}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{R}]_2, [\alpha \mathbf{f} + \mathbf{w}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \end{pmatrix}$$

–  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}^1_{2.1.1.a}(u_0,u_1)$  is the same as  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}^1_{2.1.1}(u_0,u_1)$  except that  $\mathsf{OKey}(\Gamma)$  outputs

$$\begin{cases} [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{u}^{\top} + \mathbf{w}_{start}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2} \\ \left\{ [-\mathbf{d} + s_{0}^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{p} + \mathbf{z}_{1}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{0}] \cdot \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \left\{ [\mathbf{0}] + \mathbf{z}_{0}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{0}] \cdot \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\mathbf{0}] + \mathbf{z}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\alpha \mathbf{f} + \mathbf{w}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{cases}$$

Then we prove that:

<span id="page-56-0"></span>
$$\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_{2.1.1}^{0}(u_0,u_1) \approx_c \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_{2.1.1.a}^{0}(u_0,u_1) \approx_s \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_{2.1.1.a}^{1}(u_0,u_1) \approx_c \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_{2.1.1}^{1}(u_0,u_1). \tag{49}$$

which is summarized in Fig 10 with fixed  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$ .

<span id="page-56-1"></span>Lemmas. We describe and prove the following lemmas which imply Lemma 42 by (49).

**Lemma 43.** For all A, there exists B with  $Time(B) \approx Time(A)$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^0_{2.1.1}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^0_{2.1.1.a}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] \leq O(|\Sigma|) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathrm{DDH}_{1,Q}^{G_2}}(\lambda).$$

*Proof.* We consider the case that the adversary adaptively chooses  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$  in the hybrids parameterized by

$$u_0 = (\{0\}, \{0\}, \bot, \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}), \ u_1 = (\{0\}, \{0, 1\}, \bot, \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*});$$

| Game                        | $? \cdot \mathbf{u}^{\top} + \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}} \mathbf{R} \mathbf{u}^{\top}$ | $? + \mathbf{z}_1 \mathbf{R}$                    | $? \cdot \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{R}$ | $\mathbf{?} + \mathbf{z}_0 \mathbf{R}$ | $? \cdot \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{R}$ | $? + \mathbf{z}_{end}\mathbf{R}$ | Remark                                                             |
|-----------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------|

| $\widehat{H}^{0}_{2.1.1.a}$ | $\mathbf{d} + s_0^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{p}$                                      | -d                                               | 0                                                                | 0                                      | 0                                                                | 0                                | DDH                                                                |
| $\widehat{H}^{1}_{2.1.1.a}$ | , d                                                                                  | $-\mathbf{d} + s_0^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{p}$ | 0                                                                | 0                                      | 0                                                                | 0                                | $\mathbf{d} \mapsto \mathbf{d} - s_0^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{p}$ |
| $\widehat{H}^1_{2.1.1}$     | d                                                                                    | $-\mathbf{d} + s_0^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{p}$ | d                                                                | $-\mathbf{d}$                          | d                                                                | $-\mathbf{d}$                    | DDH, $sk_{\Gamma, \boldsymbol{p}}^{0,1}[2]$                        |

<span id="page-57-0"></span>Fig. 10. Game sequence for  $\widehat{H}^0_{2,1,1}(u_0,u_1) \approx_c \widehat{H}^1_{2,1,1}(u_0,u_1)$ . In the table, we only show changes of secret key and focus on its  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components; all secret key elements in the fourth and sixth column are quantified over  $\sigma \in \Sigma$ . In the **Remark** column, "DDH" indicates DDH $_{1,O}^{G_2}$  assumption.

the lemma trivially holds in all other cases. By Lemma 4, it suffices to prove the lemma over  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components which roughly means:

$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}}^{0}[2] = \begin{pmatrix} [(\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{s}_{0}^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*})\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{start}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{1}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}] \cdot \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \{[-\mathbf{d}] + \mathbf{z}_{0}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}] \cdot \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [-\mathbf{d}] + \mathbf{z}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\alpha\mathbf{f} + \mathbf{w}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix} \approx c \begin{pmatrix} [(\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{s}_{0}^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^{*}})\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{w}_{start}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{1}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{0}] \cdot \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \{[\mathbf{0} + \mathbf{z}_{0}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{0}] \cdot \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\mathbf{0} + \mathbf{z}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\alpha\mathbf{f} + \mathbf{w}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}$$

in the presence of

$$\operatorname{ct}_{x^*}^0[2] = ([s_0 \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}]_1, [s_0]_1, [s_0 \mathbf{z}_1]_1, [s_{\text{end}} \mathbf{w}_{\text{end}}]_1, [s_{\text{end}}]_1, [s_{\text{end}} \alpha]_T \cdot m)$$

and

$$\begin{aligned} &\mathsf{aux}_1[2] = \left( [\alpha, \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{start} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{z}_0 \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{z}_1 \mathbf{B}, \{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{B}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{z}_{end} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{end} \mathbf{B}]_2 \right) \\ &\mathsf{aux}_2[2] = \left( [\mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{w}_{start} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{z}_0 \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{z}_1 \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{z}_{end} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, s_{end}^{-1} \Delta + \mathbf{w}_{end} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}]_2 \right) \end{aligned}$$

One can sample basis  $\mathbf{A}_1$ ,  $\mathbf{a}_2$ ,  $\mathbf{A}_3$ ,  $\mathbf{A}_1^{\parallel}$ ,  $\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel}$ ,  $\mathbf{A}_3^{\parallel}$  and trivially simulate mpk,  $\mathsf{aux}_1$ ,  $\mathsf{aux}_2$ ,  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^0$  and secret key using terms given out above. Furthermore, this follows from  $\mathsf{DDH}_{1,Q}^{G_2}$  assumption w.r.t  $\mathbf{z}_0$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1}$ ,  $\mathbf{z}_{\mathrm{end}}$  with  $\sigma \in \Sigma$  which implies:

$$\left([\mathbf{z}_0\mathbf{R}]_2, \left\{[\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0}\mathbf{R}]_2\right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \left\{[\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1}\mathbf{R}]_2\right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, [\mathbf{z}_{\text{end}}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2\right) \approx_c U\left((G_2^{1 \times Q})^{2|\Sigma| + 2} \times G_2^{k \times Q}\right)$$

given  $\mathsf{aux} = [\mathbf{B}, \mathbf{z}_0 \mathbf{B}, \{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{B}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{z}_{end} \mathbf{B}]_2$  where  $\mathbf{z}_0, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0}, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1}, \mathbf{z}_{end} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  for all  $\sigma \in \Sigma$  and  $\mathbf{R} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times Q}$ . Here we use the fact that  $\mathsf{ct}_{r^*}^0[2]$  does not leak  $\mathbf{z}_0, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1}, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0}, \mathbf{z}_{end}$  with  $\sigma \in \Sigma$ . This completes the proof.

**Lemma 44.** For all A, we have

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^0_{2.1.1.a}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] = \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^1_{2.1.1.a}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1]$$

*Proof.* This immediately follows from the change of variables:  $\mathbf{d} \mapsto \mathbf{d} - s_0^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}$ .

**Lemma 45.** For all A, there exists B with  $Time(B) \approx Time(A)$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^1_{2.1.1.a}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^1_{2.1.1}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] \leq O(|\Sigma|) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathrm{DDH}_{1,Q}^{G_2}}(\lambda).$$

*Proof.* The proof is analogous to that for Lemma 43.

Via the same proof idea, we can prove the following lemmas stating that  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}^0_{2,i,1}(u_0,u_1) \approx_c \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^1_{2,i,1}(u_0,u_1)$  for all  $i \in [2,\ell]$  and  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}^0_3(u_0,u_1) \approx_c \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^1_3(u_0,u_1)$ , respectively. We only sketch the proof for each lemma.

**Lemma 46.** For all  $i \in [2, \ell]$ ,  $u_0, u_1 \in I \times I \times \Sigma \times \mathcal{E}_Q$  and all  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists  $\mathcal{B}$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{A})$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^0_{2.i.1}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^1_{2.i.1}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] \leq O(|\Sigma|) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathrm{DDH}^{G_2}_{1,Q}}_{\mathcal{B}}(\lambda).$$

*Proof* (sketch). We consider the case that the adversary adaptively chooses  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$  in the hybrids parameterized by

$$u_0 = (\{i-1\}, \boxed{\{i-1\}, x_{i-1}^*\}}, \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}), \ u_1 = (\{i-1\}, \boxed{\{i-1,i\}, \bot}, \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*});$$

the lemma trivially holds in other cases. Namely, we need to prove that

$$\left(\mathsf{mpk}, \mathsf{aux}_1, \mathsf{aux}_2, \mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1}, \boxed{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma, x_{i-1}^*, \mathbf{f}_{i-1, x^*}}^{i-1}}\right) \approx_c \left(\mathsf{mpk}, \mathsf{aux}_1, \mathsf{aux}_2, \mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1}, \boxed{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma, \mathbf{f}_{i-1, x^*}}^{i-1, i}}\right).$$

Recall that  $\tau = i \mod 2$ , this roughly means that

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,x_{i-1}^*,\mathbf{f}_{i-1},x^*}^{i-1} [2] &= \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{u}^\mathsf{T} + \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^\mathsf{T}]_2, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^\mathsf{T}]_2 \\ \big\{ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_2, [(\mathbf{d} + s_{i-1}^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}) \mathbf{M}_{x_{i-1}^*} + \mathbf{w}_{x_{i-1}^*,1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \big\} \\ &\qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad \qquad$$

given

$$\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1}[2] = \left( [s_{i-1} \mathbf{w}_{x^*_{i-1}, 1-\tau}]_1, [s_{i-1}]_1, [s_{i-1} \mathbf{z}_{\tau}]_1, [s_{\mathsf{end}} \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{end}}]_1, [s_{\mathsf{end}}]_1, [s_{\mathsf{end}} \alpha]_T \cdot m \right)$$

and

$$\begin{aligned} &\mathsf{aux}_1[2] = \left( [\alpha, \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{start} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{z}_0 \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{z}_1 \mathbf{B}, \{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{B}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{z}_{end} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{end} \mathbf{B}]_2 \right) \\ &\mathsf{aux}_2[2] = \left( [\mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{w}_{start} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{z}_0 \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{z}_1 \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{z}_{end} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, s_{end}^{-1} \Delta + \mathbf{w}_{end} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}]_2 \right) \end{aligned}$$

This relies on:

$$\underbrace{\{\underbrace{(\mathbf{d} + s_{i-1}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}}_{\mathbf{f}_{i-1},x^*} | 2]}^{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,x_{i-1}^*,\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}}^{i-1}[2]}_{\mathbf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}}^{i-1,i}} \\ = \underbrace{\{\underbrace{(\mathbf{d} + s_{i-1}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}}_{\mathbf{f}_{i-1},x^*}) \mathbf{M}_{x_{i-1}^*}^* + \mathbf{w}_{x_{i-1}^*,1-\tau} \mathbf{R}, \underbrace{-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{\tau} \mathbf{R}, \mathbf{R}}_{\mathbf{r}}\}}_{\mathbf{s}} \\ \approx_s \underbrace{\{\underbrace{\mathbf{d} \mathbf{M}_{x_{i-1}^*} + \mathbf{w}_{x_{i-1}^*,1-\tau} \mathbf{R}, \underbrace{-\mathbf{d} + s_{i-1}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}}_{\mathbf{r} - \mathbf{d} + s_{i-1}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}} + \mathbf{z}_{\tau} \mathbf{R}, \mathbf{R}\}}_{\mathbf{s}}$$

in the presence of  $\mathbf{w}_{x_{i-1}^*,1-\tau}$ ,  $\mathbf{z}_{\tau}$  leaked via  $\operatorname{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1}[2]$ .

-  $\operatorname{DDH}_{1,Q}^{G_2}$  assumption w.r.t  $\mathbf{w}_{\operatorname{start}}$ ,  $\mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}$ ,  $\{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\tau}\}_{\sigma \neq x_{i-1}^*}$ ,  $\{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,\tau}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}$ ,  $\mathbf{z}_{\operatorname{end}}$ ; this implies that

$$\left( [\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}} \mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{z}_{1-\tau} \mathbf{R}]_2, \left\{ [\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\tau} \mathbf{R}]_2 \right\}_{\sigma \neq x_{i-1}^*}, \left\{ [\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,\tau} \mathbf{R}]_2 \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, [\mathbf{z}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \right) \approx_c U \left( (G_2^{1 \times Q})^{2|\Sigma| + 2} \times G_2^{k \times Q} \right)$$

and will be used to hide all d's irrelevant with the change of variables.

**Lemma 47.** For all  $u_0, u_1 \in I \times I \times \Sigma \times \mathcal{E}_Q$  and all  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists  $\mathcal{B}$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{A})$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_3^0(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_3^1(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] \leq O(|\Sigma|) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathrm{DDH}_{1,Q}^{G_2}}(\lambda).$$

*Proof* (sketch). We consider the case that the adversary adaptively chooses  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$  in the hybrids parameterized by

$$u_0 = (\{\ell\}, \boxed{\{\ell\}, x_\ell^*, \mathbf{f}_{\ell, x^*}}), \ u_1 = (\{\ell\}, \ \{\ell, *\}, \bot, \mathbf{f});$$

the lemma trivially holds in other cases. By the fact that  $\mathbf{f}_{\ell,x^*} = \mathbf{f}$  (see Lemma 5), we need to prove that

$$\left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{aux}_1,\mathsf{aux}_2,\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^\ell,\overline{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,x_\ell^*,\mathbf{f}}^\ell}\right) \approx_c \left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{aux}_1,\mathsf{aux}_2,\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^\ell,\overline{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}}^{\ell,*}}\right);$$

this roughly means:

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,x_{\ell}^*,\mathbf{f}}^{\ell}[2] \; &= \; \begin{cases} [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{u}^\top + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^\top]_2, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^\top]_2 \\ \big\{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{\bar{\ell}}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\left(\mathbf{d} + s_{\ell}^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}\right)\mathbf{M}_{x_{\ell}^*} + \mathbf{w}_{x_{\ell}^*,\bar{\ell}}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \big\} \\ &\qquad \qquad \left\{[\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,\bar{\ell}}\mathbf{R}]_2 \right\}_{\sigma \neq x_{\ell}^*} \\ \big\{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{1-\bar{\ell}}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\bar{\ell}}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \big\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ &\qquad \qquad \left[[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\alpha\mathbf{f} + \mathbf{w}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \right] \\ &\qquad \qquad \left\{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{\bar{\ell}}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{x_{\ell}^*} + \mathbf{w}_{x_{\ell}^*,\bar{\ell}}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \right\} \\ &\qquad \qquad \approx_c \\ \left\{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{\bar{\ell}}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\bar{\ell}}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ &\qquad \qquad \left\{[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{1-\bar{\ell}}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\bar{\ell}}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \left[[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{s}_{\ell}^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}]_{\ell} + \mathbf{z}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\alpha\mathbf{f} + \mathbf{w}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \end{aligned}$$

given

$$\mathsf{ct}^\ell_{x^*}[2] = \left([s_\ell \mathbf{w}_{x^*_{\ell},\bar{\ell}}]_1, [s_\ell]_1, [s_\ell \mathbf{z}_{\mathrm{end}} + s_{\mathrm{end}} \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}}]_1, [s_{\mathrm{end}}]_1, [s_{\mathrm{end}}\alpha]_T \cdot m\right)$$

and

$$\begin{aligned} &\mathsf{aux}_1[2] = \left( [\alpha, \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{start} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{z}_0 \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{z}_1 \mathbf{B}, \{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{B}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{z}_{end} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{end} \mathbf{B}]_2 \right) \\ &\mathsf{aux}_2[2] = \left( [\mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{w}_{start} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{z}_0 \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{z}_1 \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{z}_{end} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, s_{end}^{-1} \Delta + \mathbf{w}_{end} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}]_2 \right) \end{aligned}$$

This relies on:

- change of variables  $\mathbf{d} \mapsto \mathbf{d} - s_{\ell}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}$ ; this ensures that, for all  $s_{\ell}$  and  $\Delta$ , we have

$$\frac{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,x_{\ell}^*,\ell}^{\ell}[2]}{\left\{\left(\mathbf{d}+s_{\ell}^{-1}\Delta\cdot\mathbf{f}\right)\mathbf{M}_{x_{\ell}^*}+\mathbf{w}_{x_{\ell}^*,\ell}\mathbf{\bar{g}}\mathbf{R},\mathbf{-d}+\mathbf{z}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{R},\mathbf{R}\right\}}\approx_{s}\frac{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{\ell,*}[2]}{\left\{\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{x_{\ell}^*}+\mathbf{w}_{x_{\ell}^*,\ell}\mathbf{\bar{g}}\mathbf{R},\mathbf{-d}+s_{\ell}^{-1}\Delta\cdot\mathbf{f}+\mathbf{z}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{R},\mathbf{R}\right\}}$$
