in the presence of  $\mathbf{w}_{x_{e}^*, \bar{\ell}}$ ,  $\mathbf{z}_{\text{end}}$  leaked via  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{\ell}[2]$ .

 $- \ \, \mathrm{DDH}_{1,Q}^{G_2} \ \, \mathrm{assumption} \ \, \mathrm{w.r.t} \ \, \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{start}}, \mathbf{z_0}, \mathbf{z_1}, \{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,\bar{\ell}}\}_{\sigma \neq x_\ell^*}, \{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\bar{\ell}}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}; \ \, \mathrm{this} \ \, \mathrm{implies} \ \, \mathrm{that}$ 

$$\left( [\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}} \mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{z}_0 \mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{z}_1 \mathbf{R}]_2, \left\{ [\mathbf{w}_{\sigma, \bar{\ell}} \mathbf{R}]_2 \right\}_{\sigma \neq x_{\ell}^*}, \left\{ [\mathbf{w}_{\sigma, 1 - \bar{\ell}} \mathbf{R}]_2 \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \right) \approx_c U \left( (G_2^{1 \times Q})^{2|\Sigma| + 2} \times G_2^{k \times Q} \right)$$

and will be used to hide all  $\mathbf{d}$ 's irrelevant with the change of variables.

**Switching ciphertexts.** We show that  $\widehat{H}^0_{2,i,2}(u_0,u_1) \approx_c \widehat{H}^1_{2,i,2}(u_0,u_1)$  and  $\widehat{H}^0_{2,i,4}(u_0,u_1) \approx_c \widehat{H}^1_{2,i,4}(u_0,u_1)$  for all  $i \in [\ell]$  and all  $u_0,u_1$ . The proofs for them are similar. We begin with the following lemma for the former one and sketch the proof for the latter.

<span id="page-59-0"></span>**Lemma 48.** For all  $i = 1, ..., \ell$ ,  $u_0, u_1 \in I \times I \times \Sigma \times \mathcal{E}_O$  and  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists  $\mathcal{B}$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{A})$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^0_{2.i.2}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^1_{2.i.2}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] \leq \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{EXT-SWITCH}}_{\mathcal{B}}(\lambda).$$

Overview. Fix  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$ . We will prove that

$$\left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{aux}_1, \left\lceil \bar{\mathsf{au}}\bar{\mathsf{x}}_2\right\rceil, \left\lceil \mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1}\right\rceil, \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma, \mathbf{f}_{i-1, x^*}}^{i-1, i}\right) \approx_c \left(\mathsf{mpk}, \mathsf{aux}_1, \left\lceil \bar{\mathsf{au}}\bar{\mathsf{x}}_2\right\rceil, \left\lceil \mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1, i}\right\rceil, \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma, \mathbf{f}_{i-1, x^*}}^{i-1, i}\right)$$

which roughly means that

$$\underbrace{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1}}_{[\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1]_1} \approx_c \underbrace{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1,i}}_{[\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1 + s_i \mathbf{a}_2]} \quad \text{given} \quad \underbrace{\left[\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot s_{\text{end}}^{-1} \Delta + \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{r}^{\top}\right]_2}_{[\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot s_{\text{end}}^{-1} \Delta + \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2}, \underbrace{\left[-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot s_{i-1}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} + \mathbf{Z}_{\tau} \mathbf{R}\right]_2}_{[\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot s_{\text{end}}^{-1} \Delta + \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2}, \underbrace{\left[-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot s_{i-1}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} + \mathbf{Z}_{\tau} \mathbf{R}\right]_2}_{[\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot s_{\text{end}}^{-1} \Delta + \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2}, \underbrace{\left[-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot s_{i-1}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} + \mathbf{Z}_{\tau} \mathbf{R}\right]_2}_{[\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot s_{\text{end}}^{-1} \Delta + \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2}, \underbrace{\left[-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot s_{i-1}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} + \mathbf{Z}_{\tau} \mathbf{R}\right]_2}_{[\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot s_{\text{end}}^{-1} \Delta + \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2}, \underbrace{\left[-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot s_{i-1}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} + \mathbf{Z}_{\tau} \mathbf{R}\right]_2}_{[\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot s_{\text{end}}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{\text{end}}^{-1} + \mathbf{A}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{f}_$$

This is similar to Lemma 14 stating that  $G_{2.i.1} \approx_c G_{2.i.2}$  except that we need to simulate an extra term involving  $\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel}$  from aux<sub>2</sub> (highlighted by dashed box). Therefore, we use an extension of  $(\mathbf{s}_i, \mathbf{Z}_{\tau})$ -switching lemma (Lemma 49) so that we can simulate the challenge ciphertext and secret key as in the proof of Lemma 14 and also handle aux<sub>2</sub>.

### <span id="page-60-0"></span>Lemma 49 ((s, Z, W)-switching lemma). We have

$$\begin{aligned} &\text{aux, } [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1]_1, & [\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \bar{\Delta} + \mathbf{Z}\mathbf{t}^{\top}]_2, & [\mathbf{W}\mathbf{t}^{\top}]_2, & [\mathbf{t}^{\top}]_2 \\ & [\mathbf{Z}\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2, & [\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \bar{\Delta} + \mathbf{W}\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2, & [\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2 \\ \approx_{\textit{c}} \text{aux, } [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1 + \underline{[\mathbf{s}\mathbf{a}_2]]_1}, & [\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \bar{\Delta} + \mathbf{Z}\mathbf{t}^{\top}]_2, & [\mathbf{W}\mathbf{t}^{\top}]_2, & [\mathbf{t}^{\top}]_2 \\ & [\mathbf{Z}\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2, & [\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \bar{\Delta} + \mathbf{W}\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2, & [\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2 \end{aligned}$$

 $\textit{where} \ \mathsf{aux} = ([\mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{a}_2, \mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{Z}, \mathbf{a}_2\mathbf{Z}, \mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{W}, \mathbf{a}_2\mathbf{W}]_1, [\mathbf{ZB}, \mathbf{WB}, \mathbf{B}]_2) \ \textit{and} \ \mathbf{Z}, \mathbf{W} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(2k+1)\times k}, \ \mathbf{B} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \ \mathbf{s}, \mathbf{r}, \mathbf{t} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1\times k}, \ s, \bar{\Delta} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p. \ \textit{Concretely, the advantage function} \ \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{EXT-SWITCH}}(\lambda) \ \textit{is bounded by} \ O(1) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}_0}^{k-\mathsf{LIN}}(\lambda) \ \textit{with} \ \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}_0) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}).$ 

The proof for Lemma 49 is similar to that for the original (s, W)-switching lemma, cf. [11]. We omit the proof here.

*Proof* (of Lemma 48). We consider the case that the adversary adaptively chooses  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$  in the hybrids parameterized by

$$u_0 = (\overline{\{i-1\}}, \{i-1, i\}, \bot, \mathbf{f}_{i-1, x^*}), \ u_1 = (\overline{\{i-1, i\}}, \{i-1, i\}, \bot, \mathbf{f}_{i-1, x^*});$$

the lemma trivially holds in other cases. Recall that  $\tau = i \mod 2$ . We prove the lemma using  $(\mathbf{s}_i, \mathbf{Z}_\tau, \mathbf{W}_{\mathrm{end}})$ -switching lemma. On input

$$\begin{aligned} \text{aux, } [\mathbf{c}_i]_1, \ [\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \bar{\Delta} + \mathbf{Z}_{\tau} \mathbf{t}^{\top}]_2, \ \ [\mathbf{W}_{end} \mathbf{t}^{\top}]_2, \ [\mathbf{t}^{\top}]_2 \\ [\mathbf{Z}_{\tau} \mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2, \ [\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \bar{\Delta} + \mathbf{W}_{end} \mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2, \ [\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2 \end{aligned}$$

where  $\mathsf{aux} = ([\mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{a}_2, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{Z}_\tau, \mathbf{a}_2 \mathbf{Z}_\tau, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{end}, \mathbf{a}_2 \mathbf{W}_{end}]_1, [\mathbf{Z}_\tau \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{W}_{end} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{B}]_2) \text{ and } \mathbf{Z}_\tau, \mathbf{W}_{end} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(2k+1)\times k}, \mathbf{B} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times k}, \mathbf{r}, \mathbf{t} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1\times k}, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{end}, \mathbf{A}_2 \mathbf{W}_{end}]_1, [\mathbf{Z}_\tau \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{W}_{end}, \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{B}]_2)$ 

$$\mathbf{c}_i = \boxed{\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1}$$
 or  $\mathbf{c}_i = \boxed{\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1 + s_i \mathbf{a}_2}$ ,  $\mathbf{s}_i \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$ ,  $s_i \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ 

the reduction works as follows:

(Simulating mpk and  $\mathsf{aux}_1$ ) We sample  $\mathbf{k} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times (2k+1)}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}}$ ,  $\mathbf{Z}_{1-\tau}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1}$ ,  $\mathbf{Z}_{end} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(2k+1) \times k}$  for all  $\sigma \in \Sigma$ , and then we can trivially simulate mpk from  $[\mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{Z}_{\tau}, \mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{W}_{end}]_1$  and simulate  $\mathsf{aux}_1$  from  $[\mathbf{Z}_\tau\mathbf{B}, \mathbf{W}_{end}\mathbf{B}, \mathbf{B}]_2$ .

(**Simulating** aux<sub>2</sub>) We sample  $s_{\text{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and implicitly set  $\Delta = s_{\text{end}}\bar{\Delta}$ ; then we can rewrite aux<sub>2</sub> as

$$\begin{bmatrix} [\boldsymbol{r}^{\top}]_2 \end{bmatrix}, [\boldsymbol{W}_{start}\boldsymbol{r}^{\top}]_2, \begin{bmatrix} [\boldsymbol{Z}_{\tau}\boldsymbol{r}^{\top}]_2 \end{bmatrix}, [\boldsymbol{Z}_{1-\tau}\boldsymbol{r}^{\top}]_2, \{[\boldsymbol{W}_{\sigma,0}\boldsymbol{r}^{\top}]_2, [\boldsymbol{W}_{\sigma,1}\boldsymbol{r}^{\top}]_2\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, [\boldsymbol{Z}_{end}\boldsymbol{r}^{\top}]_2, \begin{bmatrix} [\boldsymbol{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \bar{\Delta} + \boldsymbol{W}_{end}\boldsymbol{r}^{\top}]_2 \end{bmatrix}, \begin{bmatrix} [\boldsymbol{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \bar{\Delta} + \boldsymbol{W}_{end}\boldsymbol{r}^{\top}]_2 \end{bmatrix}$$

All terms in the dashed boxes are provided in the lemma; all remaining terms can be simulated using  $[\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_2$  and  $\mathbf{W}_{\text{start}}$ ,  $\mathbf{Z}_{1-\tau}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1}$ ,  $\mathbf{Z}_{\text{end}}$ .

(Answering OEnc) On input  $(x^*, m)$ , we want to create a ciphertext in the following form, which is either  $\operatorname{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1}$  or  $\operatorname{ct}_{r^*}^{i-1,i}$  depending on  $\mathbf{c}_i$ :

$$\begin{cases} [\mathbf{c}_{0}]_{1}, [\mathbf{c}_{0}\mathbf{W}_{\text{start}}]_{1} \\ \left\{ [\mathbf{c}_{j}]_{1}, [\mathbf{c}_{j-1}\mathbf{Z}_{\tau}]_{1} \right\} \cdot [\mathbf{c}_{j}\mathbf{W}_{x_{j},\tau}]_{1} \right\}_{j=i \text{ mod } 2} \\ \left\{ [\mathbf{c}_{j}]_{1}, [\mathbf{c}_{j-1}\mathbf{Z}_{1-\tau}]_{1} \cdot [\mathbf{c}_{j}\mathbf{W}_{x_{j},1-\tau}]_{1} \right\}_{j\neq i \text{ mod } 2} \\ \left[ [\mathbf{c}_{\text{end}}]_{1}, [\mathbf{c}_{\ell}\mathbf{Z}_{\text{end}}]_{1} \cdot [[\mathbf{c}_{\text{end}}\mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}]_{1}]_{j} \cdot [\mathbf{c}_{\text{end}}\mathbf{k}^{\top}]_{T} \cdot m \end{cases} \end{cases} \text{ where } \begin{cases} \mathbf{c}_{i} \in \{ \mathbf{s}_{i}\mathbf{A}_{1}, \mathbf{s}_{i}\mathbf{A}_{1} + s_{i}\mathbf{a}_{2} \} \\ \mathbf{c}_{i-1} = \mathbf{s}_{i-1}\mathbf{A}_{1} + s_{i-1}\mathbf{a}_{2} \\ \mathbf{c}_{\text{end}} = \mathbf{s}_{\text{end}}\mathbf{A}_{1} + s_{\text{end}}\mathbf{a}_{2} \\ \mathbf{c}_{j} = \mathbf{s}_{j}\mathbf{A}_{1} \quad \text{if } j \notin \{i-1, i\} \end{cases}$$

Observe that,

- when  $\mathbf{c}_i = \boxed{\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1}$ , the distribution is identical to  $\boxed{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1}}$ ;
   when  $\mathbf{c}_i = \boxed{\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1 + s_i \mathbf{a}_2}$ , the distribution is identical to  $\boxed{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1,i}}$

We proceed as follows:

- We sample  $\mathbf{s}_j \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  for all  $j \neq i$ ,  $s_{i-1} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and simulate  $\{[\mathbf{c}_j]_1\}_{j \neq i}$  and  $[\mathbf{c}_{\text{end}}]_1$  using  $[\mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{a}_2]_1$ ; note that  $[\mathbf{c}_i]_1$  is given out in the lemma as the challenge term.
- We rewrite terms in the first dashed box as:

$$[\mathbf{c}_{j}\mathbf{Z}_{\tau}]_{1} = \begin{cases} [\mathbf{s}_{j}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{Z}_{\tau}]_{1} & \text{if } j \neq i-1 \text{ and } j \neq i \text{ mod } 2\\ [\mathbf{s}_{i-1}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{Z}_{\tau}]_{1} \cdot [s_{i-1}\mathbf{a}_{2}\mathbf{Z}_{\tau}]_{1} & \text{if } j = i-1 \text{ (and } j \neq i \text{ mod } 2) \end{cases}$$

which can be simulated using  $\{\mathbf{s}_j\}_{j\neq i \bmod 2}$ ,  $s_{i-1}$  and  $[\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{Z}_\tau,\mathbf{a}_2\mathbf{Z}_\tau]_1$ ; here we use the fact that we do not have any terms involving [ $\mathbf{c}_i \mathbf{Z}_{\tau}$ ]<sub>1</sub> in the ciphertext.

- We write term in the second dashed box as:

$$[\mathbf{c}_{\text{end}}\mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}]_1 = [\mathbf{s}_{\text{end}}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}]_1 \cdot [s_{\text{end}}\mathbf{a}_2\mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}]_1$$

which can be simulated using  $\mathbf{s}_{\text{end}}$ ,  $s_{\text{end}}$  and  $[\mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}, \mathbf{a}_2 \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}]_1$ ; here we use the fact that we do not have any terms involving  $[\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}]_1$  in the ciphertext.

- We simulate all remaining terms using  $\{[\mathbf{c}_j]_1\}_{j\in[0,\ell]}, [\mathbf{c}_{\mathrm{end}}]_1$  and  $\mathbf{k}, \mathbf{W}_{\mathrm{start}}, \mathbf{Z}_{1-\tau}, \{\mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1}\}_{\sigma\in\Sigma}, \mathbf{Z}_{\mathrm{end}}$ .

(Answering OKey) On input  $\Gamma$ , we want to return a secret key for  $\Gamma$  in the form

$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}}^{i-1,i} = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{D}\mathbf{u}^\top + \mathbf{W}_{\text{start}}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^\top]_2, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^\top]_2 \\ [-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot s_{i-1}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} + \mathbf{Z}_{\tau}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{D}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,\tau}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \\ \\ [-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{Z}_{1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{D}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \\ \\ [-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{Z}_{\text{end}}\mathbf{R}]_2, [[\mathbf{k}^\top \mathbf{f} + \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}\mathbf{R}]_2], [\mathbf{R}]_2 \end{pmatrix} (\mathbf{R})_2 \end{pmatrix}.$$

We sample  $\mathbf{D} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(2k+1) \times Q}$  and  $\widetilde{\mathbf{R}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times Q}$  and implicitly set

$$\mathbf{R} = \mathbf{t}^{\mathsf{T}} \cdot s_{i-1}^{-1} s_{\text{end}} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} + \mathbf{B} \cdot \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}.$$

We proceed to simulate  $\mathsf{sk}^{i-1,i}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{i-1},*}$  as follows:

- We simulate  $[\mathbf{R}]_2$  from  $[\mathbf{t}^{\mathsf{T}}]_2$ ,  $[\mathbf{B}]_2$  and  $\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}$ ,  $\widetilde{\mathbf{R}}$ ,  $s_{i-1}$ ,  $s_{\text{end}}$ .
- Recall that we set  $\Delta = s_{\rm end}\bar{\Delta}$ , we can rewrite terms in the dashed boxes as:

$$[-\mathbf{D} + (\mathbf{a}_{2}^{\parallel} \cdot \bar{\Delta} + \mathbf{Z}_{\tau} \mathbf{t}^{\top}) \cdot s_{i-1}^{-1} s_{\text{end}} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^{*}} + \mathbf{Z}_{\tau} \mathbf{B} \cdot \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}]_{2} \quad \text{and} \quad [\mathbf{k}^{\top} \mathbf{f} + \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{t}^{\top} \cdot s_{i-1}^{-1} s_{\text{end}} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^{*}} + \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{B} \cdot \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}]_{2}$$

which can be simulated using  $[\mathbf{a}_{2}^{\parallel} \cdot \bar{\Delta} + \mathbf{Z}_{\tau} \mathbf{t}^{\top}]_{2}$ ,  $[\mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{t}^{\top}]_{2}$ ,  $[\mathbf{Z}_{\tau} \mathbf{B}]_{2}$ ,  $[\mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{B}]_{2}$  and  $\mathbf{D}$ ,  $\mathbf{k}$ ,  $\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^{*}}$ ,  $\widetilde{\mathbf{R}}$ ,  $\mathbf{s}_{i-1}$ ,  $\mathbf{s}_{\text{end}}$ .

- We simulate all remaining terms using [**R**]<sub>2</sub> and **D**,  $\mathbf{W}_{\text{start}}$ ,  $\mathbf{Z}_{1-\tau}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\sigma,\tau}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1-\tau}$ ,  $\mathbf{Z}_{\text{end}}$ .

Observe that, when  $\mathbf{c}_i = \boxed{\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1}$ , oracle  $\mathsf{OEnc}(x^*, m)$  returns  $\boxed{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1}}$  and the simulation is identical to  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_{2.i.2}^0(u_0, u_1)$ ; when  $\mathbf{c}_i = \boxed{\mathbf{s}_i \mathbf{A}_1 + s_i \mathbf{a}_2}$ , oracle  $\mathsf{OEnc}(x^*, m)$  returns  $\boxed{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1,i}}$  and the simulation is identical to  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_{2.i.2}^1(u_0, u_1)$ . This completes the proof.

Via the same proof idea, we can prove the following lemmas stating that  $\widehat{H}^0_{2.i.4}(u_0,u_1) \approx_c H^1_{2.i.4}(u_0,u_1)$  for all  $i \in [\ell]$  and all  $u_0,u_2$ . We only sketch the proof.

**Lemma 50.** For all  $i \in [\ell]$ ,  $u_0, u_1 \in I \times I \times \Sigma \times \mathcal{E}_Q$  and all  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists  $\mathcal{B}$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{A})$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^0_{2.i.4}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^1_{2.i.4}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] \leq \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{EXT-SWITCH}}_{\mathcal{B}}(\lambda).$$

*Proof* (sketch). We consider the case that the adversary adaptively chooses  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$  in the hybrids parameterized by

$$u_0 = (\overline{\{i-1,i\}},\{i\},x_i^*,\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}),\ u_1 = (\overline{\ \{i\}\ ,\{i\},x_i^*,\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*})};$$

the lemma trivially holds in other cases. Namely, we will prove that

$$\left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{aux}_1,\mathsf{aux}_2,\overline{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1,i}}\right)\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,x_i^*,\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}}^i\right) \approx_c \left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{aux}_1,\mathsf{aux}_2,\overline{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^i},\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,x_i^*,\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}}^i\right)$$

which roughly means that

$$\underbrace{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1,i}}_{\mathbf{[\mathbf{s}_{i-1}}\mathbf{A}_1+\mathbf{s}_{i-1}\mathbf{a}_2]_1}^{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^i} \approx_c \underbrace{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i}}_{\mathbf{[\mathbf{s}_{i-1}}\mathbf{A}_1]_1}^{\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^i} \quad \mathsf{given} \quad \underbrace{[\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{s}_{\mathrm{end}}^{-1} \Delta + \mathbf{W}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2}_{\mathbf{a}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{A}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2}^{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,x_i^*}^i, \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}} \underbrace{[\mathbf{D}\mathbf{M}_{x_i^*} + \mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel} \cdot \mathbf{s}_{i}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} + \mathbf{W}_{x_i^*,\tau}^* \mathbf{R}]_2}_{\mathbf{a}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{A}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2}$$

The proof is analogous to that of Lemma 48 except that we use  $(\mathbf{s}_{i-1}, \mathbf{W}_{x_i^*, \tau}, \mathbf{W}_{end})$ - instead of  $(\mathbf{s}_i, \mathbf{Z}_\tau, \mathbf{W}_{end})$ -switching lemma so that we can simulate the challenge ciphertext from the challenge term in the lemma and simulate both secret key and  $\mathsf{aux}_2$  using the auxiliary terms given out in the lemma.

**Switching secret keys II.** We show that  $\widehat{H}^0_{2,i,3}(u_0,u_1) \approx_c \widehat{H}^1_{2,i,3}(u_0,u_1)$  and  $\widehat{H}^0_4(u_0,u_1) \approx_c \widehat{H}^1_4(u_0,u_1)$  for all  $i \in [\ell]$  and  $u_0,u_1$ . The proofs for them are similar. We begin with the following lemma stating that  $\widehat{H}^0_{2,i,3}(u_0,u_1) \approx_c \widehat{H}^1_{2,i,3}(u_0,u_1)$ , which is analogous to Lemma 17, and sketch the proof for the latter one.

**Lemma 51.** For all  $i \in [\ell]$ ,  $u_0, u_1 \in I \times I \times \Sigma \times \mathcal{E}_O$  and all  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists  $\mathcal{B}$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{A})$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^{0}_{2.i.3}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^{1}_{2.i.3}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] \leq \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{TRANS}}_{\mathcal{B}}(\lambda).$$

*Proof.* We consider the case that the adversary adaptively chooses  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$  in the hybrids parameterized by

$$u_0 = (\{i-1,i\}, \overline{\{i-1,i\}, \bot, \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}}), \ u_1 = (\{i-1,i\}, \overline{\{i\}, x_i^*, \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}});$$

the lemma trivially holds in other cases. Recall that  $\tau = i \mod 2$ . By Lemma 4, it suffices to prove the lemma over  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components which roughly means:

$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{i-1},x^*}^{i-1,i}[2] = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{u}^\top + \mathbf{w}_{start}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^\top]_2, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^\top]_2 \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \boxed{s_{i-1}^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1},x^* + \mathbf{z}_{\tau}\mathbf{R}} \end{bmatrix}_2, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{x_i^*} + \boxed{\mathbf{w}_{x_i^*,\tau}\mathbf{R}} \end{bmatrix}_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \\ \{ [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,\tau}\mathbf{R}]_2 \}_{\sigma \neq x_i^*} \\ \{ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\alpha\mathbf{f} + \mathbf{w}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \end{pmatrix}$$

$$\approx_c \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{u}^\top + \mathbf{w}_{start}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^\top]_2, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^\top]_2 \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \boxed{\mathbf{z}_{\tau}\mathbf{R}}]_2, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{x_i^*} + \boxed{s_i^{-1}\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}\mathbf{M}_{x_i^*} + \mathbf{w}_{x_i^*,\tau}\mathbf{R}} ]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \\ \{ [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,\tau}\mathbf{R}]_2 \}_{\sigma \neq x_i^*} \\ \{ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\alpha\mathbf{f} + \mathbf{w}_{end}\mathbf{R}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \end{pmatrix}$$

in the presence of

$$\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1,i}[2] = \begin{cases} [s_0 \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}]_1, [s_0]_1, [s_0 \mathbf{z}_1 + s_1 \mathbf{w}_{x_1^*,1}]_1, [s_1]_1, [s_1 \mathbf{z}_0]_1, [s_{\mathsf{end}} \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{end}}]_1, [s_{\mathsf{end}} \alpha]_T \cdot m & \text{if } i = 1 \\ [s_{i-1} \mathbf{w}_{x_{i-1}^*,1-\tau}]_1, [s_{i-1}]_1, [s_{i-1} \mathbf{z}_\tau + s_i \mathbf{w}_{x_i^*,\tau}]_1, [s_i]_1, [s_i \mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}]_1, [s_{\mathsf{end}} \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{end}}]_1, [s_{\mathsf{end}} \alpha]_T \cdot m & \text{if } i \in [2, \ell-1] \\ [s_{\ell-1} \mathbf{w}_{x_{\ell-1}^*,1-\ell}]_1, [s_{\ell-1}]_1, [s_{\ell-1} \mathbf{z}_\ell + s_\ell \mathbf{w}_{x_\ell^*,\ell}]_1, [s_\ell]_1, [s_\ell \mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{end}} + s_{\mathsf{end}} \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{end}}]_1, [s_{\mathsf{end}}]_1, [s_{\mathsf{end}} \alpha]_T \cdot m & \text{if } i = \ell \end{cases}$$

and

$$\begin{aligned} &\mathsf{aux}_1[2] = \left( [\alpha, \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{start} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{z}_0 \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{z}_1 \mathbf{B}, \{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{B}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{z}_{end} \mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{end} \mathbf{B}]_2 \right) \\ &\mathsf{aux}_2[2] = \left( [\mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{w}_{start} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{z}_0 \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{z}_1 \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{z}_{end} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}, \mathbf{s}_{end}^{-1} \Delta + \mathbf{w}_{end} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}]_2 \right) \end{aligned}$$

One can sample basis  $\mathbf{A}_1$ ,  $\mathbf{a}_2$ ,  $\mathbf{A}_3$ ,  $\mathbf{A}_1^{\parallel}$ ,  $\mathbf{a}_2^{\parallel}$ ,  $\mathbf{A}_3^{\parallel}$  and trivially simulate mpk, ct $_{r*}^{i-1,i}$  and secret key using terms given out above. Furthermore, we prove this using  $(\mathbf{z}_{\tau}, \mathbf{w}_{x_{\tau}^*, \tau})$ -transition lemma. On input

$$\mathsf{aux}, [\bar{\Delta}_0 + \mathbf{z}_\tau \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}]_2, [\bar{\Delta}_1 + \mathbf{w}_{x_i^*,\tau} \mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}]_2, [\mathbf{r}^\mathsf{T}]_2$$

where  $(\bar{\Delta}_0, \bar{\Delta}_1) \in \{ [s_{i-1}^{-1}\bar{\Delta}, 0), (0, s_i^{-1}\bar{\Delta}) \}$  and  $\mathsf{aux} = (\bar{\Delta}, s_{i-1}, s_i, s_{i-1}\mathbf{z}_\tau + s_i\mathbf{w}_{x_i^*, \tau}, [\mathbf{z}_\tau\mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{x_i^*, \tau}\mathbf{B}, \mathbf{B}]_2)$  with  $\mathbf{z}_\tau, \mathbf{w}_{x_i^*, \tau} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$ ,  $\mathbf{B} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times k}, \mathbf{r} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  and  $\Delta \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ , we sample  $\alpha \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p, \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}, \mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}, \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\tau}, \mathbf{z}_{\mathsf{end}}, \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  for all  $\sigma \in \Sigma$  and  $\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,\tau} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$ for all  $\sigma \neq x_i^*$  and proceed as follows:

(Simulating  $aux_1$  and  $aux_2$ ) We sample  $s_{end} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and implicitly set  $\Delta = \bar{\Delta}$ . Then we can simulate  $aux_1[2]$ ,  $aux_2[2]$  from  $[\mathbf{z}_{\tau}\mathbf{B}, \mathbf{w}_{x_{i}^{*}, \tau}\mathbf{B}, \mathbf{B}]_{2}$  and  $\bar{\Delta}$  given out in aux along with  $s_{\mathrm{end}}$ ,  $\alpha$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{start}}$ ,  $\mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}$ ,  $\{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\tau}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}$ ,  $\{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,\tau}\}_{\sigma \neq x_{i}^{*}}$ ,  $\mathbf{z}_{\mathrm{end}}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}}$ .

(Answering OEnc) On input  $(x^*, m)$ , we trivially simulate  $\operatorname{ct}_{x^*}^{i-1,i}[2]$  using  $s_{i-1}, s_i, s_{i-1}\mathbf{z}_{\tau} + s_i\mathbf{w}_{x_i^*,\tau}$  in aux and  $s_{\operatorname{end}}, \alpha$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\tau}$ ,  $\mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}$ ,  $\mathbf{z}_{\text{end}}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\text{end}}$ .

(**Answering** OKey) On input  $\Gamma$ , we want to return a key for  $\Gamma$  in the form:

$$\begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{u}^{\top} + \mathbf{w}_{start}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \Delta_{0} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^{*}} + \mathbf{z}_{\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{x_{i}^{*}} + \Delta_{1} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^{*}} + \mathbf{w}_{x_{i}^{*},\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{0} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^{*}} + \mathbf{z}_{\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{x_{i}^{*}} + \Delta_{1} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^{*}} + \mathbf{w}_{x_{i}^{*},\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{0} \cdot \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \\ [-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{0} \cdot \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}$$

$$[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{0} \cdot \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\tau}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2}$$

$$[-\mathbf{d} + \mathbf{z}_{0} \cdot \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{d}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1} \cdot \mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2}$$

Observe that

- $\text{ when } (\Delta_0, \Delta_1) = \underbrace{(s_{i-1}^{-1} \Delta, 0)}_{i}, \text{ the distribution is identical to } \underbrace{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma, \mathbf{f}_{i-1, x^*}}^{i-1, i}[2]}_{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma, \mathbf{f}_{i-1, x^*}}^*}[2] ; \\ \text{ when } (\Delta_0, \Delta_1) = \underbrace{(0, s_i^{-1} \Delta)}_{i}, \text{ the distribution is identical to } \underbrace{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma, x_i^*, \mathbf{f}_{i, x^*}}^{i}[2]}_{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma, x_i^*, \mathbf{f}_{i, x^*}}^*}[2] \; \text{since } \mathbf{f}_{i-1, x^*} = \mathbf{f}_{i, x^*} \mathbf{M}_{x_i^*} \; \text{mod } p, \text{ see Lemma 5.}$

Recall that we set  $\Delta = \bar{\Delta}$  which means we also implicitly set

$$(\Delta_0, \Delta_1) = (\bar{\Delta}_0, \bar{\Delta}_1)$$

We sample  $\mathbf{d} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times Q}$  and  $\widetilde{\mathbf{R}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times Q}$  and implicitly set

$$\mathbf{R} = \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}} \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} + \mathbf{B} \cdot \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}$$

We then generate the key for  $\Gamma$  as follows:

- We simulate  $[\mathbf{R}]_2$  from  $[\mathbf{r}^T]_2$ ,  $[\mathbf{B}]_2$  and  $\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}$ ,  $\widetilde{\mathbf{R}}$ .

- We rewrite the terms in the dashed box as follows:

$$[-\mathbf{d} + (\bar{\Delta}_0 + \mathbf{z}_\tau \mathbf{r}^\top) \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} + \mathbf{z}_\tau \mathbf{B} \cdot \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}]_2, \ [\mathbf{d} \mathbf{M}_{x_i^*} + (\bar{\Delta}_1 + \mathbf{w}_{x_i^*,\tau} \mathbf{r}^\top) \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} + \mathbf{w}_{x_i^*,\tau} \mathbf{B} \cdot \widetilde{\mathbf{R}}]_2$$

and simulate them using  $[\bar{\Delta}_0 + \mathbf{z}_{\tau} \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_2$ ,  $[\bar{\Delta}_1 + \mathbf{w}_{x_i^*, \tau} \mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_2$ ,  $[\mathbf{r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_2$ ,  $[\mathbf{z}_{\tau} \mathbf{B}]_2$ ,  $[\mathbf{w}_{x_i^*, \tau} \mathbf{B}]_2$  and  $\mathbf{d}$ ,  $\mathbf{f}_{i-1, x^*}$ ,  $\widetilde{\mathbf{R}}$ .

- We simulate all remaining terms using  $[\mathbf{R}]_2$  and  $\mathbf{d}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}$ ,  $\mathbf{z}_{1-\tau}$ ,  $\{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,\tau}\}_{\sigma \neq x_i^*}$ ,  $\{\mathbf{w}_{\sigma,1-\tau}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}$ ,  $\mathbf{z}_{\text{end}}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\text{end}}$ .

Observe that, when  $(\bar{\Delta}_0, \bar{\Delta}_1) = [(s_{i-1}^{-1}\bar{\Delta}, 0)]$ , we have  $(\Delta_0, \Delta_1) = [(s_{i-1}^{-1}\Delta, 0)]$ , then oracle  $OKey(\Gamma)$  returns  $[sk_{\Gamma, \mathbf{f}_{i-1, x^*}}^{i-1, i}[2]]$  and the simulation is identical to  $\widehat{H}^0_{2,i,3}(u_0, u_1)$ ; when  $(\bar{\Delta}_0, \bar{\Delta}_1) = [(0, s_i^{-1}\bar{\Delta})]$ , we have  $(\Delta_0, \Delta_1) = [(0, s_i^{-1}\Delta)]$ , then oracle  $OKey(\Gamma)$  returns  $[sk_{\Gamma, x_i^*, \mathbf{f}_{i, x^*}}^{i}[2]]$  and the simulation is identical to  $\widehat{H}^1_{2,i,3}(u_0, u_1)$ . This completes the proof.

Via the same proof idea, we can prove the following lemmas stating that  $\widehat{H}_{4}^{0}(u_0, u_1) \approx_c \widehat{H}_{4}^{1}(u_0, u_1)$  for all  $u_0, u_2$ . We only sketch the proof.

**Lemma 52.** For all  $u_0, u_1 \in I \times I \times \Sigma \times \mathcal{E}_Q$  and all  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists  $\mathcal{B}$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{A})$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_4^0(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_4^1(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{TRANS}}(\lambda).$$

*Proof* (sketch). We consider the case that the adversary adaptively chooses  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$  in the hybrids parameterized by

$$u_0 = (\{\ell\}, \overline{\{\ell, *\}}, \bot, \bot), \ u_1 = (\{\ell\}, \overline{\{*\}}, \bot, \bot);$$

the lemma trivially holds in other cases. Namely, we will prove that

$$\left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{aux}_1,\mathsf{aux}_2,\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^\ell,\boxed{\mathsf{sk}_\Gamma^{\ell,*}}\right)\approx_c\left(\mathsf{mpk},\mathsf{aux}_1,\mathsf{aux}_2,\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^\ell,\boxed{\mathsf{sk}_\Gamma^*}\right);$$

which roughly means that we need to show:

$$\begin{split} & [-\mathbf{d} + \boxed{s_{\ell}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f} + \mathbf{z}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{R}}]_2, \quad [\alpha \mathbf{f} + \boxed{\mathbf{w}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{R}}]_2, \quad [\mathbf{R}]_2 \qquad //\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^{\ell,*} \\ \approx_c \qquad & [-\mathbf{d} + \boxed{\mathbf{z}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{R}}]_2, \quad [\alpha \mathbf{f} + \boxed{s_{\text{end}}^{-1} \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f} + \mathbf{w}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{R}}]_2, \quad [\mathbf{R}]_2 \qquad //\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^* \end{split}$$

given  $\mathbf{d}$ ,  $\alpha$ ,  $\Delta$ ,  $s_{\ell}$ ,  $s_{\mathrm{end}}$ ,  $s_{\ell}\mathbf{z}_{\mathrm{end}}$  +  $s_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}}$ . This can be handled using ( $\mathbf{z}_{\mathrm{end}}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}}$ )-transition lemma.

## <span id="page-64-0"></span>F Concrete ABE for DFA with Adaptive Security

In this section, we show our concrete ABE for DFA with adaptive security. This is derived from our adaptively secure ABE for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NFA<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> in Section 5.1 and the transformation from DFA to  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NFA $^{\oplus p}$  in Section 3, see Lemma 1.

– Setup $(1^{\lambda}, \Sigma)$ : Run  $\mathbb{G} = (p, G_1, G_2, G_T, e) \leftarrow \mathcal{G}(1^{\lambda})$ . Sample

$$\mathbf{A}_1 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times (2k+1)}, \mathbf{k} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times (2k+1)} \quad \text{and} \quad \mathbf{W}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{Z}_0, \mathbf{Z}_1, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1}, \mathbf{Z}_{\text{end}}, \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(2k+1) \times k}, \ \forall \ \sigma \in \Sigma.$$

Output

$$\begin{aligned} & \mathsf{mpk} = \left( \left[ \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}}, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{Z}_0, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{Z}_1, \left\{ \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1} \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{Z}_{end}, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{end} \right]_1, \left[ \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}} \right]_T \right) \\ & \mathsf{msk} = \left( \mathbf{k}, \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}}, \mathbf{Z}_0, \mathbf{Z}_1, \left\{ \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1} \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{Z}_{end}, \mathbf{W}_{end} \right). \end{aligned}$$

-  $\mathsf{Enc}(\mathsf{mpk},x,m)$ : Let  $x=(x_1,\ldots,x_\ell)\in\Sigma^\ell$ . Pick  $\mathbf{s}_0,\mathbf{s}_1,\ldots,\mathbf{s}_\ell,\mathbf{s}_{\mathrm{end}}\leftarrow\mathbb{Z}_p^{1\times k}$  and output

$$\mathsf{ct}_x = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{s}_0 \mathbf{A}_1]_1, [\mathbf{s}_0 \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}}]_1 \\ \big\{ [\mathbf{s}_j \mathbf{A}_1]_1, [\mathbf{s}_{j-1} \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{Z}_{j \bmod 2} + \mathbf{s}_j \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{x_{\ell+1-j}, j \bmod 2}]_1 \big\}_{j \in [\ell]} \\ [\mathbf{s}_{\mathsf{end}} \mathbf{A}_1]_1, [\mathbf{s}_\ell \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{Z}_{\mathsf{end}} + \mathbf{s}_{\mathsf{end}} \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{end}}]_1, [\mathbf{s}_{\mathsf{end}} \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{k}^\mathsf{T}]_T \cdot m. \end{pmatrix}.$$

- KeyGen(mpk, msk,  $\Gamma$ ): Pick  $\mathbf{D} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(2k+1)\times Q}$ ,  $\mathbf{R} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times Q}$  and output

$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma} = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{D}\mathbf{f}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}}\mathbf{R}\mathbf{f}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}\mathbf{f}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \{[-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{Z}_{b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{D}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0,1\}} \\ [-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{Z}_{\mathsf{end}}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{u} + \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{end}}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}.$$

- Dec(mpk, sk $_{\Gamma}$ , ct $_{x}$ ): Parse ciphertext for string  $x=(x_{1},\ldots,x_{\ell})$  and key for  $\Gamma=(Q,\Sigma,\{\mathbf{M}_{\sigma}\}_{\sigma\in\Sigma},\mathbf{u},\mathbf{f})$  as

$$\mathsf{ct}_x = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{c}_{0,1}]_1, [\mathbf{c}_{0,2}]_1 \\ \left\{ [\mathbf{c}_{j,1}]_1, [\mathbf{c}_{j,2}]_1 \right\}_j \\ [\mathbf{c}_{\mathrm{end},1}]_1, [\mathbf{c}_{\mathrm{end},2}]_1, C \end{pmatrix} \quad \text{and} \quad \mathsf{sk}_\Gamma = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{k}_0^\mathsf{T}]_2, [\mathbf{r}_0^\mathsf{T}]_2 \\ \left\{ [\mathbf{K}_b]_2, [\mathbf{K}_{\sigma,b}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \right\}_{\sigma,b} \\ [\mathbf{K}_{\mathrm{end},1}]_2, [\mathbf{K}_{\mathrm{end},2}]_2, [\mathbf{R}]_2 \end{pmatrix}.$$

We define  $\mathbf{f}_{j,x}$  for all  $j \in [0, \ell]$  as (22) and proceed as follows:

1. Compute

$$B_0 = e([\mathbf{c}_{0,1}]_1, [\mathbf{k}_0^\top]_2) \cdot e([\mathbf{c}_{0,2}]_1, [\mathbf{r}_0^\top]_2)^{-1};$$

2. For all  $j = 1, ..., \ell$ , compute

$$[\mathbf{b}_j]_T = e([\mathbf{c}_{j-1,1}]_1, [\mathbf{K}_{j \bmod 2}]_2) \cdot e([\mathbf{c}_{j,1}]_1, [\mathbf{K}_{x_{\ell+1-j}, j \bmod 2}]_2) \cdot e([-\mathbf{c}_{j,2}]_1, [\mathbf{R}]_2) \quad \text{and} \quad B_j = [\mathbf{b}_j \mathbf{f}_{\ell+1-j, x}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T;$$

3. Compute

$$[\mathbf{b}_{\text{end}}]_T = e([\mathbf{c}_{\ell,1}]_1, [\mathbf{K}_{\text{end},1}]_2) \cdot e([\mathbf{c}_{\text{end},1}]_1, [\mathbf{K}_{\text{end},2}]_2) \cdot e([-\mathbf{c}_{\text{end},2}]_1, [\mathbf{R}]_2) \quad \text{and} \quad B_{\text{end}} = [\mathbf{b}_{\text{end}}\mathbf{f}_{0,x}^T]_T;$$

4. Compute

$$B_{\text{all}} = B_0 \cdot \prod_{j=1}^{\ell} B_j \cdot B_{\text{end}}$$
 and  $B = B_{\text{all}}^{(\mathbf{uf}_{0,x}^{\mathsf{T}})^{-1}}$ 

and output the message  $m' \leftarrow C \cdot B^{-1}$ .

## <span id="page-65-0"></span>G Missing Material from Section 6

### <span id="page-65-1"></span>G.1 An Attack for Non-injective $\rho$ with Shared Random Coins

We consider the following ABE scheme, which is the ABE scheme for NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> in Section 6.2 but with  $\mathbf{R}_j = \mathbf{R} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times Q}$  for all  $j \in \ell_{\mathrm{BP}}$ , as is the case mentioned in the **Overview** paragraph at the beginning of Section 6.2.

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{mpk} &= \left( \left[ \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}}, \left\{ \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\eta, \sigma} \right\}_{\eta \in [\ell], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{end}} \right]_1, \left[ \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{k}^\top \right]_T \right); \\ \mathsf{sk}_\Gamma &= \begin{pmatrix} \left[ \mathbf{D}_0 \mathbf{u}^\top + \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}} \mathbf{r}^\top \right]_2, \left[ \mathbf{r}^\top \right]_2 \\ \left\{ \left[ \mathbf{D}_j \mathbf{M}_{j, \sigma} - \mathbf{D}_{j-1} + \mathbf{W}_{\rho(j), \sigma} \mathbf{R} \right]_2, \left[ \mathbf{R} \right]_2 \right\}_{j \in [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}], \sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \left[ \mathbf{k}^\top \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{D}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{W}_{\mathrm{end}} \mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}} \right]_2, \left[ \mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}} \right]_2 \end{pmatrix}; \\ \mathsf{ct}_x &= \left( \left[ \mathbf{s} \mathbf{A}_1 \right]_1, \left[ \mathbf{s} \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}} \right]_1, \left\{ \left[ \mathbf{s} \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\eta, x_\eta} \right]_1 \right\}_{\eta \in [\ell]}, \left[ \mathbf{s} \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\mathrm{end}} \right]_1, \left[ \mathbf{s} \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{k}^\top \right]_T \cdot m \right). \end{split}$$

We will show a concrete attack when  $\rho$  is non-injective.

Let us consider an NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup>  $\Gamma = (Q, \ell_{\mathrm{BP}}, \ell, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma}\}_{j \in [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \rho, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f})$  where  $Q = 2, \ell_{\mathrm{BP}} = 2, \ell = 1, \Sigma = \{a, b\}, \ell \in \mathbb{N}$ 

$$\mathbf{M}_{1,a} = \mathbf{M}_{1,b} = \mathbf{M}_{2,b} = \mathbf{I}, \quad \mathbf{M}_{2,a} = \begin{pmatrix} 0 & 1 \\ 1 & 0 \end{pmatrix} = \mathbf{P}, \quad \mathbf{u} = \mathbf{f} = \mathbf{e}_1, \quad \rho(1) = \rho(2) = 1$$

and an input x = a. Then we have mpk, key for  $\Gamma$  and ciphertext for x as follows:

$$\mathsf{mpk} = \big( [\mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}}, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_a, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_b, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{end}}]_1, [\mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T \big);$$

$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma} = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{D}_{0}\mathbf{e}_{1}^{\top} + \mathbf{W}_{start}\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_{2}, [\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_{2} \\ [\mathbf{K}_{1,a}]_{2} = [\mathbf{D}_{1} - \mathbf{D}_{0} + \mathbf{W}_{a}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \\ [\mathbf{K}_{1,b}]_{2} = [\mathbf{D}_{1} - \mathbf{D}_{0} + \mathbf{W}_{b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \\ [\mathbf{K}_{2,a}]_{2} = [\mathbf{D}_{2}\mathbf{P} - \mathbf{D}_{1} + \mathbf{W}_{a}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \\ [\mathbf{K}_{2,b}]_{2} = [\mathbf{D}_{2} - \mathbf{D}_{1} + \mathbf{W}_{b}\mathbf{R}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}]_{2} \\ [\mathbf{k}^{\top}\mathbf{e}_{1} - \mathbf{D}_{2} + \mathbf{W}_{end}\mathbf{R}_{end}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{end}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}$$

$$\mathsf{ct}_{x} = \left( [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_{1}]_{1}, [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{start}]_{1}, [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{a}]_{1}, [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{end}]_{1}, [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{k}^{\top}]_{T} \cdot m \right).$$

One can check that  $\Gamma(x) = 0$  since  $\mathbf{fM}_{2,a}\mathbf{M}_{1,a}\mathbf{u} = \mathbf{e}_1\begin{pmatrix} 0 & 1 \\ 1 & 0 \end{pmatrix}\mathbf{I}\mathbf{e}_1^{\mathsf{T}} = 0 \mod p$ , which means the secret key  $\mathsf{sk}_\Gamma$  is not supposed to recover message m from  $\mathsf{ct}_x$ . However we show that this is not the case. Normal decryption computes

$$D_0 = [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{D}_0\mathbf{e}_1^{\top}]_T, D_1 = [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1(\mathbf{D}_1 - \mathbf{D}_0)]_T, D_2 = [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1(\mathbf{D}_2\mathbf{P} - \mathbf{D}_1)]_T, D_3 = [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1(\mathbf{k}^{\top}\mathbf{e}_1 - \mathbf{D}_2)]_T.$$

Besides that the shared R allows us to compute more; in particular, we compute:

$$[\mathbf{K}]_2 = [(\mathbf{K}_{2,b} - \mathbf{K}_{1,b}) - (\mathbf{K}_{2,a} - \mathbf{K}_{1,a})]_2 = [\mathbf{D}_2 - \mathbf{D}_2 \mathbf{P}]_2$$
 and  $K = e([\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1]_1, [\mathbf{K}]_2) = [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1(\mathbf{D}_2 - \mathbf{D}_2 \mathbf{P})]_T$ 

This allows us to compute

$$D_2' = [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1(\mathbf{D}_2 - \mathbf{D}_2\mathbf{P}) + \mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1(\mathbf{D}_2\mathbf{P} - \mathbf{D}_1)]_T = [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1(\mathbf{D}_2 - \mathbf{D}_1)]_T$$

and recover  $[\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T$  from  $D_0, D_1, D_2', D_3$ :

$$[\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T = [\overbrace{\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{D}_0\mathbf{e}_1^{\mathsf{T}}}^{D_0} + \overbrace{\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1(\mathbf{D}_1 - \mathbf{D}_0)}^{D_1} \mathbf{e}_1^{\mathsf{T}} + \overbrace{\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1(\mathbf{D}_2 - \mathbf{D}_1)}^{D_2'} \mathbf{e}_1^{\mathsf{T}} + \overbrace{\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1(\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{e}_1 - \mathbf{D}_2)}^{D_3} \mathbf{e}_1^{\mathsf{T}}]_T.$$

### <span id="page-66-0"></span>G.2 Missing Proof in Section 6.3

In this section, we prove that  $G_0 \approx_c G_1$  and the advantage of adversary in  $G_3$  is 0. All games are defined in Section 6.3.

**Lemma 53** ( $G_0 \approx_c G_1$ ). For all A, there exists B with  $Time(B) \approx Time(A)$  such that

$$Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_0 \rangle = 1] - Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_1 \rangle = 1] \leq \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathrm{SD}_{A_1 \mapsto A_1, a_2}}(\lambda).$$

*Proof (sketch).* This relies on  $\mathrm{SD}_{\mathbf{A}_1 \mapsto \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{a}_2}^{G_1}$  assumption which implies

$$([\mathbf{A}_1]_1, [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1]_1) \approx_c ([\mathbf{A}_1]_1, [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1 + s\mathbf{a}_2]_1)$$

where  $\mathbf{s} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  and  $s \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ . Let  $x^*$  be the selective challenge, the reduction algorithm is sketched as follows:

- we sample  $\mathbf{k}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\text{start}}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\eta,\sigma}$ ,  $\mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}$  for all  $\eta \in [\ell]$ ,  $\sigma \in \Sigma$  and create (mpk, msk) honestly using  $[\mathbf{A}_1]_1$ .
- on key query Γ, we honestly run  $sk_{\Gamma}$  ← KeyGen(mpk, msk, Γ) using mpk and msk;
- on input challenge query  $(m_0, m_1)$ , we sample  $\beta$  and create the challenge ciphertext using the term given out in the statement above.

### **Lemma 54** (Advantage in $G_3$ ). For all A, we have

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_3 \rangle = 1] = 1/2.$$

*Proof* (*sketch*). First, we argue that the secret key  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^*$  perfectly hides the  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -component of  $\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}$ , i.e.,  $\alpha = \mathbf{a}_2 \mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}$ . Recall the  $\mathbf{a}_2$ -components of the key

$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^*[2] = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}_0 \mathbf{u}^\top + \mathbf{w}_{start} \mathbf{r}^\top]_2, [\mathbf{r}^\top]_2 \\ \left\{ [\mathbf{d}_j \mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_j]_2, [\mathbf{R}_j]_2 \right\}_{j \in [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}], \sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} + \boxed{\Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}} - \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}} \mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2 \end{pmatrix}$$

We observe that it only leaks  $\alpha + \Delta$  which means that the key perfectly hides  $\alpha$ . Therefore, the unique term involving  $\mathbf{k}$  in  $\mathsf{ct}_{x^*}^*$ , i.e.,  $[\mathbf{sA}_1\mathbf{k}^\top + s\mathbf{a}_2\mathbf{k}^\top]_T$ , is independently and uniformly distributed and thus statistically hides message  $m_\beta$ .  $\square$ 

### <span id="page-67-0"></span>G.3 Missing Proof in Section 6.4

We show that the core lemma, Lemma 30, implies  $G_{2,\kappa-1} \approx_c G_{2,\kappa}$  for all  $\kappa \in [q]$ .

**Lemma 55** (**Lemma 30**  $\Rightarrow$   $G_{2,\kappa-1} \approx_c G_{2,\kappa}$ ). For all  $\kappa \in [q]$  and all A, there exists B with  $Time(B) \approx Time(A)$  and

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa-1} \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa} \rangle = 1] \leq \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{CORE}}_{\mathcal{B}}(\lambda)$$

where  $Adv_{\mathcal{B}}^{CORE}(\lambda)$  is defined in Lemma 30.

*Proof* (sketch). By Lemma 4, we only focus on  $a_2$ -components. On input aux, reduction  $\mathcal B$  works as follows:

- On input  $\Gamma$ , it proceeds as follows:
  - $\circ$  for the  $\kappa$ 'th query, return the result of oracle query  $OKey(\Gamma)$ ;
  - $\circ$  for the remaining queries, output  $\mathsf{sk}_\Gamma[2]$  or  $\mathsf{sk}_\Gamma^*[2]$  which can be created from aux;
- On input  $(x^*, m_0, m_1)$ , make an oracle query  $\mathsf{OEnc}(x^*)$  and create the challenge ciphertext with the help of aux.

Observe that, if  $\mathsf{OKey}(\Gamma)$  outputs  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}[2]$ , the simulation is identical to  $\mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa-1}$ ; if  $\mathsf{OKey}(\Gamma)$  outputs  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}^*[2]$ , the simulation is identical to  $\mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa}$ . This completes the proof.

## <span id="page-67-1"></span>G.4 Detailed Proofs of Neighbor Indistinguishability

This section provides the detailed for proving Lemma 32 restated below. The proofs are similar to those for selective security in Section 6.3.

**Lemma 56** (Neighbor indistinguishability). For all  $xxx \in \{0,2\} \cup \{1.i.i' : i \in [\ell_{BP}], i' \in [2]\}$ ,  $u_0, u_1 \in I \times \mathcal{E}_Q$  and all  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists  $\mathcal{B}$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{A})$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^0_{\times\!\times\!\times}(u_0,u_1)\rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^1_{\times\!\times\!\times}(u_0,u_1)\rangle = 1] \leq O(|\Sigma|^2) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}^{k\text{-Lin}}_{\mathcal{B}}(\lambda).$$

**Initializing.** We prove the following lemma stating that  $\widehat{H}_0^0(u_0, u_1) \approx_c \widehat{H}_0^1(u_0, u_1)$  for all  $u_0, u_1$ . This is analogous to Lemma 25.

**Lemma 57.** For all  $u_0, u_1 \in I \times \mathcal{E}_Q$  and all A, we have

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_0^0(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] = \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_0^1(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1]$$

*Proof* (*sketch*). We consider the case that the adversary adaptively chooses  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$  in the hybrids parameterized by

$$u_0 = (\boxed{\bot, \bot}), \ u_1 = (\boxed{\{0\}, \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}});$$

the lemma trivially holds in all other cases. Roughly, in this case, we prove

$$\left(\mathsf{aux},\mathsf{OEnc}(x^*), \boxed{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}[2]}\right) = \left(\mathsf{aux},\mathsf{OEnc}(x^*), \boxed{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}}^0[2]}\right)$$

where we have

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}[2] &= \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}_0\mathbf{u}^{\top}] + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2, [\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2 \\ \big\{ [\mathbf{d}_j\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_j]_2, [\mathbf{R}_j]_2 \big\}_{j \in [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}], \sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2 \end{pmatrix}, \\ \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}}^0[2] &= \begin{pmatrix} [(\mathbf{d}_0 + \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*})\mathbf{u}^{\top}] + \mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2, [\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2 \\ \big\{ [\mathbf{d}_j\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_j]_2, [\mathbf{R}_j]_2 \big\}_{j \in [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}], \sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2 \end{pmatrix} \end{split}$$

and

$$\underbrace{[\mathbf{B}, \{\mathbf{w}_{\eta, \sigma}\mathbf{B}\}_{\eta \in [\ell], \sigma \in \Sigma}]_2, \alpha, \Delta, \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{w}_{\text{end}} }_{\text{aud}} \quad \text{and} \quad \underbrace{\{\mathbf{w}_{\eta, x_n^*}\}_{\eta \in [\ell]}}_{\text{}}.$$

The lemma immediately follows from the fact  $\Gamma(x^*) = 0 \iff \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} = 0 \mod p$ , see Lemma 24.

**Key switching I.** We will prove that  $\widehat{H}^0_{1,i,1}(u_0,u_1) \approx_s \widehat{H}^1_{1,i,1}(u_0,u_1)$  and  $\widehat{H}^0_2(u_0,u_1) \approx_s \widehat{H}^1_2(u_0,u_1)$  for all  $i \in [\ell_{BP}]$  and all  $u_0,u_1$ . The proofs for them are similar. We begin with the following lemma stating that  $\widehat{H}^0_{1,1,1}(u_0,u_1) \approx_s \widehat{H}^1_{1,1,1}(u_0,u_1)$  for all  $u_0,u_1$ , which is analogous to Lemma 26, and sketch the proof for remaining statements.

**Lemma 58.** For all  $u_0, u_1 \in I \times \mathcal{E}_O$  and all A, we have

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_{1,1,1}^0(u_0,u_1)\rangle = 1] \approx \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_{1,1,1}^1(u_0,u_1)\rangle = 1].$$

*Proof.* We consider the case that the adversary adaptively chooses  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$  in the hybrids parameterized by

$$u_0 = ( \boxed{\{0\}}, \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}), \ u_1 = ( \boxed{\{0,1\}}, \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*});$$

the lemma trivially holds in all other cases. Roughly, in this case, we prove that

$$\left(\mathsf{aux},\mathsf{OEnc}(x^*), \overline{\mathsf{sk}^0_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}}[2]}\right) = \left(\mathsf{aux},\mathsf{OEnc}(x^*), \overline{\mathsf{sk}^{0,1}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}}[2]}\right).$$

More concretely, this means that

$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{0,x^*}}^{0}[2] = \begin{pmatrix} [(\mathbf{d}_{0} + \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{0,x^*})]\mathbf{u}^{\top} + \mathbf{w}_{start}\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_{2}, [\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_{2} \\ \{[\mathbf{d}_{1}\mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}(\mathbf{d}_{0})] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \{[\mathbf{d}_{1}\mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}(\mathbf{d}_{0})] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}\}_{j \neq 1,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [(\mathbf{d}_{1}\mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}(\mathbf{d}_{0})] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}\}_{j \neq 1,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [(\mathbf{d}_{1}\mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}(\mathbf{d}_{0})] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}\}_{j \neq 1,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [(\mathbf{d}_{1}\mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}(\mathbf{d}_{0})] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}\}_{j \neq 1,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [(\mathbf{d}_{1}\mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}(\mathbf{d}_{0})] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}\}_{j \neq 1,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [(\mathbf{d}_{1}\mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}(\mathbf{d}_{0})] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}\}_{j \neq 1,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [(\mathbf{d}_{1}\mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}(\mathbf{d}_{0})] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}\}_{j \neq 1,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [(\mathbf{d}_{1}\mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}(\mathbf{d}_{0})] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}\}_{j \neq 1,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [(\mathbf{d}_{1}\mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}(\mathbf{d}_{0})] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}\}_{j \neq 1,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [(\mathbf{d}_{1}\mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}(\mathbf{d}_{0})] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}\}_{j \neq 1,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [(\mathbf{d}_{1}\mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}(\mathbf{d}_{0})] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}\}_{j \neq 1,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [(\mathbf{d}_{1}\mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}(\mathbf{d}_{0})] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}\}_{j \neq 1,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [(\mathbf{d}_{1}\mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}(\mathbf{d}_{0})] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}\}_{j \neq 1,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [(\mathbf{d}_{1}\mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}(\mathbf{d}_{0})] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}\}_{j \neq 1,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [(\mathbf{d}_{1}\mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}(\mathbf{d}_{0})] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}\}_{j \neq 1,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [(\mathbf{d}_{1}\mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}(\mathbf{d}_{0})] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}\}_{j \neq 1,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [(\mathbf{d}_{1}\mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}(\mathbf{d}_{0})] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}\}_{j \neq 1,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [(\mathbf{d}_{1}\mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}(\mathbf{d}_{0})] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}\}_{j \neq 1,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [(\mathbf{d}_{1}\mathbf{M}_{1,\sigma}(\mathbf{d}_{0})] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(1),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{1}]_{2$$

given

$$\underbrace{[\mathbf{B}, \{\mathbf{w}_{\eta,\sigma}\mathbf{B}\}_{\eta \in [\ell], \sigma \in \Sigma}]_2, \alpha, \Delta, \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{w}_{\text{end}}}_{\text{and}} \quad \text{and} \quad \underbrace{\{\mathbf{w}_{\eta, x_{\eta}^*}\}_{\eta \in [\ell]}}_{\text{OEnc}(x^*)}$$

This immediately follows from change of variables  $\boldsymbol{d}_0 \mapsto \boldsymbol{d}_0 - \Delta \cdot \boldsymbol{f}_{0,x^*}$ 

Via the same proof idea, we can prove the following two lemmas stating that  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}^0_{1.i.1}(u_0,u_1) \approx_c \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^1_{1.i.1}(u_0,u_1)$  for all  $i \in [2,\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}]$  and  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}^0_2(u_0,u_1) \approx_c \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^1_2(u_0,u_1)$ , respectively. The first lemma relies on change of variable  $\mathbf{d}_{i-1} \mapsto \mathbf{d}_{i-1} - \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}$ ; while the second lemma relies on change of variable  $\mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} \mapsto \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} \to \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}},x^*}$ . We give the lemmas but omit the proofs.

**Lemma 59.** For all  $i \in [2, \ell_{BP}]$ ,  $u_0, u_1 \in I \times \mathcal{E}_Q$  and all  $\mathcal{A}$ , we have

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^0_{1,i,1}(u_0,u_1)\rangle = 1] \approx \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^1_{1,i,1}(u_0,u_1)\rangle = 1].$$

**Lemma 60.** For all  $u_0$ ,  $u_1 \in I \times \mathcal{E}_Q$  and all A, we have

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_2^0(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] \approx \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}_2^1(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1].$$

**Key switching II.** We prove the following lemma stating that  $\widehat{H}^0_{1.i.2}(u_0, u_1) \approx_c \widehat{H}^1_{1.i.2}(u_0, u_1)$  for all  $i \in [\ell_{BP}]$  and all  $u_0, u_1$ . This is analogous to Lemma 29.

**Lemma 61.** For all  $i \in [\ell_{BP}]$ ,  $u_0, u_1 \in I \times \mathcal{E}_O$  and all  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists  $\mathcal{B}$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{A})$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^0_{1.i.2}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \widehat{\mathsf{H}}^1_{1.i.2}(u_0, u_1) \rangle = 1] \leq O(|\Sigma|^2) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathrm{DDH}^{G_2}_{1,Q}}(\lambda).$$

*Proof.* We consider the case that the adversary adaptively chooses  $\Gamma$  and  $x^*$  in the hybrids parameterized by

$$u_0 = (\boxed{\{i-1,i\},\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}}),\ u_1 = (\boxed{\{i\},\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}});$$

the lemma trivially holds in other cases. Roughly, we prove that

$$\left(\mathsf{aux}, \mathsf{OEnc}(x^*), \boxed{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma, \mathbf{f}_{i-1, x^*}}^{i-1, i}[2]}\right) \approx_c \left(\mathsf{aux}, \mathsf{OEnc}(x^*), \boxed{\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma, \mathbf{f}_{i, x^*}}^{i}[2]}\right)$$

which means:

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}}^{i-1,i}[2] \; &= \; \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}_0\mathbf{u}^\top + \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}\mathbf{r}^\top]_2, [\mathbf{r}^\top]_2 \\ \big\{ [\mathbf{d}_i\mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{i-1} + \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}] + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_i]_2, [\mathbf{R}_i]_2 \big\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \big\{ [\mathbf{d}_j\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_j]_2, [\mathbf{R}_j]_2 \big\}_{j \neq i,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \big[ \alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2 \end{pmatrix} \\ \approx_c \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}_0\mathbf{u}^\top + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{start}}\mathbf{r}^\top]_2, [\mathbf{r}^\top]_2 \\ \big\{ [\mathbf{d}_i\mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{i-1} + \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}\mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_i]_2, [\mathbf{R}_i]_2 \big\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ \big\{ [\mathbf{d}_j\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_j]_2, [\mathbf{R}_j]_2 \big\}_{j \neq i,\sigma \in \Sigma} \end{pmatrix} = \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}}^i[2]; \\ \big[ \alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2 \end{pmatrix} \end{split}$$

in the presence of

$$\underbrace{[\mathbf{B}, \{\mathbf{w}_{\eta,\sigma}\mathbf{B}\}_{\eta\in[\ell],\sigma\in\Sigma}]_2, \alpha, \Delta, \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{w}_{\text{end}} }_{\text{aux}} \quad \text{and} \quad \underbrace{\{\mathbf{w}_{\eta,x_n^*}\}_{\eta\in[\ell]}}_{\{\mathbf{w}_{\eta,x_n^*}\}_{\eta\in[\ell]}}$$

We randomly guess  $x_{\rho(i)}^* \leftarrow \Sigma$ , which causes a multiplicative security loss of  $|\Sigma|$ , and prove this using the following statement implied by  $DDH_{1:O}^{G_2}$  assumption: for all  $\Delta \in \mathbb{Z}_p$ , we have

$$\left\{ [\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}\mathbf{B}]_2, [\mathbf{B}]_2, [\Delta \cdot \boxed{\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_i]_2, [\mathbf{R}_i]_2 \right\}_{\sigma \neq x^*_{\rho(i)}} \approx_c \left\{ [\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}\mathbf{B}]_2, [\mathbf{B}]_2, [\Delta \cdot \boxed{\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}\mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma}} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_i]_2, [\mathbf{R}_i]_2 \right\}_{\sigma \neq x^*_{\rho(i)}}$$

where  $\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$ ,  $\mathbf{B} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times k}$  and  $\mathbf{R}_i \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times Q}$ . On input  $\left\{ [\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \mathbf{B}]_2, [\mathbf{B}]_2, [\mathbf{t}_{\sigma}]_2, [\mathbf{R}_i]_2 \right\}_{\sigma \neq x_{\sigma(i)}^*}$  where

$$\mathbf{t}_{\sigma} = \Delta \cdot \boxed{\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_i \text{ or } \mathbf{t}_{\sigma} = \Delta \cdot \boxed{\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma}} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_i$$

we sample  $\alpha \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),x_{\sigma(i)}^*}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\text{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  and  $\mathbf{w}_{\eta,\sigma} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  for all  $\eta \neq \rho(i)$ ,  $\sigma \in \Sigma$  and proceed as follows:

(Simulating aux) We can trivially simulate aux using  $\Delta$ ,  $\{[\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}\mathbf{B}]_2, [\mathbf{B}]_2\}_{\sigma \neq x_{\rho(i)}^*}$  given in the lemma and  $\alpha$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\text{end}}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),x_{\rho(i)}^*}$ ,  $\{\mathbf{w}_{\eta,\sigma}\}_{\eta\neq\rho(i),\sigma\in\Sigma}$  sampled by ourselves.

(Answering OEnc) On input  $x^*$ , we can answer OEnc( $x^*$ ) using the knowledge of  $\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),x_{\sigma(i)}^*}$  and  $\{\mathbf{w}_{\eta,x_{\eta}^*}\}_{\eta\neq\rho(i)}$ . Here we use the fact that the oracle does not involve  $\{\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}\}_{\sigma \neq x_{\sigma(i)}^*}$ .

(**Answering** OKey) On input  $\Gamma$ , we want to simulate secret key in the form:

$$\begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}_0\mathbf{u}^\top + \mathbf{w}_{start}\mathbf{r}^\top]_2, [\mathbf{r}^\top]_2 \\ \left\{ [\mathbf{d}_i\mathbf{M}_{i,x_{\rho(i)}^*} - \mathbf{d}_{i-1} + \Delta \cdot \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),x_{\rho(i)}^*} \mathbf{R}_i]_2, [\mathbf{R}_i]_2 \right\} \\ \left\{ [\mathbf{d}_i\mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{i-1} + \mathbf{t}_{\sigma}]_2, [\mathbf{R}_i]_2 \right\}_{\sigma \neq x_{\rho(i)}^*} \\ \left\{ [\mathbf{d}_j\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_j]_2, [\mathbf{R}_j]_2 \right\}_{j \neq i,\sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [\alpha \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2 \end{pmatrix}$$

Observe that,

- $\text{ when } \mathbf{t}_{\sigma} = \Delta \cdot \boxed{\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_i, \text{ the distribution is identical to } \begin{bmatrix} \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}}^{i-1,i} [2] \end{bmatrix};$   $\text{ when } \mathbf{t}_{\sigma} = \Delta \cdot \boxed{\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma}} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_i, \text{ the distribution is identical to } \begin{bmatrix} \mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}}^{i} [2] \end{bmatrix};$   $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}}^{i} [2] \quad \mathsf{since } \mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*} = \mathbf{f}_{i,x^*} \mathbf{M}_{i,x^*_{\rho(i)}} \mod p, \text{ see } t$

We sample  $\mathbf{d}_0, \dots, \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{PR}}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_n^{1 \times Q}$  and simulate the key as follows:

- We simulate the terms in the second row using  $[\mathbf{R}_i]_2$  and  $\mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),x_{o(i)}^*}$ ;
- We simulate the terms in the third row using  $[\mathbf{t}_{\sigma}]_2$  and  $[\mathbf{R}_i]_2$ ;

- All remaining terms can be simulated using aux.

Observe that, when  $\mathbf{t}_{\sigma} = \Delta \cdot \boxed{\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_i$ , oracle OKey( $\Gamma$ ) returns  $\boxed{\mathbf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{i-1,x^*}}^{i-1,i}[2]}$  and the simulation is identical to  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_{1.i.2}^0(u_0,u_1)$ ; when  $\mathbf{t}_{\sigma} = \Delta \cdot \boxed{\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}\mathbf{M}_{i,\sigma}} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(i),\sigma}\mathbf{R}_i$ , oracle OKey( $\Gamma$ ) returns  $\boxed{\mathbf{sk}_{\Gamma,\mathbf{f}_{i,x^*}}^i[2]}$  and the simulation is identical to  $\widehat{\mathsf{H}}_{1.i.2}^1(u_0,u_1)$ . This completes the proof.

## <span id="page-70-0"></span>H Concrete ABE for Branching Program with Adaptive Security

In this section, we show our compact adaptively secure ABE for branching program (BP). This is derived from our adaptively secure ABE for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> in Section 6.2 and the transformation from BP to  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> in Section 6.1, see Lemma 23.

- Setup $(1^{\lambda}, \ell, \Sigma)$ : Run  $\mathbb{G} = (p, G_1, G_2, G_T, e) \leftarrow \mathcal{G}(1^{\lambda})$ . Sample

$$\mathbf{A}_1 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times (k+1)}, \mathbf{k} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times (k+1)} \quad \text{and} \quad \mathbf{W}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{W}_{\eta, \sigma}, \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+1) \times k}, \, \forall \, \eta \in [\ell], \sigma \in \Sigma.$$

Output

$$\begin{aligned} \mathsf{mpk} &= \left( \left[ \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}}, \left\{ \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\eta, \sigma} \right\}_{\eta \in [\ell], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{end}} \right]_1, \left[ \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{k}^\mathsf{T} \right]_T \right) \\ \mathsf{msk} &= \left( \mathbf{k}, \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}}, \left\{ \mathbf{W}_{\eta, \sigma} \right\}_{\eta \in [\ell], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{end}} \right). \end{aligned}$$

– Enc(mpk, x, m): Let  $x = (x_1, \dots, x_\ell) \in \Sigma^\ell$  and  $m \in G_T$ . Pick  $\mathbf{s} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  and output

$$\mathsf{ct}_x = \left( [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1]_1, [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}}]_1, \left\{ [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{W}_{\eta, x_{\eta}}]_1 \right\}_{\eta \in [\ell]}, [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{end}}]_1, [\mathbf{s}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{k}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T \cdot m \right).$$

– KeyGen(mpk, msk,  $\Gamma$ ): Let  $\Gamma = (Q, \ell_{\mathrm{BP}}, \ell, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma}\}_{j \in [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \rho, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f})$ . Pick

$$\mathbf{D}_0, \mathbf{D}_1, \dots, \mathbf{D}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+1) \times Q}, \ \mathbf{R}_1, \dots, \mathbf{R}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}}, \mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times Q}, \ \mathbf{r} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$$

output

$$\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma} = \left( \{ [\mathbf{D}_{j} \mathbf{M}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}+1-j,\sigma}^{\top} - \mathbf{D}_{j-1} + \mathbf{W}_{\rho(\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}+1-j),\sigma} \mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{j}]_{2} \}_{j \in [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}],\sigma \in \Sigma} \right).$$
$$[\mathbf{k}^{\top} \mathbf{u} - \mathbf{D}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{W}_{\mathrm{end}} \mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathrm{end}}]_{2}$$

- Dec(mpk,  $\mathsf{sk}_{\Gamma}$ ,  $\mathsf{ct}_x$ ): Parse ciphertext for  $x = (x_1, \dots, x_\ell)$  and key for  $\Gamma = (Q, \ell_{\mathsf{BP}}, \ell, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma}\}_{j \in [\ell_{\mathsf{BP}}], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \rho, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f})$  as

$$\mathsf{ct}_x = \left( [\mathbf{c}]_1, [\mathbf{c}_{\mathsf{start}}]_1, \left\{ [\mathbf{c}_{\eta}]_1 \right\}_{\eta \in [\ell]}, [\mathbf{c}_{\mathsf{end}}]_1, C \right) \quad \text{and} \quad \mathsf{sk}_\Gamma = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{k}_{\mathsf{start}}^\top]_2, [\mathbf{r}^\top]_2 \\ \left\{ [\mathbf{K}_{j,\sigma}]_2, [\mathbf{R}_j]_2 \right\}_{j,\sigma} \\ [\mathbf{K}_{\mathsf{end}}]_2, [\mathbf{R}_{\mathsf{end}}]_2 \end{pmatrix}.$$

We define  $\mathbf{f}_{j,x}$  for all  $j \in [0, \ell_{\mathrm{BP}}]$  as (39) and proceed as follows:

1. Compute

$$B_{\text{start}} = e([\mathbf{c}]_1, [\mathbf{k}_{\text{start}}^{\top}]_2) \cdot e([\mathbf{c}_{\text{start}}]_1, [\mathbf{r}^{\top}]_2)^{-1};$$

2. For all  $j \in [\ell_{BP}]$ , compute

$$[\mathbf{b}_j]_T = e([\mathbf{c}]_1, [\mathbf{K}_{j,x_{\rho(\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}+1-j)}}]_2) \cdot e([-\mathbf{c}_{\rho(\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}+1-j)}]_1, [\mathbf{R}_j]_2) \quad \text{and} \quad B_j = [\mathbf{b}_j \mathbf{f}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}+1-j,x}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T;$$

3. Compute

$$[\mathbf{b}_{\mathrm{end}}]_T = e([\mathbf{c}]_1, [\mathbf{K}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2) \cdot e([-\mathbf{c}_{\mathrm{end}}]_1, [\mathbf{R}]_2)$$
 and  $B_{\mathrm{end}} = [\mathbf{b}_{\mathrm{end}} \mathbf{f}_{0,x}^T]_T$ ;

4. Compute

$$B_{\text{all}} = B_{\text{start}} \cdot \prod_{i=j}^{\ell_{\text{BP}}} B_j \cdot B_{\text{end}}$$
 and  $B = B_{\text{all}}^{(\mathbf{uf}_{0,x}^{\mathsf{T}})^{-1}}$ 

and output the message  $m' \leftarrow C \cdot B^{-1}$ .

## <span id="page-71-0"></span>I Adaptively Secure CP-ABE for $\mathcal{E}_{O}$ -restricted NFA $^{\oplus p}$ and DFA

In this section, we construct adaptively secure CP-ABE for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NFA $^{\oplus p}$  from k-Lin assumption. The scheme is based on our adaptively secure KP-ABE for the same class in Section 5 and dual conversion in [4,6]. This readily gives us an adaptively secure CP-ABE for DFA by Lemma 1.

#### I.1 Basis

We will use the following two sets of bases for ciphertexts and keys, respectively:

$$\mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{A}_2 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{2k \times k} \quad \text{and} \quad (\mathbf{B}_1, \mathbf{B}_2) \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times (3k+1)} \times \mathbb{Z}_p^{(2k+1) \times (3k+1)}.$$

We use  $\mathbf{A}_1^{\perp}, \mathbf{A}_2^{\perp} \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times 2k}$  to denote the dual basis of  $(\mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{A}_2)$  such that  $\mathbf{A}_i^{\perp} \mathbf{A}_i = \mathbf{I}$  for  $i \in \{1, 2\}$  and  $\mathbf{A}_i^{\perp} \mathbf{A}_j = \mathbf{0}$  for  $i \neq j$ . Analogously, we use  $(\mathbf{B}_1^{\perp}, \mathbf{B}_2^{\perp}) \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{(3k+1) \times k} \times \mathbb{Z}_p^{(3k+1) \times (2k+1)}$  to denote the dual basis of  $(\mathbf{B}_1, \mathbf{B}_2)$ . In the proof, we will use  $\mathrm{SD}_{\mathbf{A}_1 \to \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{A}_2}^{G_2}$  and  $\mathrm{SD}_{\mathbf{B}_1 \to \mathbf{B}_1, \mathbf{B}_2}^{G_1}$  assumption, cf. Section 4.1.

### <span id="page-71-1"></span>I.2 Scheme

For notational convenience, especially reusing NFA notations in Section 5, we will generate ciphertexts over  $G_2$  and keys over  $G_1$ . Our CP-ABE for  $\mathcal{E}_O$ -restricted NFA<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> in prime-order groups is described as follows:

- Setup $(1^{\lambda}, \Sigma)$ : Run  $\mathbb{G} = (p, G_1, G_2, G_T, e) \leftarrow \mathcal{G}(1^{\lambda})$ . Sample

$$\mathbf{A}_1 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{2k \times k}, \mathbf{B}_1 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times (3k+1)}, \mathbf{k} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times 2k} \quad \text{and} \quad \mathbf{W}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{Z}_0, \mathbf{Z}_1, \mathbf{W}_0, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1}, \mathbf{Z}_{\text{end}}, \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(3k+1) \times 2k}, \ \forall \sigma \in \Sigma.$$

Output

$$\begin{aligned} & \mathsf{mpk} = \left( \left[ \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{W}_{start} \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{Z}_0 \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{Z}_1 \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{W}_0 \mathbf{A}_1, \left\{ \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0} \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1} \mathbf{A}_1 \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{Z}_{end} \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{W}_{end} \mathbf{A}_1 \right]_2, \left[ \mathbf{k} \mathbf{A}_1 \right]_T \right) \\ & \mathsf{msk} = \left( \mathbf{k}, \mathbf{B}_1, \mathbf{W}_{start}, \mathbf{Z}_0, \mathbf{Z}_1, \mathbf{W}_0, \left\{ \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,0}, \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,1} \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{Z}_{end}, \mathbf{W}_{end} \right). \end{aligned}$$

-  $\mathsf{Enc}(\mathsf{mpk},\Gamma,m)$ : Let  $\Gamma = (Q,\Sigma,\{\mathbf{M}_\sigma\}_{\sigma\in\Sigma},\mathbf{u},\mathbf{f})$  and  $m\in G_T$ . Pick  $\mathbf{D}\leftarrow\mathbb{Z}_p^{(3k+1)\times Q},\,\mathbf{S}\leftarrow\mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times Q},\,\mathbf{s}\leftarrow\mathbb{Z}_p^{1\times k}$  and output

$$\mathsf{ct}_{\Gamma} = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{D}\mathbf{u}^{\top} + \mathbf{W}_{start}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{S}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2}, [\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{S}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2} \\ \{[-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{Z}_{b}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{S}]_{2}, [\mathbf{D}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,b}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{S}]_{2}, [\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{S}]_{2}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0,1\}} \\ [-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{Z}_{end}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{S}]_{2}, [(\mathbf{W}_{0}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{s}^{\top})\mathbf{f} + \mathbf{W}_{end}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{S}]_{2}, [\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{S}]_{2} \\ [\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{s}^{\top}]_{2}, [\mathbf{k}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{s}^{\top}]_{T} \cdot m \end{pmatrix}.$$

- KeyGen(mpk, msk, x): Let  $x = (x_1, \dots, x_\ell) \in \Sigma^\ell$ . Pick  $\mathbf{r}_0, \mathbf{r}_1, \dots, \mathbf{r}_\ell, \mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  and output

$$\mathsf{sk}_{x} = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{r}_{0}\mathbf{B}_{1}]_{1}, [\mathbf{r}_{0}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{start}]_{1} \\ \{[\mathbf{r}_{j}\mathbf{B}_{1}]_{1}, [\mathbf{r}_{j-1}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{Z}_{j \bmod 2} + \mathbf{r}_{j}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{x_{j}, j \bmod 2}]_{1}\}_{j \in [\ell]} \\ [\mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{1}]_{1}, [\mathbf{r}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{Z}_{end} + \mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{end}]_{1} \\ [\mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{0} + \mathbf{k}]_{1} \end{pmatrix}.$$

- Dec(mpk, sk<sub>x</sub>, ct<sub> $\Gamma$ </sub>): Parse key for  $x = (x_1, ..., x_\ell)$  and ciphertext for  $\Gamma = (Q, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_\sigma\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f})$  as

$$\mathsf{sk}_{x} = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{k}_{0,1}]_{1}, [\mathbf{k}_{0,2}]_{1} \\ \{[\mathbf{k}_{j,1}]_{1}, [\mathbf{k}_{j,2}]_{1}\}_{j} \\ [\mathbf{k}_{\mathrm{end},1}]_{1}, [\mathbf{k}_{\mathrm{end},2}]_{1} \\ [\mathbf{k}_{\mathrm{end}}]_{1} \end{pmatrix} \quad \text{and} \quad \mathsf{ct}_{\Gamma} = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{c}_{0,1}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{c}_{0,2}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \{[\mathbf{C}_{b}]_{2}, [\mathbf{C}_{\sigma,b}]_{2}, [\mathbf{C}]_{2}\}_{\sigma,b} \\ [\mathbf{C}_{\mathrm{end},1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{C}_{\mathrm{end},2}]_{2}, [\mathbf{C}]_{2} \\ [\mathbf{c}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, C \end{pmatrix}.$$

We define

$$\mathbf{u}_{j,x}^{\top} = \mathbf{M}_{x_j} \cdots \mathbf{M}_{x_1} \mathbf{u}^{\top} \bmod p, \ \forall j \in [0, \ell]$$

as (11) in Section 4.2 and proceed as follows:

1. Compute

$$B_0 = e([\mathbf{k}_{0,1}]_1, [\mathbf{c}_{0,1}^\top]_2) \cdot e([\mathbf{k}_{0,2}]_1, [\mathbf{c}_{0,2}^\top]_2)^{-1};$$

2. For all  $j \in [\ell]$ , compute

$$[\mathbf{b}_j]_T = e([\mathbf{k}_{j-1,1}]_1, [\mathbf{C}_{j \bmod 2}]_2) \cdot e([\mathbf{k}_{j,1}]_1, [\mathbf{C}_{x_j, j \bmod 2}]_2) \cdot e([-\mathbf{k}_{j,2}]_1, [\mathbf{C}]_2) \quad \text{and} \quad B_j = [\mathbf{b}_j \mathbf{u}_{j-1,x}^\top]_T;$$

3. Compute

$$[\mathbf{b}_{\text{end}}]_T = e([\mathbf{k}_{\ell,1}]_1, [\mathbf{C}_{\text{end},1}]_2) \cdot e([\mathbf{k}_{\text{end},1}]_1, [\mathbf{C}_{\text{end},2}]_2) \cdot e([-\mathbf{k}_{\text{end},2}]_1, [\mathbf{C}]_2) \quad \text{and} \quad B_{\text{end}} = [\mathbf{b}_{\text{end}}\mathbf{u}_{\ell,x}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T;$$

4. Compute

$$B_{\text{all}} = B_0 \cdot \prod_{j=1}^{\ell} B_j \cdot B_{\text{end}}$$
 and  $B = B_{\text{all}}^{(\mathbf{fu}_{\ell,x}^{\mathsf{T}})^{-1}}$ 

5. Compute

$$D = e([\mathbf{k}_{\text{end}}]_1, [\mathbf{c}^{\top}]_2) \cdot B^{-1}$$

and output the message  $m' \leftarrow C \cdot D^{-1}$ .

**Correctness.** For  $x = (x_1, ..., x_\ell)$  and  $\Gamma = (Q, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_\sigma\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f})$  such that  $\Gamma(x) = 1$ , we have:

<span id="page-72-0"></span>
$$B_0 = [\mathbf{r}_0 \mathbf{B}_1 \mathbf{D} \mathbf{u}^\top]_T = [\mathbf{r}_0 \mathbf{B}_1 \mathbf{D} \mathbf{u}_0^\top]_T$$
(50)

$$\mathbf{b}_{j} = \mathbf{r}_{j} \mathbf{B}_{1} \mathbf{D} \mathbf{M}_{x_{j}} - \mathbf{r}_{j-1} \mathbf{B}_{1} \mathbf{D}$$
 (51)

$$B_{j} = [\mathbf{r}_{i} \mathbf{B}_{1} \mathbf{D} \mathbf{u}_{i,x}^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathbf{r}_{j-1} \mathbf{B}_{1} \mathbf{D} \mathbf{u}_{i-1,x}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{T}$$

$$(52)$$

$$\mathbf{b}_{\text{end}} = \mathbf{r}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{B}_{1} (\mathbf{W}_{0} \mathbf{A}_{1} \mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}}) \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{r}_{\ell} \mathbf{B}_{1} \mathbf{D}$$
 (53)

$$B_{\text{end}} = [\mathbf{r}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{B}_1 (\mathbf{W}_0 \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}}) \mathbf{f} \mathbf{u}_{\ell,x}^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathbf{r}_{\ell} \mathbf{B}_1 \mathbf{D} \mathbf{u}_{\ell,x}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T$$
(54)

$$B_{\text{all}} = [\mathbf{r}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{B}_{1} (\mathbf{W}_{0} \mathbf{A}_{1} \mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}}) \mathbf{f} \mathbf{u}_{\ell, r}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{T}$$

$$(55)$$

$$B = [\mathbf{r}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{B}_{1} (\mathbf{W}_{0} \mathbf{A}_{1} \mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}})]_{T}$$
(56)

$$D = [\mathbf{k}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T \tag{57}$$

Here (54) is trivial; (52) and (56) follow from facts (19); the remaining equalities follow from:

(50) 
$$\mathbf{r}_0 \mathbf{B}_1 \mathbf{D} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} = \mathbf{r}_0 \mathbf{B}_1 \cdot (\mathbf{D} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}} \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{S} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}) - \mathbf{r}_0 \mathbf{B}_1 \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}} \cdot \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{S} \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}$$

$$(51) \mathbf{r}_{j} \mathbf{B}_{1} \mathbf{D} \mathbf{M}_{x_{j}} - \mathbf{r}_{j-1} \mathbf{B}_{1} \mathbf{D} = \mathbf{r}_{j-1} \mathbf{B}_{1} \cdot (-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{Z}_{j \bmod 2} \mathbf{A}_{1} \mathbf{S}) + \mathbf{r}_{j} \mathbf{B}_{1} \cdot (\mathbf{D} \mathbf{M}_{x_{j}} + \mathbf{W}_{x_{j}, j \bmod 2} \mathbf{A}_{1} \mathbf{S})$$

$$-(\mathbf{r}_{j-1}\mathbf{B}_1\mathbf{Z}_{j \bmod 2} + \mathbf{r}_j\mathbf{B}_1\mathbf{W}_{x_j,j \bmod 2}) \cdot \mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{S}$$

$$(\mathbf{53}) \ \ r_{end} B_{1} (W_{0} A_{1} \mathbf{s}^{\top}) \mathbf{f} - r_{\ell} B_{1} \mathbf{D} = \ \ r_{\ell} B_{1} \cdot (-\mathbf{D} + Z_{end} A_{1} \mathbf{S}) + r_{end} B_{1} \cdot (W_{0} A_{1} \mathbf{s}^{\top} \mathbf{f} + W_{end} A_{1} \mathbf{S}) - (r_{\ell} B_{1} Z_{end} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end}) \cdot A_{1} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1}
