W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf{S} + r_{end} B_{1} W_{end} \mathbf$$

$$\mathbf{r}_{\text{end}}\mathbf{B}_{1}(\mathbf{W}_{0}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}})\mathbf{f}\mathbf{u}_{\ell,x}^{\mathsf{T}} = \mathbf{r}_{0}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{D}\mathbf{u}_{0,x}^{\mathsf{T}} + \sum_{j=1}^{\ell}(\mathbf{r}_{j}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{D}\mathbf{u}_{j,x}^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathbf{r}_{j-1}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{D}\mathbf{u}_{j-1,x}^{\mathsf{T}}) + (\mathbf{r}_{\text{end}}\mathbf{B}_{1}(\mathbf{W}_{0}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}})\mathbf{f}\mathbf{u}_{\ell,x}^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathbf{r}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{D}\mathbf{u}_{\ell,x}^{\mathsf{T}})$$

(57) 
$$\mathbf{k}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}} = (\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{0} + \mathbf{k}) \cdot \mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{0}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}}$$

Correctness follows readily.

### I.3 Adaptive Security

<span id="page-72-1"></span>We prove the following theorem.

**Theorem 6** (Adaptively Secure CP-ABE for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NFA<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup>). The ABE scheme for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NFA<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> in prime-order bilinear groups described in Section 1.2 is adaptively secure (cf. Section 2.1) under the k-Lin assumption with security loss  $O(q \cdot \ell \cdot |\Sigma|^3 \cdot Q^2)$ . Here  $\ell$  is the maximum length of the q-key queries.

The proof employs standard dual system argument where we handle key queries one by one; for each key, we rely on the core lemma, Lemma 19, for our adaptively secure KP-ABE for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NFA<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> (in Section 5). We only show the game sequence and sketch the proof.

**Auxiliary distributions.** We use  $\Gamma^* = (Q, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_{\sigma}\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f})$  to denote the adaptive challenge NFA and  $x = (x_1, \dots, x_{\ell})$  a key query. We describe the auxiliary ciphertext and key distributions that we use in the proof.

*Ciphertext distributions.* We sample  $\hat{\mathbf{S}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times Q}, \hat{\mathbf{s}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  and define:

- N: the real ciphertext in the scheme;
- SF: identical to an N ciphertext except that we replace  $A_1S$  and  $A_1s^{\top}$  with  $A_1S + A_2\hat{S}$  and  $A_1s^{\top} + A_2\hat{S}^{\top}$ , respectively.

That is, we write

$$\mathsf{ct}_{\Gamma^*}^{\mathsf{SF}} = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{D}\mathbf{u}^\top + \mathbf{W}_{start}(\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{S} + \boxed{\mathbf{A}_2\hat{\mathbf{S}}})\mathbf{u}^\top]_2, [(\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{S} + \boxed{\mathbf{A}_2\hat{\mathbf{S}}})\mathbf{u}^\top]_2 \\ \{[-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{Z}_b(\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{S} + \boxed{\mathbf{A}_2\hat{\mathbf{S}}})]_2, [\mathbf{D}\mathbf{M}_\sigma + \mathbf{W}_{\sigma,b}(\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{S} + \boxed{\mathbf{A}_2\hat{\mathbf{S}}})]_2, [\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{S} + \boxed{\mathbf{A}_2\hat{\mathbf{S}}}]_2\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0,1\}} \\ [-\mathbf{D} + \mathbf{Z}_{end}(\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{S} + \boxed{\mathbf{A}_2\hat{\mathbf{S}}})]_2, [(\mathbf{W}_0(\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{s}^\top + \boxed{\mathbf{A}_2\hat{\mathbf{s}}^\top}))\mathbf{f} + \mathbf{W}_{end}(\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{S} + \boxed{\mathbf{A}_2\hat{\mathbf{S}}})]_2, [\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{S} + \boxed{\mathbf{A}_2\hat{\mathbf{S}}}]_2 \\ [\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{s}^\top + \boxed{\mathbf{A}_2\hat{\mathbf{s}}^\top}]_2, [\mathbf{k}(\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{s}^\top + \boxed{\mathbf{A}_2\hat{\mathbf{s}}^\top})]_T \cdot m_\beta \end{pmatrix}.$$

Secret key distributions. We sample  $\Delta \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$ ,  $\hat{\mathbf{r}}_j$ ,  $\hat{\mathbf{r}}_{end} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times (2k+1)}$  for all  $j \in [0, \ell]$  and define

- N: the real key in the scheme;
- SF: identical to an N key except that we replace **k** with  $\Delta A_2^{\perp} + \mathbf{k}$ ;
- P-N: identical to an N key except that we replace  $\mathbf{r}_j \mathbf{B}_1$ ,  $\mathbf{r}_{end} \mathbf{B}_1$  with  $\mathbf{r}_j \mathbf{B}_1 + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_j \mathbf{B}_2$ ,  $\mathbf{r}_{end} \mathbf{B}_1 + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{end} \mathbf{B}_2$ ;
- P-SF: identical to an SF key except that we replace  $\mathbf{r}_i \mathbf{B}_1$ ,  $\mathbf{r}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{B}_1$  with  $\mathbf{r}_i \mathbf{B}_1 + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_i \mathbf{B}_2$ ,  $\mathbf{r}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{B}_1 + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{B}_2$ .

That is, we write

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{sk}_{x}^{\mathsf{SF}} &= \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{r}_{0}\mathbf{B}_{1}]_{1}, [\mathbf{r}_{0}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}}]_{1} \\ \{[\mathbf{r}_{j}\mathbf{B}_{1}]_{1}, [\mathbf{r}_{j-1}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{Z}_{j \bmod 2} + \mathbf{r}_{j}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{x_{j}, j \bmod 2}]_{1}\}_{j \in [\ell]} \\ [\mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{1}]_{1}, [\mathbf{r}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{Z}_{end} + \mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{end}]_{1}, \\ [\mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{0} + \Delta\mathbf{A}_{2}^{\perp}] + \mathbf{k}]_{1} \end{pmatrix}; \\ \mathsf{sk}_{x}^{\mathsf{P-N}} &= \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{r}_{0}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{j}\mathbf{B}_{2}]_{1}, [(\mathbf{r}_{j-1}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{j-1}\mathbf{B}_{2})\mathbf{Z}_{j \bmod 2} + (\mathbf{r}_{j}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{j}\mathbf{B}_{2})\mathbf{W}_{x_{j}, j \bmod 2}]_{1}\}_{j \in [\ell]} \\ [\mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{2}]_{1}, [(\mathbf{r}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{2})\mathbf{Z}_{j \bmod 2} + (\mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{2})\mathbf{W}_{end}]_{1}, \\ [(\mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{2})]_{1}, [(\mathbf{r}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{2})\mathbf{W}_{start}]_{1} \\ [\mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{2}]_{1}, [(\mathbf{r}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{2})\mathbf{Z}_{j \bmod 2} + (\mathbf{r}_{j}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{j}\mathbf{B}_{2})\mathbf{W}_{x_{j}, j \bmod 2}]_{1}\}_{j \in [\ell]} \\ [\mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{2}]_{1}, [(\mathbf{r}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{2})\mathbf{Z}_{end} + (\mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{j}\mathbf{B}_{2})\mathbf{W}_{x_{j}, j \bmod 2}]_{1}\}_{j \in [\ell]} \\ [\mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{2}]_{1}, [(\mathbf{r}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{2})\mathbf{Z}_{end} + (\mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{2})\mathbf{W}_{end}]_{1}, \\ [(\mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{2})]_{1}, [(\mathbf{r}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{2})\mathbf{Z}_{end} + (\mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{2})\mathbf{W}_{end}]_{1}, \\ [(\mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{2})]_{1}, [(\mathbf{r}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{2})\mathbf{Z}_{end} + (\mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{2})\mathbf{W}_{end}]_{1}, \\ [(\mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{2})]_{1}, [(\mathbf{r}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{2})\mathbf{Z}_{end} + (\mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{2})\mathbf{W}_{end}]_{1}, \\ [(\mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{2})]_{1}, [(\mathbf{r}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{1} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{\ell}\mathbf{B}_{2})\mathbf{Z}_{end} + (\mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{2}) + (\mathbf{r}_{end}\mathbf{B}_{2})\mathbf{Z}_{en$$

Game sequences. We prove Theorem 6 via a series of games following the standard dual system method [20,22,4]:

- $G_0$ : Identical to the real game where all keys and challenge ciphertext are  $sk_x^N$  and  $ct_{r*}^N$ , respectively.
- G<sub>1</sub>: Identical to G<sub>0</sub> except that the challenge ciphertext is ct<sup>SF</sup><sub>r\*</sub>.
- $G_{2,\kappa,0}$  for  $\kappa \in [q]$ : Identical to  $G_1$  except that the first  $\kappa 1$  secret keys are sk<sup>SF</sup><sub>x</sub>.
- $G_{2.\kappa.1}$  for  $\kappa \in [q]$ : Identical to  $G_{2.\kappa.0}$  except that the  $\kappa$ -th secret key is  $\mathsf{sk}_x^{\mathsf{P-N}}$ .  $G_{2.\kappa.2}$  for  $\kappa \in [q]$ : Identical to  $G_{2.\kappa.1}$  except that the  $\kappa$ -th secret key is  $\mathsf{sk}_x^{\mathsf{P-SF}}$ .
- G<sub>2.κ.3</sub> for  $\kappa \in [q]$ : Identical to G<sub>2.κ.2</sub> except that the  $\kappa$ -th secret key sk<sup>SF</sup><sub>x</sub>.
- G<sub>3</sub>: Identical to G<sub>2,d,3</sub> except that the challenge ciphertext is an encryption of a random message.

Note that we have  $G_{2.1.0} = G_1$  and  $G_{2.\kappa.0} = G_{2.\kappa-1.3}$  for  $q \in [2, q]$ .

**Proof sketch.** Most proofs are standard:  $G_0 \approx_c G_1$  follows from  $SD_{\mathbf{A}_1 \to \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{A}_2}^{G_2}$  assumption; both  $G_{2.\kappa.0} \approx_c G_{2.\kappa.1}$  and  $G_{2.\kappa.2} \approx_c G_{2.\kappa.3}$  with  $\kappa \in [q]$  follow from  $SD_{\mathbf{B}_1 \to \mathbf{B}_1, \mathbf{B}_2}^{G_1}$  assumption and  $G_{2.q.3} \approx_s G_3$  is straightforward by a standard statistical argument involving  $\mathbf{k}$  and  $\mathbf{\Delta}$ . We focus on  $G_{2.\kappa.1} \approx_c G_{2.\kappa.2}$  for all  $\kappa \in [q]$ .

**Lemma 62**  $(G_{2,\kappa,1} \approx_c G_{2,\kappa,2})$ . For all  $\kappa \in [q]$  and all  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists  $\mathcal{B}$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{A})$  and

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa.1} \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa.2} \rangle = 1] \leq O(\ell \cdot |\Sigma|^3 \cdot Q^2) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{k\text{-Lin}}(\lambda)$$

*Proof* (*sketch*). We use the core lemma, Lemma 19, to prove the lemma. By the core lemma, it is sufficient to prove that for all  $\kappa$  and all  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists  $\mathcal{B}$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{A})$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa.1} \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa.2} \rangle = 1] \leq \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{CORE}}_{\mathcal{B}}(\lambda).$$

For this, we define two auxiliary games  $\hat{\mathsf{G}}_{2.\kappa.1}$  and  $\hat{\mathsf{G}}_{2.\kappa.2}$  by the following change of variables in both  $\mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa,1}$  and  $\mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa.2}$ :

$$\begin{split} \mathbf{W}_{\text{start}} &\mapsto \mathbf{W}_{\text{start}} + \mathbf{B}_{2}^{\perp} \hat{\mathbf{W}}_{\text{start}} \mathbf{A}_{2}^{\perp}, \\ \mathbf{Z}_{b} &\mapsto \mathbf{Z}_{b} + \mathbf{B}_{2}^{\perp} \hat{\mathbf{Z}}_{b} \mathbf{A}_{2}^{\perp}, \quad \forall b \in \{0, 1\}, \\ \mathbf{W}_{\sigma, b} &\mapsto \mathbf{W}_{\sigma, b} + \mathbf{B}_{2}^{\perp} \hat{\mathbf{W}}_{\sigma, b} \mathbf{A}_{2}^{\perp}, \quad \forall \sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0, 1\} \\ \mathbf{Z}_{\text{end}} &\mapsto \mathbf{Z}_{\text{end}} + \mathbf{B}_{2}^{\perp} \hat{\mathbf{Z}}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{A}_{2}^{\perp}, \\ \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} &\mapsto \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} + \mathbf{B}_{2}^{\perp} \hat{\mathbf{W}}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{A}_{2}^{\perp}, \\ \mathbf{D} &\mapsto \mathbf{D} + \mathbf{B}_{2}^{\perp} \hat{\mathbf{D}} \end{split}$$

and

$$\mathbf{W}_0 \mapsto \mathbf{W}_0 - \mathbf{B}_2^{\perp} \left( \beta (\hat{\mathbf{r}}_{end} \hat{\mathbf{b}}_2^{\perp})^{-1} \cdot \hat{\mathbf{b}}_2^{\perp} \Delta \right) \mathbf{A}_2^{\perp}, \quad \text{where} \quad \beta = \begin{cases} 0 & \text{in } \mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa.1} \\ 1 & \text{in } \mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa.2} \end{cases}$$

where  $\hat{\mathbf{W}}_{\text{start}}, \hat{\mathbf{Z}}_b, \hat{\mathbf{W}}_{\sigma,b}, \hat{\mathbf{Z}}_{\text{end}}, \hat{\mathbf{W}}_{\text{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(2k+1)\times k}$  for all  $\sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0,1\}$ ,  $\hat{\mathbf{D}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(2k+1)\times Q}$  and  $\hat{\mathbf{b}}_2^{\perp} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{2k+1}$ . Looking ahead,  $\hat{\mathbf{b}}_2^{\perp}$  is a part of dual basis of (59) defined later. It is clear that we have

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa.1} \rangle = 1] = \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \hat{\mathsf{G}}_{2.\kappa.1} \rangle = 1] \quad \text{and} \quad \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa.2} \rangle = 1] = \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \hat{\mathsf{G}}_{2.\kappa.2} \rangle = 1]$$

since the change of variables does not change the two games. Now it is sufficient to prove that

<span id="page-74-0"></span>
$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \hat{\mathsf{G}}_{2.\kappa, 1} \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \hat{\mathsf{G}}_{2.\kappa, 2} \rangle = 1] \le \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{CORE}}(\lambda). \tag{58}$$

Observe that, in the new games, we have mpk,  $\mathsf{sk}_x^\mathsf{N}$  and  $\mathsf{sk}_x^\mathsf{SF}$  unchanged due to the fact that  $\mathbf{A}_2^\perp \mathbf{A}_1 = \mathbf{0}$  and  $\mathbf{B}_1 \mathbf{B}_2^\perp = \mathbf{0}$ ; the challenge ciphertext is in the form of

$$\text{ct}_{\Gamma^*}^{\mathsf{SF}} \cdot \begin{bmatrix} [\mathbf{B}_2^{\perp} \hat{\mathbf{D}} \mathbf{u}^{\top} + \mathbf{B}_2^{\perp} \hat{\mathbf{W}}_{start} \hat{\mathbf{S}} \mathbf{u}^{\top}]_2, [\mathbf{0}]_2 \\ \{[-\mathbf{B}_2^{\perp} \hat{\mathbf{D}} + \mathbf{B}_2^{\perp} \hat{\mathbf{Z}}_b \hat{\mathbf{S}}]_2, [\mathbf{B}_2^{\perp} \hat{\mathbf{D}} \mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \mathbf{B}_2^{\perp} \hat{\mathbf{W}}_{\sigma,b} \hat{\mathbf{S}}]_2, [\mathbf{0}]_2 \}_{\sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0,1\}} \\ [-\mathbf{B}_2^{\perp} \hat{\mathbf{D}} + \mathbf{B}_2^{\perp} \hat{\mathbf{Z}}_{end} \hat{\mathbf{S}}]_2, [-\mathbf{B}_2^{\perp} \cdot \beta (\hat{\mathbf{r}}_{end} \hat{\mathbf{b}}_2^{\perp})^{-1} \cdot \hat{\mathbf{b}}_2^{\perp} \Delta \hat{\mathbf{s}}^{\top} \cdot \mathbf{f} + \mathbf{B}_2^{\perp} \hat{\mathbf{W}}_{end} \hat{\mathbf{S}}]_2, [\mathbf{0}]_2 \end{bmatrix} \quad \text{where} \quad \beta = \begin{cases} 0 & \text{in } \hat{\mathsf{G}}_{2.\kappa.1} \\ 1 & \text{in } \hat{\mathsf{G}}_{2.\kappa.2} \end{cases}$$

while the  $\kappa$ -th key in the two games are in the form of

$$\mathsf{sk}_{x}^{\mathsf{P-N}} \cdot \begin{bmatrix} [\mathbf{0}]_{1}, [\hat{\mathbf{r}}_{0}\hat{\mathbf{W}}_{\mathsf{start}}\mathbf{A}_{2}^{\perp}]_{1} \\ \{[\mathbf{0}]_{1}, [\hat{\mathbf{r}}_{j-1}\hat{\mathbf{Z}}_{j \bmod{2}}\mathbf{A}_{2}^{\perp} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{j}\hat{\mathbf{W}}_{x_{j}, j \bmod{2}}\mathbf{A}_{2}^{\perp}]_{1} \}_{j \in [\ell]} \\ [\mathbf{0}]_{1}, [\hat{\mathbf{r}}_{\ell}\hat{\mathbf{Z}}_{\mathsf{end}}\mathbf{A}_{2}^{\perp} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{\mathsf{end}}\hat{\mathbf{W}}_{\mathsf{end}}\mathbf{A}_{2}^{\perp}]_{1} \\ [\mathbf{0}]_{1} \end{bmatrix}$$

It is clear that the two games are identical except that boxed parts, so it is sufficient to prove the indistinguishability between the boxed parts in games. Formally, we capture this by the following claim. Note that we neglect  $\mathbf{B}_2^{\perp}$  and  $\mathbf{A}_2^{\perp}$  which are unrelated to the argument and give out  $\hat{\mathbf{S}}$  and  $\hat{\mathbf{r}}_j$ ,  $\hat{\mathbf{r}}_{end}$  in order to simulate  $\mathsf{ct}_{\Gamma^*}^{\mathsf{SF}}$ -part of the challenge ciphertext and  $\mathsf{sk}_x^{\mathsf{P-N}}$ -part of the  $\kappa$ -th key.

*Claim.* For all A, there exists B with  $Time(B) \approx Time(A)$  and

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_0 \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_1 \rangle = 1] \leq \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{CORE}}_{\mathcal{B}}(\lambda)$$

where we define:

$$\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_{\beta} \rangle := \left\{ \beta' \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathsf{OEnc}(\cdot), \mathsf{OKey}(\cdot)} \right\}$$

and the two oracles work as follows:

– OEnc(Γ): output

$$\begin{pmatrix} [\hat{\mathbf{D}}\mathbf{u}^{\top} + \hat{\mathbf{W}}_{start}\hat{\mathbf{S}}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2}, [\hat{\mathbf{S}}\mathbf{u}^{\top}]_{2} \\ \left\{ [-\hat{\mathbf{D}} + \hat{\mathbf{Z}}_{b}\hat{\mathbf{S}}]_{2}, [\hat{\mathbf{D}}\mathbf{M}_{\sigma} + \hat{\mathbf{W}}_{\sigma,b}\hat{\mathbf{S}}]_{2}, [\hat{\mathbf{S}}]_{2} \right\}_{\sigma \in \Sigma, b \in \{0,1\}} \\ [-\hat{\mathbf{D}} + \hat{\mathbf{Z}}_{end}\hat{\mathbf{S}}]_{2}, [\beta(\hat{\mathbf{r}}_{end}\hat{\mathbf{b}}_{2}^{\perp})^{-1} \cdot \hat{\mathbf{b}}_{2}^{\perp} \Delta \hat{\mathbf{s}}^{\top} \cdot \mathbf{f} + \hat{\mathbf{W}}_{end}\hat{\mathbf{S}}]_{2}, [\hat{\mathbf{S}}]_{2} \end{pmatrix}$$

- OKey(x): output

$$\begin{pmatrix} [\hat{\mathbf{r}}_0]_1, [\hat{\mathbf{r}}_0\hat{\mathbf{W}}_{\text{start}}]_1 \\ \{ [\hat{\mathbf{r}}_j]_1, [\hat{\mathbf{r}}_{j-1}\hat{\mathbf{Z}}_{j \bmod 2} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_j\hat{\mathbf{W}}_{x_j, j \bmod 2}]_1 \}_{j \in [\ell]} \\ [\hat{\mathbf{r}}_{\text{end}}]_1, [\hat{\mathbf{r}}_\ell\hat{\mathbf{Z}}_{\text{end}} + \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{\text{end}}\hat{\mathbf{W}}_{\text{end}}]_1 \end{pmatrix}$$

with the restrictions that (1)  $\mathcal{A}$  makes only one query to each oracle; (2) queries  $\Gamma$  and x satisfy  $\Gamma(x) = 0$ .

It is direct to verify that the terms given out in the claim are sufficient to simulate both games and readily implies (58). This leaves us with the proof for the claim which is sketched as follows.

*Proof of Claim (sketch).* The claim relies on the core lemma, Lemma 19, for adaptively secure KP-ABE for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NFA $^{\oplus p}$  in Section 5. Consider another set of basis which is motivated by that used for our KP-ABE for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -NFA $^{\oplus p}$ , i.e.,

<span id="page-75-1"></span>
$$\hat{\mathbf{B}}_1 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times (2k+1)}, \quad \hat{\mathbf{b}}_2 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times (2k+1)}, \quad \hat{\mathbf{B}}_3 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times (2k+1)}$$

$$(59)$$

and use  $(\hat{\mathbf{b}}_1^{\perp}, \hat{\mathbf{b}}_2^{\perp}, \hat{\mathbf{b}}_2^{\perp}) \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{(2k+1) \times k} \times \mathbb{Z}_p^{2k+1} \times \mathbb{Z}_p^{(2k+1) \times k}$  to denote this dual as in Section 4.1. Note that  $\hat{\mathbf{b}}_2$  has appeared in the reply of  $\mathsf{OEnc}(\Gamma).$  Then we define two auxiliary games as follows:

 $- \ \mathsf{H}'_{\beta} \text{ is identical to } \mathsf{H}_{\beta} \text{ except that we sample } \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{j} \leftarrow \mathsf{span}(\hat{\mathbf{B}}_{1}) \text{ for all } j \in [0,\ell] \text{ and } \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{end} \leftarrow \mathsf{span}(\hat{\mathbf{B}}_{1},\hat{\mathbf{b}}_{2}).$ 

It is direct to prove that

- $\ \mathsf{H}_0 \approx_c \mathsf{H}_0' \ \text{by} \ \mathsf{SD}_{\mathbf{B}_1 \rightarrow \mathbf{B}_1, \mathbf{B}_3}^{G_1} \ \text{assumption (for } \hat{\mathbf{r}}_{\text{end}}) \ \text{and} \ \mathsf{SD}_{\mathbf{B}_1 \rightarrow \mathbf{B}_1, \mathbf{b}_2, \mathbf{B}_3}^{G_1} \ \text{assumption (for } \hat{\mathbf{r}}_j); \\ \ \mathsf{H}_1 \approx_c \mathsf{H}_1' \ \text{by} \ \mathsf{SD}_{\mathbf{B}_1 \rightarrow \mathbf{B}_1, \mathbf{B}_3}^{G_1} \ \text{assumption and } (\cdot, \hat{\mathbf{W}}_{\text{end}}) \text{-switching lemma (for } \hat{\mathbf{r}}_j) \ \text{due to the presence of } \hat{\mathbf{b}}_2^{\perp}; \\ \cdots \cdots \cdots \cdots \cdots \cdots \cdots \cdots \cdots \cdots \cdots \cdots \cdots \cdots \cdots \cdots \cdots \cdots$
- $H'_0 \approx_c H'_1$  by the core lemma, Lemma 19.

This readily proves the claim and the lemma.

# <span id="page-75-0"></span>J Adaptively Secure CP-ABE for $\mathcal{E}_{O}$ -restricted NBP $^{\oplus p}$ and BP

In this section, we construct a compact adaptively secure CP-ABE for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NBP $^{\oplus_p}$ . The scheme is based on our KP-ABE for the same class in Section 6 and dual conversion in [4,6]. This readily gives us a compact adaptively secure CP-ABE for BP by Lemma 23 where the key size grows linearly with the length of input and independent of the program size.

### J.1 Basis

We will use the following two sets of bases for ciphertexts and keys, respectively:

$$\mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{A}_2 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{2k \times k}$$
 and  $(\mathbf{B}_1, \mathbf{b}_2) \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times (k+1)} \times \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times (k+1)}$ .

We use  $\mathbf{A}_1^{\perp}, \mathbf{A}_2^{\perp} \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times 2k}$  to denote the dual basis of  $(\mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{A}_2)$  such that  $\mathbf{A}_i^{\perp} \mathbf{A}_i = \mathbf{I}$  for  $i \in \{1, 2\}$  and  $\mathbf{A}_i^{\perp} \mathbf{A}_j = \mathbf{0}$  for  $i \neq j$ . Analogously, we use  $(\mathbf{B}_1^{\perp}, \mathbf{b}_2^{\perp}) \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+1) \times k} \times \mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+1) \times 1}$  to denote the dual basis of  $(\mathbf{B}_1, \mathbf{b}_2)$ . In the proof, we will use  $\mathrm{SD}_{\mathbf{A}_1 \mapsto \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{A}_2}^{G_2}$ and  ${\rm SD}_{{\bf B}_1 \rightarrow {\bf B}_1, {\bf b}_2}^{G_1}$  assumption, cf. Section 4.1.

### <span id="page-76-0"></span>J.2 Scheme

For notational convenience, especially reusing the branching program notations in Section 6, we will generate ciphertexts over  $G_2$  and keys over  $G_1$ . Our CP-ABE for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> in prime-order groups is described as follows:

- Setup $(1^{\lambda}, \ell, \Sigma)$ : Run  $\mathbb{G} = (p, G_1, G_2, G_T, e) \leftarrow \mathcal{G}(1^{\lambda})$ . Sample

$$\mathbf{A}_1 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{2k \times k}, \ \mathbf{B}_1 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times (k+1)}, \ \mathbf{k} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times 2k} \quad \text{and} \quad \mathbf{W}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{W}_{\eta, \sigma}, \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}, \mathbf{W}_0 \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+1) \times 2k}, \ \forall \ \eta \in [\ell], \sigma \in \Sigma.$$

Output

$$\begin{aligned} & \mathsf{mpk} = \left( \left[ \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}} \mathbf{A}_1, \left\{ \mathbf{W}_{\eta, \sigma} \mathbf{A}_1 \right\}_{\eta \in [\ell], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{end}} \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{W}_0 \mathbf{A}_1 \right]_2, \left[ \mathbf{k} \mathbf{A}_1 \right]_T \right) \\ & \mathsf{msk} = \left( \mathbf{k}, \mathbf{B}_1, \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}}, \left\{ \mathbf{W}_{\eta, \sigma} \right\}_{\eta \in [\ell], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{end}}, \mathbf{W}_0 \right). \end{aligned}$$

- Enc(mpk,  $\Gamma$ , m): Let  $\Gamma = (Q, \ell_{\mathrm{BP}}, \ell, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma}\}_{j \in [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \rho, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f})$  and  $m \in G_T$ . Pick

$$\mathbf{D}_0, \mathbf{D}_1, \dots, \mathbf{D}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{(k+1) \times Q}, \mathbf{S}_1, \dots, \mathbf{S}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}}, \mathbf{S}_{\mathrm{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times Q}, \mathbf{s}_{\mathrm{start}}, \mathbf{s} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$$

and output

$$\mathsf{ct}_{\Gamma} = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{D}_0 \mathbf{u}^\top + \mathbf{W}_{start} \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{s}_{start}^\top]_2, [\mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{s}_{start}^\top]_2 \\ \{ [\mathbf{D}_j \mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{D}_{j-1} + \mathbf{W}_{\rho(j),\sigma} \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{S}_j]_2, [\mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{S}_j]_2 \}_{j \in [\ell_{BP}], \sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [(\mathbf{W}_0 \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{s}^\top) \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{D}_{\ell_{BP}} + \mathbf{W}_{end} \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{S}_{end}]_2, [\mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{S}_{end}]_2 \\ [\mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{s}^\top]_2, [\mathbf{k} \mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{s}^\top]_T \cdot m \end{pmatrix}.$$

- KeyGen(mpk, msk, x): Let  $x = (x_1, ..., x_\ell) \in \Sigma^\ell$ . Pick  $\mathbf{r} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  and output

$$\mathsf{sk}_{x} = \left( [\mathbf{r}\mathbf{B}_{1}]_{1}, [\mathbf{r}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{0} + \mathbf{k}]_{1}, [\mathbf{r}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{\text{start}}]_{1}, \left\{ [\mathbf{r}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{\eta, x_{\eta}}]_{1} \right\}_{\eta \in [\ell]}, [\mathbf{r}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{\text{end}}]_{1} \right).$$

- Dec(mpk,  $\mathsf{sk}_x$ ,  $\mathsf{ct}_\Gamma$ ): Parse key for  $x = (x_1, \dots, x_\ell)$  and ciphertext for  $\Gamma = (Q, \ell_{\mathsf{BP}}, \ell, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma}\}_{j \in [\ell_{\mathsf{BP}}], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \rho, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f})$  as

$$\mathsf{sk}_{x} = \left( [\mathbf{r}_{0}]_{1}, [\mathbf{k}_{0}]_{1}, [\mathbf{k}_{\text{start}}]_{1}, \{ [\mathbf{k}_{\eta}]_{1} \}_{\eta}, [\mathbf{k}_{\text{end}}]_{1} \right) \quad \text{and} \quad \mathsf{ct}_{\Gamma} = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{c}_{\text{start},1}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, [\mathbf{c}_{\text{start},2}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2} \\ \{ [\mathbf{C}_{j,\sigma}]_{2}, [\mathbf{C}_{j}]_{2} \}_{j,\sigma} \\ [\mathbf{C}_{\text{end},1}]_{2}, [\mathbf{C}_{\text{end},2}]_{2} \\ [\mathbf{c}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{2}, C \end{pmatrix}.$$

We define

$$\mathbf{u}_{j,x}^{\top} = \mathbf{M}_{j,x_{\rho(j)}} \cdots \mathbf{M}_{1,x_{\rho(1)}} \mathbf{u}^{\top} \bmod p, \ \forall j \in [0,\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}]$$

as (30) in Section 6.2 and proceed as follows:

1. Compute

$$B_{\text{start}} = e([\mathbf{r}_0]_1, [\mathbf{c}_{\text{start},1}^\top]_2) \cdot e([\mathbf{k}_{\text{start}}]_1, [\mathbf{c}_{\text{start},2}^\top]_2)^{-1};$$

2. For all  $j \in [\ell_{BP}]$ , compute

$$[\mathbf{b}_j]_T = e([\mathbf{r}_0]_1, [\mathbf{C}_{j,x_{\rho(j)}}]_2) \cdot e([-\mathbf{k}_{\rho(j)}]_1, [\mathbf{C}_j]_2) \quad \text{and} \quad B_j = [\mathbf{b}_j \mathbf{u}_{j-1,x}^\top]_T;$$

3. Compute

$$[\mathbf{b}_{\mathrm{end}}]_T = e([\mathbf{r}_0]_1, [\mathbf{C}_{\mathrm{end},1}]_2) \cdot e([-\mathbf{k}_{\mathrm{end}}]_1, [\mathbf{C}_{\mathrm{end},2}]_2) \quad \text{and} \quad B_{\mathrm{end}} = [\mathbf{b}_{\mathrm{end}}\mathbf{u}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}},x}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T;$$

4. Compute

$$B_{\text{all}} = B_{\text{start}} \cdot \prod_{j=1}^{\ell_{\text{BP}}} B_j \cdot B_{\text{end}}$$
 and  $B = B_{\text{all}}^{(\mathbf{fu}_{\ell_{\text{BP}},x})^{-1}}$ 

5. Compute

$$D = e([\mathbf{k}_0]_1, [\mathbf{c}^{\top}]_2) \cdot B^{-1}$$

and output the message  $m' \leftarrow C \cdot D^{-1}$ .

**Correctness.** For  $x = (x_1, ..., x_\ell)$  and  $\Gamma = (Q, \ell_{\text{BP}}, \ell, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma}\}_{j \in [\ell_{\text{BP}}], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \rho, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f})$  such that  $\Gamma(x) = 1$ , we have:

<span id="page-77-0"></span>
$$B_{\text{start}} = [\mathbf{r}\mathbf{B}_1\mathbf{D}_0\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T = [\mathbf{r}\mathbf{B}_1\mathbf{D}_0\mathbf{u}_{0,x}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T$$
(60)

$$\mathbf{b}_{i} = \mathbf{r}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{D}_{i}\mathbf{M}_{i,x_{o(i)}} - \mathbf{r}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{D}_{i-1}$$

$$(61)$$

$$B_{j} = [\mathbf{r}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{D}_{j}\mathbf{u}_{j,x}^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathbf{r}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{D}_{j-1}\mathbf{u}_{j-1,x}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{T}$$

$$(62)$$

$$\mathbf{b}_{\text{end}} = \mathbf{r}\mathbf{B}_{1}(\mathbf{W}_{0}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}})\mathbf{f} - \mathbf{r}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{D}_{\ell_{\text{BP}}}$$
(63)

$$B_{\text{end}} = [\mathbf{r}\mathbf{B}_{1}(\mathbf{W}_{0}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}})\mathbf{f}\mathbf{u}_{\ell_{\text{BP}},x}^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathbf{r}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{D}_{\ell_{\text{BP}}}\mathbf{u}_{\ell_{\text{BP}},x}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{T}$$
(64)

$$B_{\text{all}} = [\mathbf{r}\mathbf{B}_{1}(\mathbf{W}_{0}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}})\mathbf{f}\mathbf{u}_{\ell_{\text{RD},X}}^{\mathsf{T}}]_{T}$$

$$(65)$$

$$B = [\mathbf{r}\mathbf{B}_1(\mathbf{W}_0\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}})]_T \tag{66}$$

$$D = [\mathbf{k}\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}}]_T. \tag{67}$$

Here (64) is trivial; (62) and (66) follow from facts (38), the remaining equalities follow from:

$$(60) r\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{D}_{0}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} = \mathbf{r}\mathbf{B}_{1} \cdot (\mathbf{D}_{0}\mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{W}_{start}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{s}_{start}^{\mathsf{T}}) - \mathbf{r}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{start} \cdot \mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{s}_{start}^{\mathsf{T}}$$

$$(\textbf{61}) \ \mathbf{rB}_{1} \mathbf{D}_{j} \mathbf{M}_{j, x_{o(i)}} - \mathbf{rB}_{1} \mathbf{D}_{j-1} = \ \mathbf{rB}_{1} \cdot (\mathbf{D}_{j} \mathbf{M}_{j, x_{o(i)}} - \mathbf{D}_{j-1} + \mathbf{W}_{\rho(j), x_{o(i)}} \mathbf{A}_{1} \mathbf{S}_{j}) - \mathbf{rB}_{1} \mathbf{W}_{\rho(j), x_{o(i)}} \cdot \mathbf{A}_{1} \mathbf{S}_{j}$$

$$\textbf{(63)} \ \ r \boldsymbol{B}_{1} (\boldsymbol{W}_{0} \boldsymbol{A}_{1} \boldsymbol{s}^{\top}) \boldsymbol{f} - r \boldsymbol{B}_{1} \boldsymbol{D}_{\ell_{BP}} = \ \boldsymbol{r} \boldsymbol{B}_{1} \cdot ((\boldsymbol{W}_{0} \boldsymbol{A}_{1} \boldsymbol{s}^{\top}) \boldsymbol{f} - \boldsymbol{D}_{\ell_{BP}} + \boldsymbol{W}_{end} \boldsymbol{A}_{1} \boldsymbol{S}_{end}) - \boldsymbol{r} \boldsymbol{B}_{1} \boldsymbol{W}_{end} \cdot \boldsymbol{A}_{1} \boldsymbol{S}_{end}$$

(65) 
$$\mathbf{rB}_{1}(\mathbf{W}_{0}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}})\mathbf{f}\mathbf{u}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}},x}^{\mathsf{T}} = \mathbf{rB}_{1}\mathbf{D}_{0}\mathbf{u}_{0,x}^{\mathsf{T}} + \sum_{j=1}^{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}}(\mathbf{rB}_{1}\mathbf{D}_{j}\mathbf{u}_{j,x}^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathbf{rB}_{1}\mathbf{D}_{j-1}\mathbf{u}_{j-1,x}^{\mathsf{T}}) + (\mathbf{rB}_{1}(\mathbf{W}_{0}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}})\mathbf{f}\mathbf{u}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}},x}^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathbf{rB}_{1}\mathbf{D}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}}\mathbf{u}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}},x}^{\mathsf{T}}).$$

$$\mathbf{k}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}} = (\mathbf{r}\mathbf{B}_{1}\mathbf{W}_{0} + \mathbf{k}) \cdot \mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}} - \mathbf{r}\mathbf{B}_{1}(\mathbf{W}_{0}\mathbf{A}_{1}\mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}}).$$

Correctness follows readily.

## J.3 Adaptive Security

<span id="page-77-1"></span>We prove the following theorem.

**Theorem 7** (Adaptively Secure CP-ABE for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup>). The ABE scheme for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NBP $^{\oplus p}$  in prime-order bilinear groups described in Section J.2 is adaptively secure (cf. Section 2.1) under the k-Lin assumption with security loss  $O(q \cdot \ell_{BP} \cdot |\Sigma|^2 \cdot Q^2)$ . Here  $\ell_{BP}$  are program length in adversary's challenge query and q is the number of key queries.

The proof employs standard dual system argument where we handle key queries one by one; for each key, we rely on the core lemma, Lemma 30, for our adaptively secure KP-ABE for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NBP<sup> $\oplus p$ </sup> (in Section 6). We only show the game sequence and sketch the proof.

**Auxiliary distributions.** We use  $\Gamma^* = (Q, \ell_{\mathrm{BP}}, \ell, \Sigma, \{\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma}\}_{j \in [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}], \sigma \in \Sigma}, \rho, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{f})$  to denote the adaptive challenge NBP and  $x = (x_1, \dots, x_\ell)$  a key query. We describe the auxiliary ciphertext and key distributions that we use in the proof.

*Ciphertext distributions.* We sample  $\hat{\mathbf{S}}_1, ..., \hat{\mathbf{S}}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}}, \hat{\mathbf{S}}_{\mathrm{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times Q}, \hat{\mathbf{s}}_{\mathrm{start}}, \hat{\mathbf{s}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  and define:

- N: the real ciphertext in the scheme;
- SF: identical to an N ciphertext except that we replace  $\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{s}_{\text{start}}^{\top}$ ,  $\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{S}_j$ ,  $\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{S}_{\text{end}}$ ,  $\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{s}^{\top}$  with  $\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{s}_{\text{start}}^{\top}$  +  $\mathbf{A}_2\hat{\mathbf{s}}_{\text{start}}^{\top}$ ,  $\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{S}_j$  +  $\mathbf{A}_2\hat{\mathbf{s}}_j$ ,  $\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{S}_{\text{end}}$ ,  $\mathbf{A}_1\mathbf{s}^{\top}$  +  $\mathbf{A}_2\hat{\mathbf{s}}^{\top}$ , respectively.

That is, we write

$$\mathsf{ct}_{\Gamma}^{\mathsf{SF}} = \begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{D}_0 \mathbf{u}^\top + \mathbf{W}_{start} (\mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{s}_{start}^\top + \boxed{\mathbf{A}_2 \hat{\mathbf{s}}_{start}^\top})]_2, [\mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{s}_{start}^\top + \boxed{\mathbf{A}_2 \hat{\mathbf{s}}_{start}^\top}]_2 \\ \{ [\mathbf{D}_j \mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{D}_{j-1} + \mathbf{W}_{\rho(j),\sigma} (\mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{S}_j + \boxed{\mathbf{A}_2 \hat{\mathbf{S}}_j})]_2, [\mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{S}_j + \boxed{\mathbf{A}_2 \hat{\mathbf{S}}_j}]_2 \}_{j \in [\ell_{BP}], \sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [(\mathbf{W}_0 (\mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{s}^\top + \boxed{\mathbf{A}_2 \hat{\mathbf{s}}^\top})) \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{D}_{\ell_{BP}} + \mathbf{W}_{end} (\mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{S}_{end} + \boxed{\mathbf{A}_2 \hat{\mathbf{S}}_{end}})]_2, [\mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{S}_{end} + \boxed{\mathbf{A}_2 \hat{\mathbf{S}}_{end}}]_2 \\ [\mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{s}^\top + \boxed{\mathbf{A}_2 \hat{\mathbf{s}}^\top}]_2, [\mathbf{k} (\mathbf{A}_1 \mathbf{s}^\top + \boxed{\mathbf{A}_2 \hat{\mathbf{s}}^\top})]_T \cdot m_{\beta} \end{pmatrix}.$$

Secret key distributions. We sample  $\Delta \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$ ,  $\hat{r} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p$  and define:

- N: the real key in the scheme;
- SF: identical to an N key except that we replace **k** with  $\Delta A_2^{\perp} + \mathbf{k}$ ;
- P-N: identical to an N key except that we replace  $\mathbf{rB}_1$  with  $\mathbf{rB}_1 + \hat{r}\mathbf{b}_2$ ;
- P-SF: identical to an SF key except that we replace  $\mathbf{rB}_1$  with  $\mathbf{rB}_1 + \hat{r}\mathbf{b}_2$ .

That is, we write

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{sk}_{x}^{\mathsf{SF}} &= \Big( [\mathbf{r} \mathbf{B}_{1}]_{1}, [\mathbf{r} \mathbf{B}_{1} \mathbf{W}_{0} + \boxed{\Delta \mathbf{A}_{2}^{\perp}} + \mathbf{k}]_{1}, [\mathbf{r} \mathbf{B}_{1} \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}}]_{1}, \big\{ [\mathbf{r} \mathbf{B}_{1} \mathbf{W}_{\eta, x_{\eta}}]_{1} \big\}_{\eta \in [\ell]}, [\mathbf{r} \mathbf{B}_{1} \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{end}}]_{1} \big\}; \\ \mathsf{sk}_{x}^{\mathsf{P-N}} &= \Big( [\mathbf{r} \mathbf{B}_{1} + \boxed{\hat{r}} \mathbf{b}_{2}]_{1}, [(\mathbf{r} \mathbf{B}_{1} + \boxed{\hat{r}} \mathbf{b}_{2}) \mathbf{W}_{0} + \mathbf{k}]_{1}, [(\mathbf{r} \mathbf{B}_{1} + \boxed{\hat{r}} \mathbf{b}_{2}) \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}}]_{1}, \big\{ [(\mathbf{r} \mathbf{B}_{1} + \boxed{\hat{r}} \mathbf{b}_{2}) \mathbf{W}_{\eta, x_{\eta}}]_{1} \big\}_{\eta \in [\ell]}, [(\mathbf{r} \mathbf{B}_{1} + \boxed{\hat{r}} \mathbf{b}_{2}) \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{end}}]_{1} \big\}; \\ \mathsf{sk}_{x}^{\mathsf{P-SF}} &= \Big( [\mathbf{r} \mathbf{B}_{1} + \boxed{\hat{r}} \mathbf{b}_{2}]_{1}, [(\mathbf{r} \mathbf{B}_{1} + \boxed{\hat{r}} \mathbf{b}_{2}) \mathbf{W}_{0} + \Delta \mathbf{A}_{2}^{\perp} + \mathbf{k}]_{1}, [(\mathbf{r} \mathbf{B}_{1} + \boxed{\hat{r}} \mathbf{b}_{2}) \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{start}}]_{1}, \big\{ [(\mathbf{r} \mathbf{B}_{1} + \boxed{\hat{r}} \mathbf{b}_{2}) \mathbf{W}_{\eta, x_{\eta}}]_{1} \big\}_{\eta \in [\ell]}, [(\mathbf{r} \mathbf{B}_{1} + \boxed{\hat{r}} \mathbf{b}_{2}) \mathbf{W}_{\mathsf{end}}]_{1} \big\}. \end{split}$$

Game sequences. We prove Theorem 7 via a series of games following the standard dual system method [20,22,4]:

- $G_0$ : Identical to the real game where all keys and challenge ciphertext are  $sk_x^N$  and  $ct_{\Gamma_*}^N$ , respectively.
- $G_1$ : Identical to  $G_0$  except that the challenge ciphertext is  $ct_{\Gamma^*}^{\mathsf{SF}}$ .
- $G_{2,\kappa,0}$  for  $\kappa \in [q]$ : Identical to  $G_1$  except that the first  $\kappa 1$  secret keys are  $sk_x^{SF}$ .
- $G_{2.\kappa,1}$  for  $\kappa \in [q]$ : Identical to  $G_{2.\kappa,0}$  except that the  $\kappa$ -th secret key is  $sk_x^{P-N}$ .
- $G_{2.\kappa,2}$  for  $\kappa \in [q]$ : Identical to  $G_{2.\kappa,1}$  except that the  $\kappa$ -th secret key is  $sk_r^{P-SF}$ .
- $G_{2,\kappa,3}$  for  $\kappa \in [q]$ : Identical to  $G_{2,\kappa,2}$  except that the  $\kappa$ -th secret key sk  $\stackrel{\circ}{s}$ .
- $-G_3$ : Identical to  $G_{2,q,3}$  except that the challenge ciphertext is an encryption of a random message.

Note that we have  $G_{2,1,0} = G_1$  and  $G_{2,\kappa,0} = G_{2,\kappa-1,3}$  for  $q \in [2,q]$ .

**Proof sketch.** Most proofs are standard:  $G_0 \approx_c G_1$  follows from  $SD_{\mathbf{A}_1 \mapsto \mathbf{A}_1, \mathbf{A}_2}^{G_2}$  assumption; both  $G_{2.\kappa.0} \approx_c G_{2.\kappa.1}$  and  $G_{2.\kappa.2} \approx_c G_{2.\kappa.3}$  with  $\kappa \in [q]$  follow from  $SD_{\mathbf{B}_1 \mapsto \mathbf{B}_1, \mathbf{b}_2}^{G_1}$  assumption and  $G_{2.q.3} \approx_s G_3$  is straightforward by a standard statistical argument involving  $\mathbf{k}$  and  $\mathbf{\Delta}$ . We focus on  $G_{2.\kappa.1} \approx_c G_{2.\kappa.2}$  for all  $\kappa \in [q]$ .

**Lemma 63**  $(G_{2,\kappa,1} \approx_c G_{2,\kappa,2})$ . For all  $\kappa \in [q]$  and all  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists  $\mathcal{B}$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{A})$  and

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa.1} \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa.2} \rangle = 1] \leq O(\ell_{\mathit{BP}} \cdot |\Sigma|^2 \cdot Q^2) \cdot \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{k-\mathsf{LIN}}(\lambda)$$

*Proof* (*sketch*). We use the core lemma, Lemma 30, to prove the lemma. By the lemma, it is sufficient to prove that for all  $\kappa$  and all  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists  $\mathcal{B}$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{A})$  such that

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa.1} \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa.2} \rangle = 1] \leq \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{CORE}}_{\mathcal{B}}(\lambda).$$

For this, we define two auxiliary games  $\hat{G}_{2.\kappa,1}$  and  $\hat{G}_{2.\kappa,2}$  by the following change of variables in both  $G_{2.\kappa,1}$  and  $G_{2.\kappa,2}$ :

$$\begin{split} \mathbf{W}_{\text{start}} &\mapsto \mathbf{W}_{\text{start}} + \mathbf{b}_{2}^{\perp} \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}} \mathbf{A}_{2}^{\perp}, \\ \mathbf{W}_{\eta,\sigma} &\mapsto \mathbf{W}_{\eta,\sigma} + \mathbf{b}_{2}^{\perp} \mathbf{w}_{\eta,\sigma} \mathbf{A}_{2}^{\perp}, \quad \forall \eta \in [\ell], \sigma \in \Sigma \\ \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} &\mapsto \mathbf{W}_{\text{end}} + \mathbf{b}_{2}^{\perp} \mathbf{w}_{\text{end}} \mathbf{A}_{2}^{\perp}, \\ \mathbf{D}_{j} &\mapsto \mathbf{D}_{j} + \mathbf{b}_{2}^{\perp} \mathbf{d}_{j}, \quad \forall j \in [\ell_{\text{BP}}] \end{split}$$

and

$$\mathbf{W}_0 \mapsto \mathbf{W}_0 - \mathbf{b}_2^{\perp}(\beta \hat{r}^{-1} \Delta) \mathbf{A}_2^{\perp}, \quad \text{where} \quad \beta = \begin{cases} 0 & \text{in } \mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa.1} \\ 1 & \text{in } \mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa.2} \end{cases}$$

where  $\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \mathbf{w}_{\eta, \sigma}, \mathbf{w}_{\text{end}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times k}$  for all  $\eta \in [\ell], \sigma \in \Sigma$  and  $\mathbf{d}_0, \dots, \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\text{BP}}} \leftarrow \mathbb{Z}_p^{1 \times Q}$ . It is clear that we have

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa.1} \rangle = 1] = \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \hat{\mathsf{G}}_{2.\kappa.1} \rangle = 1] \quad \text{and} \quad \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{G}_{2.\kappa.2} \rangle = 1] = \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \hat{\mathsf{G}}_{2.\kappa.2} \rangle = 1]$$

since the change of variables do not change the two games. Now it is sufficient to prove that

<span id="page-79-0"></span>
$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \hat{\mathsf{G}}_{2.\kappa, 1} \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \hat{\mathsf{G}}_{2.\kappa, 2} \rangle = 1] \le \mathsf{Adv}_{\mathcal{B}}^{\mathsf{CORE}}(\lambda). \tag{68}$$

Observe that, in the new games, we have mpk,  $\mathsf{sk}_x^\mathsf{N}$  and  $\mathsf{sk}_x^\mathsf{SF}$  unchanged due to the fact that  $\mathbf{A}_2^\perp \mathbf{A}_1 = \mathbf{0}$  and  $\mathbf{B}_1 \mathbf{b}_2^\perp = \mathbf{0}$ ; the challenge ciphertext is in the form of

$$\mathsf{ct}_{\Gamma^*}^{\mathsf{SF}} \cdot \begin{bmatrix} [\mathbf{b}_2^{\perp} \mathbf{d}_0 \mathbf{u}^{\mathsf{T}} + \mathbf{b}_2^{\perp} \mathbf{w}_{start} \hat{\mathbf{s}}_{start}^{\mathsf{T}}]_2, [\mathbf{0}]_2 \\ \{ [\mathbf{b}_2^{\perp} \mathbf{d}_j \mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{b}_2^{\perp} \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{b}_2^{\perp} \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma} \hat{\mathbf{S}}_j]_2, [\mathbf{0}]_2 \}_{j \in [\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}], \sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [-\mathbf{b}_2^{\perp} \cdot \beta \hat{r}^{-1} \Delta \hat{\mathbf{s}}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{b}_2^{\perp} \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\mathrm{BP}}} + \mathbf{b}_2^{\perp} \mathbf{w}_{\mathrm{end}} \hat{\mathbf{S}}_{\mathrm{end}}]_2, [\mathbf{0}]_2 \end{bmatrix} \quad \text{where} \quad \beta = \begin{cases} 0 & \text{in } \hat{\mathsf{G}}_{2,\kappa,1} \\ 1 & \text{in } \hat{\mathsf{G}}_{2,\kappa,2} \end{cases}$$

while the  $\kappa$ -th key in the two games are in the form of

$$\mathsf{sk}_{x}^{\mathsf{P-N}} \cdot \overline{\left( [\mathbf{0}]_{1}, [\mathbf{0}]_{1}, [\hat{r}\mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{start}}\mathbf{A}_{2}^{\perp}]_{1}, \left\{ [\hat{r}\mathbf{w}_{\eta, x_{\eta}}\mathbf{A}_{2}^{\perp}]_{1} \right\}_{\eta \in [\ell]}, [\hat{r}\mathbf{w}_{\mathsf{end}}\mathbf{A}_{2}^{\perp}]_{1} \right)}.$$

It is clear that the two games are identical except that boxed part, so it is sufficient to prove the indistinguishability between the boxed parts in games. Formally, we capture this by the following claim. Note that we neglect  $\mathbf{b}_2^{\perp}$  and  $\mathbf{A}_2^{\perp}$  which are unrelated to the argument and give out  $\hat{\mathbf{s}}_{\text{start}}$ ,  $\hat{\mathbf{S}}_j$ ,  $\hat{\mathbf{S}}_{\text{end}}$  for the simulation of  $\text{sk}_{\Gamma^*}^{\text{SF}}$ -part of the challenge ciphertext.

*Claim.* For all  $\mathcal{A}$ , there exists  $\mathcal{B}$  with  $\mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{B}) \approx \mathsf{Time}(\mathcal{A})$  and

$$\Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_0 \rangle = 1] - \Pr[\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_1 \rangle = 1] \leq \mathsf{Adv}^{\mathsf{CORE}}_{\mathcal{B}}(\lambda)$$

where we define:

$$\langle \mathcal{A}, \mathsf{H}_{\beta} \rangle := \left\{ \beta' \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathsf{OEnc}(\cdot), \mathsf{OKey}(\cdot)} \right\}$$

and the two oracles work as follows:

– OEnc(Γ): output

$$\begin{pmatrix} [\mathbf{d}_0\mathbf{u}^\top + \mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}\hat{\mathbf{s}}_{\text{start}}^\top]_2, [\hat{\mathbf{s}}_{\text{start}}^\top]_2 \\ \left\{ [\mathbf{d}_j\mathbf{M}_{j,\sigma} - \mathbf{d}_{j-1} + \mathbf{w}_{\rho(j),\sigma}\hat{\mathbf{s}}_j]_2, [\hat{\mathbf{s}}_j]_2 \right\}_{j \in [\ell_{\text{BP}}], \sigma \in \Sigma} \\ [-\beta \hat{r}^{-1} \Delta \hat{\mathbf{s}}^\top \mathbf{f} - \mathbf{d}_{\ell_{\text{BP}}} + \mathbf{w}_{\text{end}}\hat{\mathbf{s}}_{\text{end}}]_2, [\hat{\mathbf{s}}_{\text{end}}]_2 \end{pmatrix}$$

- OKey(x): output

$$(\mathbf{w}_{\text{start}}, \{\mathbf{w}_{\eta, x_{\eta}}\}_{\eta \in [\ell]}, \mathbf{w}_{\text{end}}).$$

with the restrictions that (1)  $\mathcal{A}$  makes only one query to each oracle; (2) queries  $\Gamma$  and x satisfy  $\Gamma(x) = 0$ .

It is direct to verify that the terms given out in the claim are sufficient to simulate both games and readily implies (68). Furthermore, the claim itself is straightforward by the core lemma, Lemma 30, for adaptively secure KP-ABE for  $\mathcal{E}_Q$ -restricted NBP $^{\oplus p}$  in Section 6. This proves the lemma.
